



The Couenant betweene God and Man plainelie declared in laying open the first and smallest points of Christian Religion.
Question.

IN what state was man created first in the beginning of the world?

 Answere.
Of mans creation.
Man was created in a blessed state, after the image of God, Gen. 1.26.27. Thus God created the man in his image: in the image of God created he him. 
 Quest. VVas man created like vnto God in outward proportion of his bodie, as with heade, legges, armes, etc?
Ans. No, not in proportion of bodie (for God is a spirit, Iohn. 4.24. and not a bodie) but in inward graces of the minde, as in knowledge Coloss. 3.10. in righteousnesse and true holinesse. Ephes. 4.24. and such like.
 Quest. What? was man righteous, as God is righteous? was man good as God is good? was man holie, as God is holie? and was mans knowledge as much as Gods knowledge?

Ans. In these and such other graces, man after some sort resembleth God, and is like vnto him, but is not equall with God in any thing, for there is a dubble difference. First these properties are essentiall in God, and of his essence, so that he were no God if he wanted them: but in man they are accidentall, and the most part of men now want many of them. Secondly, they are in God in all fulnes, and without measure, as God is all goodnesse it selfe, all righteousnesse it selfe, all holines, all wisedome, all mercie, and so of all the rest: but in man they are in a certaine measure, according as the Lord gaue them, and as was sufficient for a creature. Wherefore we make not man equall with God, though we say that he was created like vnto God, and in the image of God in righteousnes, holines, wisedome, and such others.
 Quest. Shewe me then what that image of God in man is? and wherein principally it consisteth?
Ans.The image of God in man. These graces before mentioned, and such like, are the image of God in man. And they consist partly in the minde indued with such excellent wisedome, that he could giue apt and proper names to other creatures in the earth, Gen. 2.20. and spake of
the woman as he did, Gen. 2.23.
This is to be vnderstood according to the reueiled will of God. and with such free will and power to obey God, that if he would, he might haue continued in that integrity and innocency wherein he was created, and not haue sinned; so that the fault and cause of his miserie after his disobedience, is wholly and iustly to be ascribed to himselfe, as the holy Ghost witnesseth, Ecclesiastes cap. 7.31. This haue I found, that God hath made man righteous, but they haue sought many inuentions. And partly in the whole man, in whome the Lord hath set such an imperiall maiesty, that all inferiour creatures, as beastes of the earth, fishes of the sea, and foules of they ayre doe reuerence and obey him as their king and master.
 Quest. Whether did GOD bestowe this good creation, and blessed state vpon the person of Adam onely, or so gaue it to him that it shoulde also redownde to all his posteritie for an euerlasting inheritance?
Ans.All were created good in Adam. When the scripture affirmeth all mankinde through the disobedience of Adam to be subiect to death and damnation, Rom. 5.12. By one man sinne entred into the worlde, and death by sin, and so death went ouer all men: Forasmuch as all men haue sinned. It is manifest that all were created
in Adam good and righteous. For else they could not haue lost that they neuer had.
 Quest. Whether was Adam and all his posteritie to liue perpetually in that most happie state of life, wherein they were created, or had they some limitation of time, which beeing expired they should die, and lose their blessednes?
Ans. We doe not reade in the worde of God, of any prescription of time for life and blessednesse appointed to Adam at his first creation, but that he and his posteritie were to continue blessed for euer, if they continued obedient to God. For death came not into the worlde, but by reason of sinne, Rom. 5.12.
 Quest. Whether receiued Adam this blessed state to continue in it for euer, simplie and absolutely, or with condition?
Ans. Not simplie, and absolutely; but with condition.
 Quest. What was that condition?
Ans. That he should be obedient to God his creator as it was meete; and that if he disobeyed, he should then certainly die the death, Gen. 1.17. Whensoeuer thou eatest thereof thou shalt certainly die the death.
Quest.
^^^^ans Whether did Adam then keepe the condition,  and obey the commaundement of God, or no?

Ans. No, he kept not the condition, but disobeyed the commandement of his God, as we may read, Gen. 3.6. So the woman tooke of the fruite thereof, and did eate, and gaue also to her husband with her, and he did eate. 
 Quest. Whether did Adam onely sinne in this transgression, or all his posteritie sinned in him and with him?
All sinned in Adam.
Ans. All mankind in this first trespasse sinned in Adam and with Adam. For as Leui being as yet in the loynes of Abraham, paid tithes in Abraham vnto Melchizedek, Gen. 14.20. Heb. 7.9.10. So all mankind being then in the loynes of Adam, sinned in Adam.
 Quest. VVhat happened then to man after he had disobeyed the commandement of God?
Ans. That death and eternal damnation,
All men dead in Adam. which God forewarned him of, Gen. 2.17. befell to Adam, and to all his posteritie. For thus saith the Lord, Gen. 3.19. In the sweate of thy face shalt thou eate bread, till thou returne to the earth, for out of it was thou taken: for thou art dust, and to dust shalt thou returne. And in an other place thus: By one man sinne entered into the worlde, and death by sinne, and so death went ouer all men: forasmuch as all men haue sinned, Rom. 5.12. And againe, In Adam all die. 1. Cor. 15.22.
 Quest. Shew me then mans state after his
fall, and what it is.
Ans. First, man is conceiued and borne in sinne,
The state and misery of man after his fall. and commeth sinfull and filthie into the worlde, as the prophet Dauid saith of himselfe, Psalm. 51.5. Behold, I was borne in iniquitie, and in sinne hath my mother conceiued me. And Iob. chap. 15. vers. 14. saith thus: What is man, that he should be cleane? and he that is borne of a woman, that he should be iust? Againe, who can bring a cleane thing out of filthines? Iob. 14.4.
 Secondlie, the whole course of mans life is wicked and wretched, as the Apostle describeth it, Ephes. 2.2.3.12. namely, that man in this state walketh according to the course of this worlde, and after the prince that ruleth in the ayre, euen the spirit, that now worketh in the children of disobedience fulfilling the lust of the flesh, and of the minde: that man is the child of wrath, a straunger from the couenant of promise, without hope, and without GOD in the worlde. Thus farre the Apostle speaketh. Dauid also hee saith, Psal. 58.3. The wicked (that is, all that are not regenerate, but lie in the sinne of Adam) are straungers from the wombe: euen from the bellie haue they erred, and speake lies. Their poyson is
like the poyson of a serpent, etc. Reade Psalm. 36.1.2.3.4. and Tit. 3.3. Gen. 6.5.
 Thirdlie, his departure out of this short and transitorie life, is most woefull and damned. For he goeth into euerlasting fire prepared for the diuell and his Angells, Matth, 25.41. Where the worme dieth not, and the fire neuer goeth out, Marke. 9.44. Esai. 66.24. and into a lake of fire burning with brimstone, Apoc. 19.20.
 Quest.
Of our redemption by Christ. VVhat then? is all mankinde vtterly loste and condemned for euer? is no man able to recouer that fall, and redeeme himselfe from that condemnation?
Ans. No man of himselfe, is able to redeeme himselfe from death, because he is not able to ouercome death.
 Quest. Is there any other meanes then for mans saluation and redemption?
Ans. There is yet some hope,
Christ is our redeemer. and that onely in Christ Iesus. For first GOD, seeing (Esai, 59.16.) there was no man able to redeeme himselfe from death, of his meere mercie and grace promised Christ to bee the redeemer and Sauiour of all that beleeue in him, Genne. 3.15.
He (that is, Christ the blessed seede of the virgin Marie) shall breake thine head (that is, destroy him that had the power of death, that is, the deuill, Heb. 2.14.) and thou (that is, the serpent, euen Satan) shalt bruise his heele. Reade Gen. 12.3. Esai. 7.14. And secondly in the fulnesse of times, he sent him, as the storie of the Gospell witnesseth. For God so loued the world, that he hath giuen his onely begotten Sonne, that whosoeuer beleeueth in him should not perish, but haue euerlasting life, Iohn. 3.16. and 1. Iohn. 4.9.
 Quest. What hath Christ done for our redemption?
Ans. He hath done especially fower things for vs.
 Quest. What is the first?
Ans.Christ made man First Christ being in the forme of God, and equall with God, made himselfe of no reputation, and tooke on him the forme of a seruant, and was made like vnto men, and was found in shape as a man, Philip. 2.6.7. For he in no sort tooke the Angels (that is the nature of Angels) But he tooke the seede of Abraham. Heb. 2.16.
 Quest. 
Christ suffered death for vs. What then? or wherefore was this?
Ans. Secondly, because the iustice of God required, that humain nature, that sinned, should beare the punishment for sinne, Christ hauing
taken our nature vpon him, humbled him self, and became obedient vnto the death, euen the death of the crosse. Phil. 2.8. For it was meete that the Prince of our saluation, euen Christ, that he might bring vs to glorie, should be consecrated through afflictions, Heb. 2.10. Wherefore Christ was made a cursse for vs, that he might redeeme vs from the cursse of the law, Gal. 3.13. According as it was prophesied before, Esai: 53.4.1.
Quest. VVhat is the third thing? 
Ans. Thirdly, Christ in that our nature, which he tooke of the virgin Marie, fulfilled the law for vs,
Christ our righteousnes. and imputeth his righteousnes vnto vs that beleeue in him, Rom. 8.3.4 For Christ is the end of the law for righteousnes for euery one that beleeueth, Rom. 10.4. And these two latter, that is, the second thing and the third which Christ hath done for vs, are plainely and briefely set downe 2. Cor. 5.21.  For he hath made him to be sinne for vs which knew no sinne,
Christ at Gods right hand maketh request for vs. that we should be made the righteousnes of God in him.
Quest. VVhat is the fourth thing?
Ans. Fourthly, Christ that suffered death for vs, is risen againe from death, and as a glorious conqueror, is triumphantly ascended into the heauens, and sitteth at the right hand of the maiestie in the highest places, Heb. 13. maketh
request for vs, Rom. 8.34. and is able perfectly to saue them that come to GOD by him, Heb.  7.25.
Quest.
Christ our reconciliation. Are we then, that through sinne were separated from God, reconciled to God againe by Christ?
Ans. We are, so many of vs as truely beleeue in him. For God hath set him forth to be a reconciliatio^ through faith in his blood, Rom. 3.25. And he hath reconciled vs to God, 1. Ioh. 2.2. Ephes. 2.16.
 Quest.
Of mans vocation and calling Seing then we obtaine al mercie and goodnes of God through Iesus Christ, who not onely nowe is, but also from the beginning hath alwaies beene the hope of all the endes of the tell me and of them that are farre off in the sea, earth, further by what meanes wee that nowe liue may come to the knowledge of these mysteries of saluation? For he that knovveth them not, cannot haue the benefite of them.
Ans. Though I might answere you in one word, and say, that we know these things, and are made partakers of them by the ministerie of the word, yet to speake more distinctly and more plainely for euery mans vnderstanding,
Two meanes of our vocation I answere at this time, and say there are two meanes, whereby
we are made partakers of saluation in Iesus Christ. 
The worde and the Spirite
Quest. What be those meanes?
Ans. They are the word of God outwardly sounding in our eares, and the spirite of God inwardly working in our hearts.
Quest. Doth God then call some men,
The word and the Spirit both necessarie for an effectuall calling. and at some tymes by his vvorde, but others and at an other time by his holy spirit?
Ans. No, that is not my meaning. But albeit that alwayes for the effectuall calling of any, the outward worke of the worde, and the inward grace of the spirit do concurre and may not be separated; and albeit the Lorde for this cause hath promised to accompanye the ministrye of his worde with the grace and power of his spiritte, Esai. 59.21. yet my purpose is to speake of them seuerally for further declaration of them.
Quest.
God hath called men diuers waies by his word in former times Hovv doth GOD call men then by his vvord? for I take it to be your purpose to speake of the vvord first.
Ans. God in the beginning so came to men as they were able to abide his presence and spake vnto them him selfe either by visions, or by dreames, as Elihu affirmeth Iob. 33.15. And as he appeared to Abraham, Gen. 15.1. to Eliphaz the Temanite
Iob. 4.13. And to Iob, as he himselfe confesseth Iob. 7.14. That those patriarks might instruct their families, Gen. 18.18, 19. But afterwards the Lord writte his owne will and word, Exo. 31.18. And vpon the request of the people Exod. 20.19. Deut. 5.24 etc. promised to raise them vp prophets, and by them to speake to the people, Deut. 18.15.19.17.18. Wherefore after that time the Lord ordinarily appeared to his prophets by visions or dreames, as Moses saith, Num. 12.6. and they spake vnto the people. Moreouer the Lord ordained a publicke ministerie at the same time, euen Aaron and his sons successiuely to be priestes, and the rest of the Leuites to help them. And thus God called whom he would to the knowledge of mysteries of saluation by visions, and dreames til the time that he deliuered Israell out of Egipt. After that time he gaue his word and his wil in writing, which conteined the meanes and misteries of saluaon, and ordeined a publick minysterie to read and preach the written word of God to the people, himselfe alway being resident among them in his owne Tabernacle betweene the Cherubims which were ouer the mercy-seate and ouer the arke of the couenant to resolue them of all doubtes, Exod 25.22. and 19.42. Num. 7.89. and Exod: 28.30. Num. 27.21.
Iud. 20, 18.7.28. and 1. Sam. 22.10.15. And further spake to the^, by prophts as it pleased him.
Quest. But God doth not speake to vs now after that manner. 
Ans.In these last daies God hath called men by his sonne God spake to the church of the Iewes after that manner til the comming of Christ in the flesh. But now in these last daies the greate prophet so long since foretold, Deut. 18.18:19. Euen Iesus Christ is come, and by him doth GOD speake vnto vs, Heb. 11. and by them whom he hath sent, first the Apostles, and then the ordinary ministers of his word. And now the whole counsell of God is written for our instruction.
 Qu. Can no man atteine to the knowledge of these mysteries of saluation by naturall reason,
Naturall reason cannot reach to the mysteries of saluation and by consideration of the workes of God, but only by the word of God?
Ans. No, no man. For Paul 1. Cor. 2.7. calleth the reuelation of these mysteries, the hid wisdom of God, which the wise men of the world cannot attaine vnto. And the same Apostle in the ninth verse, alleadging the prophesie of Esaias Chap. 52.14. and Chap. 64.4. saith further, that these mysteries are such things, as the eye of a natural man by light of nature and reason hath not seene, neither the care hath heard, neither came into mans heart.
 Quest. VVhether doth God call all men by his
word, and so reueale these mysteries of saluation vnto all, or vnto some men only?
Ans.The gospel sonded throughout the world. That which the prophet Dauid spake Psa. 19.4. of the creatures of God, and namely of the heauens, the same hath the holy Ghost affirmed also of the word of God, Rom. 10.10. that their sound went out through al the earth, and their wordes into the ends of the world.
 Quest. Hath the gospell then beene Preached in euery nation vpon earth, as we see it is preached among vs at this day?
Ans. Although the gospel was not euerie where preached in that plentifull manner that we haue it now, yet the Apostles commanded by Christ to goe into all the world,
Niceph. li. 3. Cap. 1. Auent li. 2 and to preach the gospel to euerie creature, Mark: 16.15. were dispersed throughout Asia, Europe, and Afrik, as Eusebius lib. 3. reporteth out of Origene, and so preached, that by their ministerie the sound of the gospell came in some measure to all people vpon earth. Whereof Paul being prisoner at Rome giueth good testimonie in his epistle to the colossians Chap. 1.23. If ye continue in the faith, and be not moued from the gospell, which hath beene preached to euery creature which is vnder heauen
 Quest. Whether do all that heare these misteries preached vnto them, receiue the saluation that is offred in the gospel?

Ans. Christ shewed by a parable of seede sowne in the ground, Mat. 13. That there are diuers sortes of hearers,
Many hearers, few beleuers: so that some men receiue the seede of the word into their hard heartes, as if it were in the path waies, and the euill one commeth, and catcheth away that which was sowen in their heartes. Some receiue it as in stony ground, and assoone as tribulation commeth for the word, by and by they are offended. Others receiue it as among thornes, and worldly cares choke it. Lastly other some receiue it as into good ground, and they bring forth much fruite. Then of foure sortes of hearers, but one only bringeth forth fruit, wherefore Christ saide in an other place, (Math. 22.14.) Many are called but few chosen. And to make men with greater care and reuerence to attend vnto the word of God preached, that they may be saued, he saith in the end of the parable, If any man haue an eare to heare, let him heare.
 Quest. Can you tell me who those be that receiue the word of God when it is preached as into good ground, and bring forth the fruit thereof?
Ans. Those which haue not onely the word outwardly sounding in their eares, but also the holy spirit of God inwardly working in their hearts which is the other meanes of obtaining the mercies of God in Christ, as I noted
before in answering your 23. question.
 Quest. Then, to come to the other meanes of our calling, which is the inward worke of the spirit, is it necessarie that the mercies of GOD in Christ outwardlie preached by the ministerie of men, should inwardly be applied and appropriated vnto vs by the secret worke, power, and grace of the holy ghost?
The inward worke of the spirit is necessarie for aneffectuall calling.
Ans. Yea verely, it is most requisite, that to the outward ministery of the word should be adioyned the inward working of the spirit to beget faith in vs, and thereby to apply, make proper, and profitable vnto vs, that which the word hath declared. For except a man be borne of water and of the spirit, he cannot enter into the kingdom of God. Ioh. 3.5. And this inward working of the spirit, is that which pricked the hart of those three thousand which heard Peter preach, and were conuerted to the faith. Acts. 2.37, 41. And which opened the heart of Lydia. Act, 16.14. and which opened the mysteries of saluation to babes, but hid them from the wise and men of vnderstanding Math. 11.25. and which reuealed vnto Peter that Christ was the sonne of God, Math. 16, 17 and whereby Paul could say, I liue by the faith of the sonne of God, VVho hath loued me, and giuen him selfe for me, Gallat. 2.20.
Quest. Is it not possible for vs to attaine, to the
mercies of God in Christ by the outward hearing of the word onely, except we haue also this inward grace and working of the spirit?
Ans. No verelie, for Christ saith, Iohn. 6.44. No man can come to me except the father drawe him. And againe, Iohn. 8.47. Ye therefore heare not my wordes, because ye are not of God. And the Apostle Paul saith, 1. Cor. 2.11. As no man knoweth the things of a man saue the spirit of a man which is in him: euen so the things of God knoweth no man, but the Spirit of God. And yoong Elihu perceiuing the follie that was in three ancient graue religious men, Iobs friendes, and admiring at it, at the last said, Verelit it is the Spirit in man; and the inspiration of the Almightie, that giueth vnderstanding, Iob. 32.8.
 Quest. Were it not good then to leaue off hearing the word, as some men doe, and seeke by speculation, reuelation, praier, or by some other meanes, to obtaine the grace of the holie Ghost?
Ans. No,
The ministerie of the worde and the worke of the spirit goe together. that were great ignorance to forsake the word which we are warned to seeke after, Ioh. 5.39. for God doth ioine these two together, and alwaies accompany the outward ministry of the word, with the inward work and power of his holy spirit, according as he promised long since by his prophet Esaias, Ch. 59.21.
My spirit that is vpon thee, and my wordes which I haue put in thy mouth, shal not depart out of thy mouth, nor out of the mouth of thy seed, nor out of the mouth of the seed of thy seed, saith the Lord, from henceforth euen for euer. So that he which desireth the work of the spirit, must attend vpon the ministerie of the word, as vpon the holy meanes which the Lorde hath appointed. And for this cause it is, that the worke of regeneration, wrought both by the word and also by the spirit, is sometime attributed to the spirit as Iohn. 3.6. that that is borne of the spirit, is spirit, and sometime to the worde as 1. Pet. 1.23. Being borne a new, not of mortall seede, but of immortall, by the word of God, who liueth and endureth for euer. And 1. Cor. 4.15. Also faith (without which no man can please God, Heb. 11.6.) is said to be the fruite of the worde, Rom. 10.14. how shall they beleeue in him, of whome they haue not heard, and the fruit of the spirit, Galat. 5.22. But the fruit of the spirit is loue, ioy, peace, long suffering, gentlenesse, goodnesse, faith. Whereas it is the effect of them both.
 Quest. Whether doth the spirit inwardlie worke alike in all the hearers of the word?
Ans.The diuers worke of the worde in diuers hearers. No, for some men will not suffer the spirite to worke vpon them, but oppose themselues against the worde, and so want
the grace of the spirite, as those did, whose heartes brast for anger, when they hearde the worde at Stephens mouth, and they gnashed at him with their teeth, Act. 7.54. and those which were full of enuie, and spake against those things, which were spoken of Paul and Barnabas, contrarying them, and rayling on them, Act. 13.45. And faith is not proper to al men, 2. Thes. 3.2. And in another place Paul saith, To the one we are the sauour of death, vnto death and to the other the sauour of life, vnto life.
 Quest. Who then are partakers of these two means effectually, that is, of the outward ministerie of the word, and of the inward grace of the spirit, so that they are effectually called, that they in deed beleeue, and bring forth the fruites thereof?
Ans.The elect onely effectually called. Those which are ordained to eternal life. And as many as were ordained vnto eternal life, beleeued, Act. 13.48. And Christ saith, Iohn. 10.26. But ye beleeue not: for ye are not of my sheepe, as I said vnto you. Paul saith, Rom. 8.30. Whom he predestinate, them also he called effectually. Iohn saith, he that knoweth God, heareth vs: he that is not of God, heareth vs not. Hereby know we the spirit of truth and the spirit of error, 1. Iohn. 4.6.
 Qu. Are no others partakers of these two means the outward ministery of the word and the inward worke of the spirit, but the elect of God onely?

Ans.Many gifts of the spirit are co^mon to the reprobate There are many besides Gods elect that are in some measure partakers of both, though not effectually, and some retaine both for a longer time, and some for a shorter time, as it appeareth in the parable, Math. 13. for some receiuing the word into their hard harts, as it were in the path way, let it goe againe by and by; as it came in at one eare, so it went out at the other. Some receiue both as among thornes, and the couetous desires of the world choke it. Some as among stones, but when troubles, and the very crosses of Christ come vpon him, he letteth the grace of God wither away rather then his bodie should suffer, Saul had the spirit of the Lord to giue him much grace, and turne him into an other man. 1. Sam. 10.6. Neuerthelesse it is saide, 1. Sam. 16.14. But the spirit of the Lord departed from Saul, and an euill spirit sent of the Lord vexed him. Iudas receiued such grace of the spirit that he was a preacher of the gospell, yet after he had determined to betray the Lord of life, and after he had receiued the soppe 'Satan entred into him, Iohn. 13.27. But to let passe other giftes of the spirit, such as were in Saul, Balaam, Iudas, which were for execution of such speciall duties, and to passe ouer also the gift of the Spiritte which consisteth in knowledge and is common to diuels as to men, Iames. 2.19.
and in the gospell often did the diuels confesse Christ: it seemeth, Heb. 6.4. that some tast of other manner of graces, and yet fall away in the end. But the spirit of adoption, and regeneration seemeth rather to be proper to the elect onely. But this would require a larger treatise, and is of late verie pithily and plentifully handled by others.
 Quest. Can you iudge of these, and discerne who haue the spirit of regeneratio^, and who want it and consequently who are elect, and who are not?
Ans. No,
The elect and the reprobate cannot be discerned at al times for it is certaine there wilbe tares among good corne, that is to say, the hypocrits among true beleeuers whiles the world indureth. But we must iudge the best, and thinke most charitably of all that outwardly receiue and professe the word, and yeeld some obedience vnto it.
 Quest. Then to leaue this iudgment to the Lord, to whom it belongs, I pray you tell me, what the state is of those men, whom the Lord doth effectually call with an holy calling?
Ans.The blessed state of the^ which are effectually called. Although I may answere you generally, that mans state, when he is effectually called, is most happie and blessed, yet if I would descend to the particulars of this blessednes, I must confesse with Dauid, Psal. 40.5. They are moe then I am able to expresse. For although we are partakers of the promises in Christ, Eph. 3.6.
Citizens with the saintes, and of the housholde of God, Ephes. 2.19. partakers of the godlie nature, 2. Pet. 1.4. the brethren of Christ, Psa. 22.23. Heb. 2.11. a chosen generation, a royall priesthood an holy nation, 1. Pet. 2.9. the iudges of the world, 1. Cor. 6.2. called to Gods eternall glorie by Christ Iesus, 1. Pet. 5.10. come to the mount Sion, and to the citie of the liuing GOD, the celestiall Ierusalem, and to the companie of innumerable Angels, and to the congregation of the first borne, which are written in heauen, and to God the iudge of all, and to the spirits of iust and perfect men, and to Iesus the mediator of the newe testament, and to the bloode of sprinkling that speaketh better thinges then that of Abell. Heb. 12.22. and although now we be the sonnes of God, neuerthelesse yet it doth not appeare what we shalbe, 1. Iohn. 3.2. And the Apostle Paul giueth the reason hereof, 1. Cor. 2.9. The things which the eye hath not seene, neither eare hath heard, neither came into mans heart, are, which God hath prepared for them that loue him.
Quest. When God calleth any man with an holy calling, from that miserable state of conde^nation, whereof you spake in your answere to my 12. questio^, vnto this blessed state ye haue now spoken of, I pray you tel me what condition he requireth of man, or what couenant he maketh with man?

Ans.Of the couenant of God. When God calleth man with an holy calling, and receiueth him to his mercie and fauour againe in Iesus Christ, then there are as it were indentures drawen between God and man, conditions on both sides agreed vpon, and so a new couena^t made between God and man.
 Quest. What is that couenant, or what be the conditio^s, or what be the words, or where shal we find any such thing in all the scripture?
The summ of the couenant.
Ans. Although this couenant was made before, euer since the blessed seede of the virgin was promised, Gen. 3. yet we may see it more plainly set down afterward, Ge. 17.1. between God and Abraham in these words, I am God all sufficient: walke before me and be thou vpright. In the first words, God for his part promiseth that he wilbe god al sufficient vnto Abraha^, to blesse him with al necessary blessings for this life, and for the life to come, as it is afterward in the text declared. In the latter words the Lord requireth of Abraha^, obedience, that he walk vprightly before God. Likewise where this couenant is renewed againe, Exod. 19.5.9. between God and the Israelites, the Lord for his part freely and of his own meere grace and fauour promiseth, that he wil be their God, and make them a kingdome of priests, and an holy nation vnto himselfe. And on the other part he requireth that they should obey his voyce
and keepe his commandements. And the condition of obedience which God requireth, and man promiseth is the chiefest thing which is vrged and required of vs in the scripture, as to him that will take paines to read the places, it appeareth, Deut. 7.12 and 10.12. and 1. Sam. 15.22 Ierem. 7.23. And this couenant is vsually repeated in the old and new testament, and very often in these wordes. I wilbe your God, and ye shalbe my people; as Ierem. 31.1.33. and 2. Cor. 6.18. zachar. 8.8. and Heb. 8.10. Ezek. 37.26.27. and 2. Cor. 6.16.
 Quest. I pray you shew me the meaning of this couenant more fully?
Ans. The meaning is very plaine and manifest, that whereas man before through Adams fall was the child of the deuil, Act. 13.10 Iohn. 8.44. the seruant of sinne, Iohn. 8.34. and 2. Pet. 2.19. without God in the world, Eph. 2.12. now he is become the sonne of God. Galat. 3.26. the seruant of righteousnes, Rom. 6.17.19. and an inheritour of the kingdom of heauen, Iam. 2.5. if so be that he continue in the couenant, and obey the co^mandements of God.
 Quest.
The condition of the couenant, is to be obedient to God. When man entreth into this couenant with God, doth he solemnly promise, and straitly binde himselfe to keepe all the commandements of God?
Ans. Yea, he doth bind himself to be obedient
to al Gods commandements as I haue shewed, els there could be no couenant. And when Moses had been the second time in the mount with God, and brought with him the two tables of the couenant, then he red them to the people, who answered with one voice. Exod. 24.3, 7. All things which the Lord hath saide, we will doe, and be obedient. For except a man be resolued in himselfe to obey the commandementes of God, it is to no purpose euer to thinke of any couenant. And Christ sheweth by two examples, of a man that purposeth to build a house, and of a king that minds to make warre, Luk. 14.28. etc. That it is lost labour to enter into Gods couenant, except we be resolued to do what the Lord commaundeth. 
Man breaks the couenant.
Quest. Is there any man in the world, that keepeth this condition, and that breaketh not the commaundementes of God?
Ans. No indeede there is no man that can so absolutely keepe the co^maundementes of God as he ought to doe, but he daily offendeth.
 Quest. Are not all men then as deepely condemned for so many sins as we daylie commit,
Christ is our righteousnes. as euer Adam was for his first disobedience?
Ans. No, for Christ hath not only suffred for vs, and reconciled vs to God againe, but
also fulfilled the law for vs. Ro. 8.2.3.4. and 10. imputing his obedience to vs that beleeue that hereafter we should not be condemned againe.
 Q. But doth God accept of Christs righteousnes and fulfilling of the law, as if we our selus had fulfilled it?
A. Paul saith 1. Cor. 1.30. That God hath made Christ to be our righteousnes, that we should be made the righteousnes of God in him 2. Cor. 5.21.
 Quest. What say you then for our sins which we daily commit, doth Christ answer for them all?
Ans.Christ is our mediatour. I answer with the Apostle. 1. Ioh 2.1. If any man sinne (of infirmitie, not of obstinacy and malice) we haue an aduocate with the father, Iesus Christ the iust, who appeareth now in the sight of God for vs. Heb. 24. Who euer liueth to make intercession for vs, and is able perfectly to saue them that come to God by him, Heb. 7.25.
 Quest. If the case be so as you say, that Christ is our righteousnes, and we the righteousnes of God in him, and that he is our reconciliation, and now appeareth in the sight of God making the attonement for vs, it skilleth not for our obedience it is no matter whether we sin or not, we may take our pleasurs of this world for we are not vnder the law but vnder grace.
Ans.We must not return with the dog to his vomit. Not so, for then our condition should be farre worse and more damnable then it was befere we were redeemed by Christ, as Peter telleth vs 22. Pet. 20. For if they, after they haue escaped from the filthines of the world, through the
knowledge of the Lord, and of the Sauiour Iesus Christ, are yet tangled againe therein, and ouercome, the latter end is worse then the beginning. For it had beene better for them, not to haue knowen the way of righteousnes, then after they haue knowen it, to turne from the holy commandement giuen vnto them. And Christ saith, that if a man hauing an euill spirit, driuen out of him, shall admit him to come with seauen other spirits worse then himselfe, and returne and dwell there, the last state of that man is worse then the first Luk. 11.26.
 Q. What shal we say or do the^ for we al sin daily?
Sin must not reigne in vs.
Ans. Though sinne cannot vtterly be abolished out of our mortal bodies, but we all sin daily: yet the Apostle teacheth vs what we must do, and saith Rom. 6.12. Let not sin reign therefore in your mortall body, that ye should obey it in the lustes thereof.

Q. Is it sufficient for vs after we be reconciled to God by Christ, that we suffer not sin to reign in vs

Ans.The combate betweene the flesh and the spirit. If we feele in our selues a combate betweene the flesh and the spirit, such as Paul speaketh of, Galat. 5.17. so that we allow not the euil which we doe, but desire and striue to do the good we cannot attaine vnto, it is no more we that do it, but sin that dwelleth in vs Rom. 7 10. And then though in respect of the infirmitie of the flesh we cry out with Paul Rom 7.24.
O wretched man that I am, who shall deliuer me from the bodie of this death? Yet we may likewise reioyce with the same Apostle. Rom. 7.25. and say, I thanke God through Iesus Christ our Lord.
 Quest. The papistes say, that after our baptisme and regeneration, we must by our workes merit saluation, and for our sinnes of infirmitie make sitisfaction by our good deedes. What say you to this? for ye saide before, that Christ maketh satisfaction for all, if your doctrine be true, shew me the papists error.
Ans.Popish il workes confuted Hereunto I answere two waies. First, if our sinnes committed before baptisme and before our regeneration were so great that they could not be purged by any mans works, but the death and blodsheding of Iesus Christ was necessarily required to wash vs and make vs cleane; then I say that sinne committed after regeneration, can in no wise be purged by workes of men, but only by the bloud of Christ: My reason is, because sinne is alwayes of one nature, though some sinnes be greater then other. And because sinnes committed after Baptisme are greater then sinnes committed before regeneration. For before regeneration wee walke in darkenesse, (though we haue so much light as is sufficient to make vs excuseles) and so commit much
sinne through ignorance: but after regeneration we are in the light, we haue more knowledge, and greater power to resist sinne. And therefore sinne committed after regeneration, is greater then the sinne committed before in the same degree. Wherefore if sinne committed before regeneration, cannot be purged but by the bloud of Christ, it is manifest that sinne after regeneration can no other way be forgiuen then by Christ, whose death is effectuall and auailable aswell for sinnes after regeneration as before. Secondly, the greatest papist of them all, yea the Pope himselfe, I thinke, can doe no greater, nor no better workes then did the Apostle Paul. But he after his regeneration, fleeth to the mercie of God in Christ, and saith, Phil. 3.8.9. That he counteth all his righteousnes losse for Christes sake, and desireth to be found in him, not hauing his owne righteousnes which is of the law, but that which is through the faith of Christ, euen the righteousnes which is of God through faith. wherfore except the papists looke otherwise to be saued then Paul was, or haue better works then he had, they cannot be saued by them. I might ad hereto, that the wages of sinne whether it be before or after regeneration is death, Rom. 6.23. And thereon infer, that popish
works may deliuer the^ out of popish purgatorie for they are both of them popish dreames; but no works of me^ can deliuer from death and hel. No mens works can deliuer vs from this death of the body, for we se all die, much lesse from death of body and soule in hel. But these neede not:  there is sufficient sayd before.
Q. If works do not iustifie vs wherefore serue they? is there any vse of the?
Four causes why we must do good workes. Io. 15, 8. serue they to any purpose?
Ans. Christ answereth this question Math. 5.16. saying, Let your light so shine before men, that they may see your good workes and glorifie your father which is in heauen. For as a leude sonne dishonoureth his father: so a wicked Christian dishonoureth God, and causeth all men to speake euill of God, as the Lord complaineth by his prophet Ezekiel diuers tymes, that the Iewes in Babilon pulluted Gods name among the heathen. But by a holy conuersation, there is greate occasion ministred to glorifie God. Besides good workes serue for edification of our brethren. Somtimes they may serue for to winne vnbeleeuers to God, 1. Cor. 7.16. and 1. Pet. 3.1. Lastly they are notable testimonies to our consciences, that we are Gods elect, as Paul sheweth Rom. 8.1. etc: Phil. 2.12. and Peter also 2. Pet. 1.10. and. 1. Io. 3.19
Quest. But to returne to that I desired specially
to know,  euen to the couenant of God againe, for whether it hath beene your answeres or my questions that caried me away, I know not, I pray you now shew me, whether the Israelites continued in, and kept that holy couenant, whereto they bound themselues with such sollomne consent.
Ans. Many and the most part of them transgressed grieuously,
The Israelites transgressed the couenant of God often. and brake their promise with God both in the wildernes before they entred into the Land of Canaan, as it appeareth in the bookes of the law Exod. Leuit. Numb. and deut. And Moses plainely telleth them Deut. 9.7. Remember, and forget not, how thou prouokedst the Lord thy God to anger in the willdernes, since the day that thou diddest depart out of the Land of Egipt, vntil ye came vnto this place ye haue rebelled against the Lord etc. And the Lord himselfe complaining of their often rebellion, saith. They haue tempted me this ten times and haue not obeyed my voice. Numb. 14.22. And also after they were come into the promised land, as it is to be seene in the former prophets which wrote things done and past as Iosua and the rest, and the latter prophets which also foretold things to com as Esai and they following. And the prophet Dauid til his dayes maketh relation of all, Psal. 78.10.37.41, etc. and Psal. 106.

 Quest. What saide the Lord, or what did he, when they had thus broken his couenant?
Ans.Man punished for breaking his couenant with God. He was exceeding wrath with the people, and often smote them with grieuous iudgments: for when they worshipped the calfe, Exod 32. The Lord minded to destroy them, had not Moses stand in the breach to turne away his wrath, Deut. 9.14.18. Ps. 106.23. When they murmured he consumed them with fire. Numb. 11.1.3. When they lusted after flesh, he slew them with an exceeding greate plague, euen the strongest of them and the chosen men in Israel, Numb. 11.33. Psal. 78.31. When they refused to enter into the Land of Canaan Numb. 14. The Lord sware in his wrath, that they shoulde not enter into his rest, Psal. 95.11. when they committed fornication with the daughters of Moab, the Lord slew 24. thousand of them Num. 25.9. The books of Iudges, Samuel and kings are full of examples.
 Quest. Doth not the Lord also breake his couenant and promise, when man is vnfaithfull and disobedient,
Mans vnbeliefe maketh not Gods promise voide. and so all the couenant betweene God and man is made voide and of none effect?
Ans. No, God forbid that we should think or say so, for the gifts or calling of God are without repentance, Rom. 11.1, 29. The Apostle saith, Heb. 6.17.18. that, God willing more
abundantly to shew vnto the heires of promise the stablenesse of his counsell, bound himselfe by an oath, that by two immutable things (that is, his word, and his oath) wherein it is vnpossible that God should lie, we might haue strong consolation, which haue our refuge to hold fast the hope that is set before vs, which we haue, as an ancre of the soul, both sure and stedfast, etc. And herupo^ Dauid said, Psal. 89.34. his couenant he will not breake nor alter the thing that is gone out of his lippes. And Paul saith, Rom. 3.3. For what, though some did not beleeue? shall their vnbelief make the promise of God of none effect? God forbid: Yea let God be true, and euery man a lyar. And againe in another place: If we beleeue not, yet abideth he faithfull, he cannot deny himselfe 2. Tim. 2.13. The prophet Esai he also saith, Chap. 54.10. For the mountaines shall remooue, and the hils shal fall downe: but my mercy shal not depart from thee; neither shal the couenant of my peace fall away saith the Lord that hath compassion on thee. And in many other places of scripture besides these, the stablenes of Gods couenant is declared as Iere. 31.35. and 33.20.25.26.
 Quest. This is a most sweet and comfortable doctrine, wherefore I pray you giue me some reason of it, if there be any to be rendred? for it is an vnmeasurable mercie of the Lord, to perform his promise, though man breake his.

Ans.The couenant renued two waies. It commeth to passe two waies specially that God keepeth his couenant, when man doth not. First the Lord is mercifull, and gracious, slowe to anger, and abundant in goodnes and trueth, reseruing mercie for thousandes, forgiuing iniquitie, and transgression and sinne, Exod. 34.6. and deliteth rather in the conuersion, then in the condemnation of a sinner, Ezek. 18.23. and therefore by patience and long suffering inuiteth men to repentance, Rom. 2.4. protesting that his waies are not like to our waies, that is, that he is not vnreconciliable as often time we are Esai. 55.8. that if men hauing broken the couenant of God, doe repent, and turne to the Lord, preuenting his further iudgementes by repentance, the Lord hath promised, Deut. 30.1.2.3. that he wilbe reconciled. For if we acknowledge our sinnes, he is faithfull and iust, to forgiue vs our sinnes, and to cleanse vs from all vnrighteousnesse, 1. Iohn. 1.9. And thus though man breake Gods couenant, yet by repentance the couenant is renewed and continued, Deut. 4.31.
Secondlie, when men continue in their sinnes, and doe not by repentance turne to the Lord, and renewe the couenant betweene God and them, then the Lorde powreth his indignation vpon them, till he haue destroyed
and weeded out the chiefe rebels and great sinners, and then after some chastisement will he bring the rest as it were by strong hande into the bonde of the couenant, as the prophet Ezechiel sheweth, Chap. 20.33.37.38. And thus as the Lorde chose man at the first making of the couenant, euen of his own mercie, for all men lay vnder the curse by reason of sinne: euen so doth the Lorde of his mercie continue the couenant, as the same prophet Ezekiel speaketh in plaine wordes, Chap. 36. vers. 22.32. Thus saith the Lorde God, I doe not this for your sakes, O house of Israell, but for mine owne holy names sake. And in another place, I might euen deale with thee as thou hast done, when thou diddest dispise the oath in breaking the couenant. Neuerthelesse, I will remember my couenant made with thee in the daies of thy youth, and I will confirme vnto thee an euerlasting couenant, Ezek. 16.59.60. And in the verse following he plainly telleth them, that he doth renewe this his couenant of his meere mercy, but not by thy couenant, that is, not because thou hast kept the couenant, for thou hast broken the couenant on thy part.
 Quest. I pray you shewe these two waies of the continuance of the couenant betweene God and man, by some examples.

Ans.Examples of renewing the couenant. When the Lord brought Israel out of Aegypt, there was a solemne couenant made between God and them, Exod. 19.3. etc. But whiles Moses was in the mount with God to receiue the lawes of the Lord, the people made a molten calfe, and so brake their promise and their couenant with God. Wherfore through the Lordes long suffering that did not presently destroy them, but inuited them to repentance, and through Moses prayer to God, and reprouing of them and of their idolatrie, they fell to repentance and humbling of themselues before God, Exod. 33.4. etc. and the Lordes anger was so pacified, that he commaunded Moses to hew him new tables of stone (for the first writen with the finger of God were broken, Exod. 32.19.) and came vp into the mountaine the second time, for the Lord now pacified, woulde vouchsafe to renewe the tables of the couenant againe. Exod. 34.1. And Moses hauing receiued the lawe the second time, came downe to the people againe after fourtie daies, and then reade the lawe to the people and renewed the couenant againe, Exodus. 24. verse. 3. etc to verse. 9. Where all the people answered with one voyce, and saide. All the thinges which the Lord hath said, will we doe, and be obedient, vers. 3. and 7.

 When Iosua waxed olde, and was readie to enter into the way of all the world. Iosh. 23.14. and when there was some inclination to idolatrie among the people, then Ioshua before his death called all the tribes of Israell to Shechem, Ioshua, 24.1. etc. and expostulating the matter with them in very many and most pithie wordes throughout the most part of the chapter, specially ve. 14. etc. at the last brought them to this, that they put away their strange Gods. vers. 23. and said, vers. 24. The Lord our God will we serue, and his voyce will we obey.
And so Ioshua renewed the couenant, vers. 25.
 In the booke of Iudges it is written generally, chap. 2.8.11. that after the death of Ioshua and of the Elders, the Israelites forsooke the Lord, and followed idols, and that when they repenting but a little, cried to the Lord, hee was mercifull and sent them Iudges to deliuer them out of their enemies handes. And particularly it is afterward often said, When the children of Israell cried vnto the Lord, the Lord stirred them vp a Sauiour as, chap. 3.9.15. and 6.7. and 10.10. which words are sometime also to be vnderstood, and so vpon their repentance was the couenant in those daies often renewed as in one place specially, and in steade of many, it is manifest, euen, Chap. 10.16.

 In Samuels daies the people repented, and he renewed the couenant between God and Israel, 1. Sam. 7.2.3.4. etc.
 Because in Sauls daies religion was not regarded, Dauid in assembling al Israel to setch the Arke of God to Ierusalem, seemeth to renewe the couenant of God, 1. Chro. 13.
Asa King of Iudah encouraged by Azariah the prophet, destroyed idolatrie in his kingdome, restored true religion, and most gloriously renewed the couenant of the Lord their God, and reuiued the lawe of Deut. 13. as it is at large declared, 2. Chro. 15.12. etc.
Iosiah that good young king renewed the same couenaunt, 2. Kinges. 11.17. and 2. Chro. 23.16.
Iosiah that worthie king of religious memory likewise renewed this couenaunte, 2. Kings. 23.3. and 2. Chro. 34.31.
And though there be not the name and word of the couenant expressed, yet it is not to be doubted but that Iehosaphat and Hezekiah in reformation of religion renewed the Lords couenant.
 But after the Iewes were come out of Babylon to Ierusalem againe, Ezra returning the next yeare after the buylding of the Temple was finished, found that the people
by marying straunge wiues had broken the Lordes couenaunt, wherefore with greate feare and trembling, he procured that they put awaie their straunge wiues, and so the couenant was renewed. Ezr. 10. 
 About thirteene yeare after Ezra, (Ezr. 7.1.8. Nehem. 2.1.) came Nehemiah out of Babylon to Ierusalem, and builded vppe the walles of the Citie, and abode there twelue yeares (Nehem. 5.14.) in which space among other thinges, he finding that the people had transgressed the couenant againe by taking of straunge wiues, did renewe this couenaunt againe, and caused them to put away their straunge wiues, as the whole matter is declared in two whole Chapters, Nehem. 9. and 10. And heereto I might adde verie well, that which happened when Nehemiah that zealous prince returned to Ierusalem the second time, Nehem. 13.3. etc. But thus I haue gone through the whole storie of the olde Testament, and shewed howe the people ten times by a speciall kinde of repentance broke off their sinnes, preuented further iudgementes, and verie solemnely renewed the couenant betweene GOD and them. And I wish with such hearty desire as I beare to Gods glorie, and to the salvation
of my brethren, that these fewe, but worthie and notable examples, might driue vs all to repentance generally, and to the renewing of the Lordes couenant, which by our sinnes we haue broken, and so preuent greater iudgements which hang ouer our heades. For the Lorde by famine and dearth, by diuers and straunge diseases these fewe yeares past, euen such as neyther wee, norour fathers haue knowen, by a most terrible and fearefull plague and pestilence, which made vs all to tremble, by taking away many good men, euen some of the best men in the lande, doth euen thunder from heauen his terrible voyce to driue vs to renewe the couenant of our GOD, least if we consider not his fearefull iudgementes, but continue still in our sinnes, his holy hand, which yet is stretched out still, take holde on iudgement, and he execute vengeance on his enemies, and weede out them that hate him before he will renewe his couenant againe. For that as I saide before, is the seconde way of continuing GODS couenant, and whereof also I will giue you one example or two. For that it is a terrible kinde of renewing the coueuaunt, and there are not, as I thinke, many examples of it.

When the Israelites were come to Kadesh barnea (Deut: 2.14.) in the second yeare after they departed out of Egipt, they sent twelue men to searche the land of Canaan, that they might the better know which way to enter into it, and set vpon the inhabitants Num: 13. But ten of these twelue at their returne brought vp an euill report of the land Num: 13.32. Whereat the Israelites murmured and rebelled grieuously Num: 14. for which cause the Lords wrath so kindled against them, that he sware they should not enter into that land. But the Lorde made them continew in the wildernesse 38. yeres afterward, till he had destroyed all those rebels and not left one of them aliue Deut: 2.14. And all those also which followed Baal Peor Deut: 4.3, 4. Afterward the Lorde of his mercie had compassion on their posteritie, and in the 40. yere after their departure out of Egypt, when they were in the plaine of Moab by Iorden Num: 33.48.50, the couenant made at Horeb as I shewed before, was nowe againe renewed, as it is largely sette downe Deut: 29.
 Againe though by the meanes of Iosua, Samuel, and many good kings the couenant was often renewed, as I shewed before, yet their sinnes and their rebellions so mightely
increased day by day, that at the last the lorde caried the Iewes captiues into Babilon, and there weeded fro^ among the rest, the rebells, and the great sinners, and destroyed them Ezek: 20.38. and after seauentie yeres had compassion of the rest, and of his meere mercie, not of their deserts, brought them to Ierusalem againe, and renewed his couenant with them, euen of his mercie Ezek: 16.61. and 36.22, 32. And that we may throughly see this couenant was renewed of Gods free mercie only, both Ieremie before the captiuitie began, saith, It is the Lords mercies that we are not consumed, because his compassions faile not Lament: 3.22. and also Malachi after the captiuitie saith, Because I the Lorde change not, therefore ye sonnes of Iaccob are not consumed Malach: 3.6.
 Lastly, when the Iewes were returned out of captiuitie, and the couenant of grace was renewed, yet for all that Zerubbabel or Iehoshua, that Haggai or Zachariah, that Ezra, Nehemiah or Malachi could doe, they waxed worse and worse, and to fill vp the full measure of all their sinnes, they finally crucified the Lorde of life, euen the Lorde Iesus Christ our alone Sauiour: wherefore the Lorde hath nowe reiected them as reprobates, and scattered them vpon the face of
the earth, as fearefull spectacles of his heauy wrath euerie where. All this notwithstanding the faithful God, which keepeth couenant and mercy to a thousand generations, hath still continued his couenant to a fewe of the Iewes, as Paul sheweth Rom: 11.1. I demaund then, hath God cast away his people? God forbid: for I also am an Israelite, of the seede of Abraham etc. and to teach vs that this proceedeth of the Lorde free mercie, he saith Vers: 5. Euen so then at this present time is there a remnant through the election of grace.
 Quest. By this you haue said, it appeares to be a most fearefull thing to enter into Gods couenant. Were it not better to be out of the couenant?
Ans. It is not onely a fearefull thing, but also a most damnable thing to be out of Gods couenant, for they that be out, haue no hope of saluation. And to be in the couenant, is only blessednes, if man continue therin. As the magistrate is not to be feared for good workes, but for euill, Rom. 13.3. so the Lord is not a terror to them that keep his couenant but to them that breake it.
Quest. I see, and it is too manifest to be deried, that there was continually a couenant made betweene God and man vnder the law before
Christ came. But now in the tyme of the Gospel is there, or ought there to be any such couenant?
Ans.The couenant of God vnder the gospel. Yea, there ought to be, there hath beene, and is at this day, and shall be to the end of the world. When Iohn the baptist began to preach the gospel, and gather a new Church, a new people for Christ, he renewed this couenant with all those whome he baptised. For when the scripture Math. 3. witneseth, that he admitted none to baptisme, but vpon confession of their sinnes, which was both a renouncing of them, and also a promising of amendment of life, and of obedience of God; and that many voluntarily submitted themselues to his order, which was the ordinance of God, and receiued the sacrament of Baptisme, which is the signe of the couenant, and to be ministred to none, but only to them that are in the couenant: it is more then manifest, that Iohn gathering a holy people to the Lord out of that corrupt and disordred state of the Iewes, renewed the couena^t of God. when Peter conuerted so many at one sermon Act. 2.38. He admonished them of repentance, and so after they had yeelded themselues to the couenant of God, and promised to do what the Lord commaunded, they receiued baptisme, which is the signe of
the couenant. The same is to be affirmed of those whome Paul conuerted, Act, 19.17.18. And afterward when the Apostle planted Churches in diuers places, it appeareth many wayes that they at the first made the couenant betweene God and them; els they could haue planted no Church. For declaration herof mark what Paul speaketh of the Church which then was at Rome, Rom. 6.17. But God be thanked, that ye vvere the seruants of sin, but ye haue obeyed from the heart vnto the form of doctrine, vvhereunto ye were deliuered. The same co^me^dation he also giueth of som other Churches as of the Church at Corinth 2. Cor. 9.13. Which by experimente of this ministration, praise God for your voluntary submissio^ to the Gospel of Christ. And of the Church of Macedonia, 2. Cor. 8.5. They gaue their owne selues first to the Lord and after vnto vs by the vvill of God. And of the Church at Philippi Phillip. 2.12. Wherefore my beloued, as ye haue alwaies obeied, not as in my presence only, but novv much more in mine absence etc. Out of these and diuers such other places, it is euident, that where the Apostles planted any Churches, they caused all the beleeuers to promise to doe whatsoeuer the Lord commaundeth. But I will conclude with one word. When Christ the mediator renewed
this new couenant betweene God and man, the Apostle Heb. 8.10. rehearsing the couenant, mentioneth the very words wherein it was first made, and wherein it hath so often beene renewed, euen these; I vvill be their God, and they shalbe my people. Which general wordes the Apostle Paul applieth to the Church at Corinth, 2. Cor. 6.16.
 Quest. Can you shevv by examples hovv this couenant hath beene continued, and renevved vnder the Gospel, as you did before vnder the lavv?
Ans.The continewance of the conenant vnder the Gospel Although the history of the gospell in the new testament conteine in it but a short time, that from the time when Iohn Baptist began to preach, to the end of the Actes and writings of the Apostles there is not full foure score yeare (I except the prophesies) that we might shew the repetition of the couenant from time to time, as we did out of the old testament, which conteineth a historie of things done in that Church from the beginning of the world almost til Christ came in the flesh, euen till the dayes of Alexander the greate who liued about 330. yeares afore Christ came: Neuerthelesse that which is written Deut. 29.14.15. Neither make I this couenant, and this oath vvith you on ly, but asvvell vvith him that standeth here with vs this day before the Lord our God, as
vvith him that is not here vvith vs this day, (that is, with the posteritie which is yet vnborne) and Deut. 31.10. of the repeating of the couenant euery seauenth yere more solemnely, must be taken more generally then for the posteritie of Iacob only, and being rightly compared with my last answere before will proue sufficiently that the couenant hath beene renewed often vnder the Gospel, as it was vnder the Law. Besides, that which is wanting, in the new testame^t by reason of the shortnes of the story, is somwhat touched and in part supplyed by ecclesiasticall writers, which haue recorded some of the practises and customes of the churches in their dayes.
 Qu. VVhat hath any ecclesiasticall vvriter spoken hereof? or vvhat hath beene the custom of the Church herein?
Ans. Ecclesiasticall writers make mention of two manners of catechising, which differed both in regard of time, and in respect of persons: the one was before baptisme: the other was after baptisme: the one was catechising of them that were strangers from the couenant; the other was of them that were in the couenant: the one was of heathens before they were receiued into Gods couenant and into the fellowship of the Church; the other was of the children of the faithful.

 Quest. What is there vvritten of the former manner of catechising, that we may therein see the continuance or renuing of the couenant?
Ans.^^e former maner of catechising.Iustine, sometimes a heathen Philopher, but after a famous martire of Christ, reporteth in his second apollogie of Christians that if any heathen man desired to be receiued into the fellowshippe of the Church, he was first catechised in the principles of reliligion, and then hearing further the word of God as it were the conditions of the couena^t, afterward came into the face of the congregatio^ and co^fessed that he did beleeue, and promised that he would obey the word of God, wherupo^ he was baptised and receiued into the fellowship of the Church. Now when the Church obserued this order, it is cleare that they co^tinewed the couenant of God among them. And that this order might be the better obserued, the church appointed sometimes, and in some places a longer space, at other times and in other places a shorter time for catechising of heathens before they were baptised. Socrates lib. 7. Cap: 30. writeth that the Burgonians werseauen daies inlearning their catechisme, and then baptised the eight, Ierome ad pammachiam saith, the custome in his days was to catechise them fourty daies, and then to baptise them. Tertullian de baptismo writeth
that there were two times in the yeare, ^^ster and Whitsontide specially appointe^ (...) the Church for baptisme, and strangers: (...) the couenant were instructed in the principl^ of religion all the rest of the yeare against these two times. And thus farre the couenant was continued, that no stranger was admitted into the societie of the Saintes, but he first solemnly entred into Gods couenant, and promised to doe what the Lorde commaunded in his worde.
 Quest. You haue sufficiently shewed me that the Church was so mindfull of the couenant that they receiued none into their felowship, but those onely that submitted themselues to the ordinances of God, which is a thing worthie good consideration. But my desire was and is to know if the faithfull themselues beeing of the couenaunt, did at any time repeate it or renewe it.
Ans. The second manner of catechising,
The seco^d manner of catechi^sing. whereof I spake before, and which now is to be declared, sheweth the continuance of the couenant euen among the faithfull. For the place, Deut. 26.14.15. whereof I spake a little before, teacheth vs that when the Lord receiueth any into his couenant, hee doth not receiue that partie alone which then in his owne person doth promise to
doe what the Lord commaundeth, but also (...) his infinite mercie he receiueth that mans ^^^teritie though then vnborne, euen for ^housandes of generations,
^^e former manner of cachis^. as also it appeareth, Gen. 17.7. I will establish my couenant betweene mee and thee and thy seede after thee in their generations for an euerlasting couenant. And the other place of Deut. 31.10. before mentioned also, as touching the solemne repeating of the lawe and couenant: euen both these places teach vs that there ought to be a continuall repeating of the couenant, which thing hath well beene obserued in this other kinde of catechising. For the children of the faithfull which were baptised in their infancie, when they came to yeares of discretion haue been taught both priuatly at home, and publikely in the congregation, what great thinges the Lorde did for them and for their forefathers when he receiued them into his couenant: which thinges when the children of the faithfull had learned, and were able sensibly to render a reason of their faith, then they in the presence of the congregation did openly declare their faith, and promised to obey the commaundementes of God, and so in their owne person renewed Gods couenant, and were then confirmed to be of the couenant. And
this is that which in auncient times was casled confirmation, howsoeuer the detestab^^ two horned beastes and antichrist^^^ Rome haue abused it. Also that the ^^^^dren of the faithfull might be religiou^ ^^structed in the principles of religion,
Two chief ticles of and know what greate thinges God had done for them, and be able thereof to render a sound reason and sensible,  before they were confirmed: there were in the primitiue Church catechisers which instructed both heathens before they were baptised, and also the children of the faithfull before they were confirmed. Such catechisers or doctors were Pantenus (Euseb. lib. 5. cap. 9.) Clemens (Euseb. lib. 6. cap. 6. Origene (Euseb. lib. 6. cap. 8.) and others after them in the Church of Alexandria in Aegypt. And such a catechiser was Optatus at Carthage in Ciprians daies, Ciprian. lib. 3. Epist. 22. And by these and such other meanes was Gods couenant repeated, renewed, and continued from generation to generation, euen to these our daies as you see.
 Quest. Was there any other custome in the primitiue Church to declare the continuance of this couenant?
Ans. The Church then so diligently kept this holy couenant, that if any man performed not
his promise of obeying Gods commaun^^^entes, but transgressed, neyther vpon due ^^^^^ition amended his fault as Gods lawes ^^^houd; the same person was banished and ex^^reth unicated out of the companie and fe^^^wship of the faithfull till hee amended. And you see excommunication continueth to this day, so that you neede no more to let you vnderstande what care the Church of Christ hath had of the co^tinuance of Gods couenant.
 Quest. It is most true and euident vvhich you say, and I am therewith satisfied. But as excommunication is continewed in the Church, so I wish catechising were also continewed, that though there be fewe or no heathens at all which desire to be of Gods couenant (so neare is the fulnesse of the gentiles come in, and so neare may we feare least our reiection bee at hand, whereof Paul long since admonished vs, Rom. 11.22.25.) yet the children of the faithfull might be instructed, and so continue the couenant of God, why is not this catechising now vsed?
Ans.Catechising continued. It is continued amongs vs or else the fault is in the preachers, who are enioyned to catechise the youth of their parish euery Lordes day in the after noone. And the children of the faithfull thus catechised and taught the principles of religion, are to
come into the face of the congregation assembled in the Church, and there to confesse their faith, and to promise obedi^^^^ vnto the commaundementes of Go^ ^^^^^ding to that little and short catechi^^ (...) forth by authority,
Two chief ^^ticles of wherein the holy practises of the primitiue Church are most worthily and liuely expressed as touching this thing speake of,  euen the continuance and renewing of the couenant. For therein the childe openly promiseth in his owne person three thinges: first to forsake the flesh, the world and the diuell; secondly to beleeue all the articles of the christian faith; thirdly to keepe God holy commaundementes.
 Quest. What are the principles of religion that long since were, and now are, or ought to be taught in the Church of Christ?
Ans.Of the principles of Christian religio^. Those which are set downe by the holy Ghost, Heb. 6.1.2. as for example. 1. First, repentance from dead workes, that is, both true sorrow for former sinnes, and also in regard of the time to come, a renouncing of the workes of the flesh, the worlde and the diuell. 2. Secondly, faith towards God, that is, a confession of the trinitie, and of our saluatio^ by the mercies of God in Iesus Christ our Lord. 3. Thirdly, the doctrine of baptisme, that is, the mysterie and the meaning of
the sacramentes. 4. Fourthly, laying on (...) handes, that is, that the children of the (...) being catechised, should make open (...) of their repentance, of their faith, (...) sacramentes of God, and so haue handes laide vpon them, and be confirmed to be of the couenant of God, and of the visible Church. 5. Fiftly, the resurrection from the dead, that is, that albeit they should die and their bodies be laide in the earth, yet at the last day they should be raised vp to life againe. 6. Sixtly, eternall iudgement, that is, that God the eternall iudge, who will then condemne the wicked to eternall condemnation, will giue them that are thus receiued into his holy couenant, and accordingly continue therin, an euerlasting crowne of glory in his heauenly kingdom for euermore.
 Quest. Why are not our children now a daies taught these principles of religion?
Ans. They be. For when they are taught the Lords praier, the articles of Christian faith, the ten commandements, and the meaning and vse of the sacraments, then do they learne these principles of religion before mentioned. And if you consider well the questions propounded and answers made by children in our churches where there is a godly and painefull minister, ye shall see that these things are both taught
and learned. For when our children in answering the minister, solemnly renounce the flesh the world, and the diuell; when they conf^^^ the articles of christian faith; and wh^^^ promise to obey Gods commaundement (...) that little catechisme established by authoritie requireth:
Two chief articles of then they plainely shewe they haue learned these principles of religion, and keepe the custom of the primitiue Church,  and so the couenant between God and ma^ is renued and continued from generation to generation.
 Quest. I pray you declare and lay open these principles of religion more fully, and first for their order, secondly for the summe of them.
Ans. That order I thinke best,
The order to be obserued in the principles of religion. which is most naturall and most agreeable to the couenant of God. For where there is no couenant between God and man, there these principles of Christian religion are not regarded. But where there is a couenant made betweene God and man, God first requireth that his gracious promises should be beleeued, and secondly that his commandements should be obeied. Againe as the fire is before the heat, the sunne before the light, the fountaine before the riuer that runneth from it, and generally as the cause efficient is before the effect, so is faith before the law. For good works are the fruites of faith. Thirdly without faith neither the sacramentes
can be comfortable vnto vs, nor our obedience see ptable to God, nor yet our praiers be hard (...) granted. For without faith it is impossible (...) God. Heb. 11.6.
^^^st. Then your meaning is, that the first place of right belo^geth to faith, the second to the commandementes.
Ans. Whether we respect the time in the making of the couenant, or the naturall order of causes, or the expresse word of God, faith must needes be set before the workes of the Law.
Quest. But what say you to the other priuciples of religion, as prayer, and the sacramentes? what place will you assigne to them?
Ans. The order agreed vpon for faith and for the law, there needs no great question to be made for the rest. For the sacraments are as necessarily annexed to faith, as the seale to an obligation. And praier likewise followeth the commandements, that what wants soeuer we find either in our faith, or in our obedience to the co^mandements by reason of our manifold infirmities, we should by earnest and often praiers craue of God that he would minister vnto vs some supply by the powerful presence of his Spirit, and specially that through the obedience of Iesus Christ we may be accepted.
 Quest. I vnderstand then it is your meaning to obserue this order; to speake first of faith and of
the sacraments, secondly of the commandements and of prayer. I pray you therefore let me heare what the chiefe articles of faith be, which we ought to beleeue.
Ans.Two chief articles of faith. The holy ghost setteth downe two principal articles of our faith Heb. 11.6. in these wordes, He that commeth to God must beleeue 1. that God is, and 2. that he is a rewarder of them that seeke him. 
 Q. Concerning the former of these two articles, is there any ma^ which denieth that there is a God?
Ans. The Apostle saith not, he that co^meth to God must beleeue that there is a God, as though he had to deal with Protagoras who doubted whether there were any God or no, or as though he had to deale with Diagoras Melius, Theodorus, Cyrenaicus, Eumenes, Tegeates, and such like who denied flatly that there was any God: but he saith, he that commeth to God, and so professeth God, must beleeue that God is, that is, that he is such a God as the word describeth him to be, omniscient, omnipotent, iust, righteous, mercifull, gracious etc. and not to say in hart, God seeth me not when I commit iniquitie Psal. 10.11.13. and Psal. 50.21. or, though I commit these abhominations yet God wilbe mercifull vnto me and not punish me according to his word Deut. 29.19. Rom. 2.3
or to haue any other such imagination in his heart. He I say that commeth to GOD must not haue any of these, or any such other cogitation in his minde, but must faithfully and firmly beleeue that God is euen such a God, as he sheweth himselfe in his word. Yea he that commeth to God must not hypocritically confesse him with his mouth, and most impiously denie him in his workes Tit. 1.16.
 Quest. Do you not then condemne many men in these dayes,, who say they are gospellers, and if ye demaund of them whether they beleeue that God is, will answere you angerly, and say ye abuse the^ to ask any such question, and yet in their deeds God wots are wicked men, as vsurers, drunkards, gluttons, whormo^gers, cruell oppressors, theeues, bribers, couetous, murderers, craftie deceiuers and such like, as without repentance shall neuer enter into the kingdom of heauen.
Ans. No if there be anie such, I condemne them not, but it is their owne deedes 1. Cor. 6.9. Rom. 8.23. Galat. 5.19. It is the word of God Iohn. 12.48. and their owne consciences Rom. 2.15. Tit. 3.11. that shall condemne such hypocrites at that day. Who nothing regarding the terror of the Lord (2. Cor. 5.11.) doe abuse his maiestie in a hie degree of presumptuous sinne, which is most dangerous and dreadfull. For the Lord hath
saide Deut. 29.19. That he will not be mercifull to such.
 Quest. But to leaue such to God, what say you more concerning faith in God?
Ans.Of faith It is first requisite that we know what faith is, before we can shew what faith in God is. 
 Quest. What is faith then how do you define it, or what doe you call it?
Ans.Two sorts of faith Before we can define it and declare what it is, it must of necessitie first be distinquished or deuided. For there are two sortes of faith so diuers in their nature, that they cannot both possibly be comprehended in one definition or description. 
 Quest. Which be those two kindes of faith?
Ans. There neither is, neither can there be any faith, but where two persons are, the one promising some thing, and the other receiuing and beleeuing that promise. And in either of these two persons there is a seuerall faith differing either from other, euen one in him that promiseth, and an other in him to whome the promise is made. But the faith of the one is so diuers and differring from the faith of the other that they cannot both be conteined in one definition.
 Quest. VVhat is his faith that maketh the promise?

Ans. It is truth, faithfulnesse, constancie in performing that he promised. This faith is specially in God, who is alwaies trew in all his doings, and faithfull in all his promises, as the scripture euery where witnesseth. And this faith ought to be in euery man truely and saith fully to performe all his promises made either to God or man. And the prophet Dauid saith, it is one of the markes whereby Gods elect are knowne and discerned from others Psal. 15.4. to performe that he promiseth though it be to his losse.
 Quest. What is his faith to whome any thing is promised, and which receiueth and beleeueth the promise?
Ans. It is a sure, a certaine, a full perswasion that in due time and maner we shall enioy the thinges which are promised.
 Quest. Now then to goe forward with your purpose,
Of the person of God what is it to beleeue that God is?
Ans. It is to beleeue that God is such a God as he hath promised to be vnto vs, and such a God as the word describeth him to be both in respect of his person, and also in respect of his properties or essentiall qualities, if I may so speake.
 Quest. I pray you shew me these two things you spake of the person and the propertie of God, and first what saith the scripture touching the
person of God?
The scripture sheweth these things, 1. that there is one God only in essence or substance: 2. that there are three persons, the Father, the Sonne, and the holy Chost: 3. that euery one of these three persons is God: 4. that there are not three Gods, but one God only.
 Quest. These are deepe misteries and difficult matters whereof you speake, yet I desire to beare somwhat of them, and first shew me that there is one God alone.
Ans. That there is one God only it is proued first by testimonie of the scripture Deut. 6.4.
There is but one God. Heare O Israell the Lord our God is Lord only. Secondly by the creation of the worlde Ierem: 10.10.11.12. The Gods that haue not made the heauens and the earth, shall perish from the earth, and from vnder the heauens. And Dauid saith Psal. 96.5. The Gods of the people are idols, but the Lord made the heauens. Thirdly by his prouidence, as it appeareth Esai 45.5.6.7, 8. the words I omit for breuity fourthly by the miracls which he wroght in Egipt and for deliuerance of Israel as Moses sheweth that the Lord is God alone. Deut. 4.34.35.36. And Christ also proued himselfe to be God by the miracles he did Iohn. 5.36. and 10.25.38.
 Quest. Shew me also that there are three
persons.
There are three persons.
Ans. This is manifest Esai 63.9.10. For there is first the Lord, that was troubled in their troubles: secondly, there is the Angel of his presence, which is Iesus Christ: thirdly, there is his holy spirit, which the Israelites vexed. And if you read the text, you shall see it plainely. Also when Iohn baptized Christ Math. 3.17. there is first Christ baptised: Secondly, there is the voice of the father from heauen: Thirdly, there is the holy ghost descending like a doue. Againe Math. 28.19. Christ commaundeth that baptisme be ministred in the name of the Father, of the son and of the holy ghost you may reade also 2. Cor. 13.13.
 Quest. Can it likewise be proued, that each of these three persons, is God?
Ans.The Father is god First concerning the father, I suppose there is no doubt, there fore it shall suffice to say with Iohn 3.16. God so loued the world, that he gaue his only begotten sonne etc.
Secondly; of the sonne thus speaketh the Prophet Esai.
The son is God. 9.6. But vnto vs a childe is borne, and vnto vs a sonne is giuen: and the gouernement is vpon his souldiers, and he shall call his name wonderfull, Counseller. The mightie God, the euerlasting father, the Prince of peace etc. Paul saith Rom. 9.5.
of whome came Christ, who is GOD ouer all blessed for euer. And in an other place it is said Heb: 1.8. But vnto the sonne he saith,
O God, thy throne is for euer etc.
Thirdly,
The holy Ghost is God. of the holy Ghost thus saith Peter act: 5.3. Why hath Sathan filled thine hearte, that thou shouldest lie vnto the holy Ghost. And in the next verse, thou hast not lied vnto men, but vnto GOD. Paul saith 1. Cor: 6.19. knowe ye not that your bodie is the temple of the holy Ghost. and 1. Cor: 3.16. knowe ye not that ye are the Temple of God, and that the spirit of God dwelleth in you?
 Quest.
There are not three Gods, but one God alone. Lastly it remaineth yet that you shew there are not three Gods, but one God alone.
Ans.
