In the sixt chapter of Esai, the prophet saw the Lord in a vision ver: 1. and the Angels cried one to an other, Holy holy holy is the Lord of hostes vers: 3. and the Lord commanded Esaiah to go and prophesie vnto the people vers: 8, 9. Nowe if it be demanded who this Lord was that appeared to Esaiah, and bad him go and prophesie, I suppose all men will easily grant it was the Father. And that it was the Sonne it appeareth Iohn: 12.41. These things said Esaias when he saw his glory (that is, Christs glory) and spake of him, that is, of Christ. And Paul witnesseth
that it was the holy Ghost act: 28.25. For in citing that sixt chapter of Esaias, he saith thus: Well spake the holy ghost by Esaias the Prophet etc.
Also the Apostle Iohn in his first epistle Chap. 5. Vers. 7. speaketh thus: There are three which beare record in heauen, the Father, the word, and the holy Ghost: and these three are one. 
 Quest. Now that you haue declared these foure things concerning the person of God, I desire to heare somthing also of the properties of God, as you promised before?
Ans.The properties of God We must first consider the properties of God generally as he is one God in Essence, and secondly the properties of euery person by himselfe.
 Quest. What say you then of the properties of God in generall?
Ans. He that co^meth to God must beleeue that God is, that is, such a one as the word describeth him to be, as for example, that he is omniscient Prou. 15.3. The eyes of the Lord in euery place hehold the euill and the good. That he is omnipotent Psal. 115.3. Our god is in heauen: he doth whatsoeuer he will. That he is eternal Psal. 90.2. from euerlasting to euerlasting thou art our God. That he is infinite 1. King. 8.27. Behould, the heauens,
and the heauens of heauens are not able to containe thee. That he is good, Math. 5.45. and 19.17. That he is mercifull, Exod. 34.6. That he is iust, Psal. 97.2. etc. And as they that come to God must thus beleeue that God is, so must they not say when they commit iniquity, The Lord shall not see: neyther will the God of Iacob regard it, Psal. 94.7. Nor in their destresse, despaire of the power and goodnesse of God, as the Israelites did, Psal. 78.19. nor in prosperity say as the Edomites did, Obadi. vers. 3. nor when they haue satisfied the desires of the flesh, wipe their mouth and say with the harlot, Pro. 30.20. I haue not committed iniquity, nor when they are threatned with Gods iudgements say contemptuously, Let him make speede, let him hasten his worke that vve may see it. Esat. 5.19. nor seeke deepe to hide their counsell from the Lord when they do euill secretly, Esai. 29.15. nor desperately say, We haue made a couenant with death, Esay. 28.15. nor denie the Lord and say, it is not hee, Ierem. 5.12. nor giue the Nazarites wine to drinke: nor commaund the prophets saying, prophesie not, Amos. 2.12. Mich. 26. nor sweare by the sinne of Samaria, Amos. 8.14. nor generally they must not thinke, speake, or do any thing, which the Lord forbiddeth in his word. But they must reuerently feare and obey the
Lord and his ministers, and all his ordinances. Thus must they beleeue that God is, which wil come to him to be of his house and familie.
 Quest. What say you now touching the special properties of euery person by himselfe?
Ans.The Father The Father is said to beget the Son, the Son is begotten, the holy Ghost proceedeth from them both, but the maner of the begetting of the Son and of the proceeding of the holy Ghost is vnsearchable and vncomprehensible, and therefore we may not be curious to inquire too farre of the maiesty least we be oppressed of the glory. Then to speake within the boundes of the scripture and of our owne measure, the Father is said to be Almighty, etc as was said before generally, not because those properties are peculiar to the first person only, but because the first person is as it were the fountaine and the welspring of the deity.
 Quest. What say you of the Sonne?
Ans.The person of the Son. The Son is specially to be considered as he is the mediator between God and man, and therfore as he is both God and man. Wherfore we must first co^sider his person, then his office.
Quest. What say you of this person?
Ans. He being God equal with the Father, assumed and tooke to his deity humain nature and was borne of the virgin Mary, Math. 1.18. etc. Luk. cap. 1. and 2. and 3. and so was one person
consisting of two natures, the diuine and the humaine.
 Quest. Wherefore did he take our nature vpon him, and became man also as we bee?
An. Because he must be the mediator betwen God and man, and by his owne death satisfie Gods iustice and reconcile vs to God againe.
 Quest. Could he not haue done this being God onely, except he also tooke our nature?
Ans. No, for if he had beene only God, he could not haue suffred death for vs: and if he had beene man onely, he could not haue ouercome death. Therefore that he might suffer death for vs to satisfie the iustice of God, who would not be reconciled to vs but by death, Gen. 2.17 it was necessary that he should be man and that he might ouercome death, and so deliuer vs fro^ death, and the ransom paid might be answerable and sufficie^t, Act. 20.28. and 1. Pe. 1.19. it was necessary that he should be God also
 Quest. Seeing then Christ is both God and man in respect of his person, what say you of his office?
Ans.The office of Christ. Christ our mediator being both God and man in one person, is in respect of his office annointed with the holy Ghost, (Act. 10.38.) to be a Prophet, a Priest and a King.
 Quest. How is he a Prophet, or what is his office in that he is a Prophet?
Ans.Christ our prophet. He is our Prophet in that the Lorde
hath appointed him to reueile vnto vs and teach vs the will and the counsell of God so farre as concerneth our saluation.
 Quest. How then did they that died before Christ came, had they no prophets? or knew not they the meanes of saluation? For I take it your meaning is, that Christ is our onely prophet.
Ans. It is true, Christ is our only doctor or prophet,
Christ our Prophet from the beginning and we are forbid to acknowledge any other, Mat. 23.8. But as the messenger or inferiour magistrate sent from the king with commission and authority to execute some duty, doth not make that therfore there is no king, or that there are two kinges: so other prophets being men and sent by Christ, do not make that Christ is not our prophet, or that we haue moprophets then Christ. And that Christ hath beene the great prophet to reueil the mysteries of saluation to Gods elect from the beginning of the world, I meane since the first fall of Adam, it may be proued by the testimony of Peter, who 1. Pet. 3.19. witnesseth that eue^ Christ though then he had not taken our nature, went by his diety and preached in Noe before the floud to those disobedient persons which are mentioned, Gen. 6. and which perished in the waters for not obeying Christ their Prophet, and now are, as Peter saith, in prison, that is in bell. And that Christ preached afterwards in
the other prophets it appeareth, in that he gaue commandement to that great prophet Moses Exod. 3.2. Act. 7.30. etc. And as the Lord said of Christ since he tooke our nature, Mat. 17.5. heare him: so the same Lord said of Christ long since, euen when Israel was newly come out of Aegypt, Exod. 23.21. Beware of him, and heare his voyce, and prouoke him not, etc. And whosoeuer wil not hearken to my words, which he (that is, Christ) shall speake in my name, I will require it of him saith the Lord, Deut. 18.19. as it is plainely expounded, Act. 3.22. etc. and 7.37. etc
 Quest. But seeing Christ hath been the prophet since the beginning, and now in these last daies took our nature and came and preached in his own person, after died, and rose againe, and is ascended into heauen, and sitteth at the right hand of the father, doth he not cease to do the office of a prophet?
Ans. No, as before his comming in the flesh he preached in the former prophets; so he now preacheth in the ordinary ministers of his word and saith of the^. He that heareth you, heareth me: and he that despiseth you, despiseth me, Luk. 10.16. 
 Quest. Then it is your opinion that there ought as great reuerence and obedience to be giuen to the word of God preached in these daies by silly poore me^ and sinners, as if Christ himself preached
Ans. Yea, For Christ saith, Iohn. 20.21. that as the father sent him, so he sendeth them.
Which words lest any man should thinke to be spoken to the twelue Apostles onely, Paul telleth vs, Ephes. 4.12. that Christ gaue aswel ordinarie pastors and teachers, as extraordinarie Apostles. Also preachers teach the same doctrine that Christ did, and that Christ commaunded them, Mat. 28.20. and hath promised to be with them alwaies vnto the end of the world. Wherefore as it was saide to the rich man in hell of Moses and the prophets, Luke. 16.29.31. so I say of the preachers of the world which teach nothing but that Christ commandeth them, that those which will not beleeue the word of God preached by men called to that office, will not beleeue though Christ came againe and preached. Iohn saith, he that knoweth God heareth vs. 1. Iohn. 4.6.
Quest. What say you more concerning Christ our prophet? 
Ans.Foure obseruations In his office of prophesie I obserue these foure things. 1. First, that Christ hath reueiled, and daily doth reueile vnto vs the whol counsell of God, so farre as concerneth vs and the meanes of our saluation. For Christ himselfe saith, Iohn. 15.15. All things that I haue heard of my Father, haue I made knowen to you. 2. Secondly, that the ministers of the word are the ambassadours of Christ: as Paule sheweth, 2. Cor. 5.20. Now then are we ambassdours for
Christ: as though God did beseech you through vs, we pray you in Christes steed, that ye be reconciled to God. 3. Thirdly, they that in these daies of the cleare light of the gospell, are ignorant of the means ofsaluation, shalbe excuseles at the day of iudgement. For if our gospel be hid, saith Paul, 2. Cor. 4.3. it is hid to them that are lost. Wherfore he saith in an other place, if any man be ignorant, let him be ignorant, 1. Cor. 14.38. 4. Fourthly, they that contemne saluation so plentifully offred, shal perish for euermore.
 Quest. VVhat say you now of his other office, of his priesthood?
Ans.Christ our priest. That he was ordained of God from the beginning to be our priest, euen our high priest after an other order and after a better order then that priesthood of Aarons was, as it appeareth, Psa. 110.4. The Lord sware and wil not repent, Thou art a priest for euer after the order of Melchizedek which sheweth that he was perfigured in Melchizedek from the be ginning, Gen. 14.
 Quest. What difference betweene Christ and Aaron, and their priesthoods?
Ans. Very great.
Differences betweene Christ and Aaron. First in regard of their parentage they differ, for Aarons linage and stocke is knowen and recorded in the scripture, Exo. 6.16.18.20. and elsewhere. But Christ answerably to the type of Melchizedek, is
without father, touching his humanitie, and without mother, concerning his deity, Heb. 7.3. Also Aaron came of the tribe of Leui, but Christ of the tribe of Iuda, Heb. 7.13.14.
 Secondly, the manner of their consecration was diuers, wereby it is euident that their priesthoodes are not all one. For Christ was consecrated priest with an oath, as it is, Psa. 110.4. The Lord sware, etc. but Aaron without an oath, Heb. 7.20.21. Againe, Aaron was made priest after the Law of the carnall commaundement, but Christ after the power of the endlesse life, Heb. 7.16. Also materiall oyle was powred vpon Aaron at his consecration, Leu. 8.12. but Christ was annointed with the holy Ghost, (Act. 10.38.) who at his baptisme descended like a doue and light vpon him, Math. 3.16.
 Thirdly their offices and the execution therof, differ in many things, as for example.
 The Leuitical priesthood was vnperfect, but Christs priesthood was and is perfect, He. 7.11.
 The Leuites died and had successors, and al their priesthood was temporary; but Christ, priesthood is eternall, and he liueth for euer, Heb. 7.23.24.
Aaron and his successors were priests only, but Christ is both king and priest, Heb. 7.1.2.
 As Melchizedek was greater then Abraham,
in that he receiued tythes of him and blessed him (for the lesse is euer blessed of the greater) so Christ and his priesthoode is greater then Aaron and his priesthoode Heb. 7.4. etc. Aaron and his successors offred the bodies and the blood of beastes,  but Christ offred his owne bodie and his owne bloud Heb. 9.12. and 10.5:
Aaron and his successors were sinners,  and offered sacrifices as well for themselues as for the people; but Christ being without sin (1: Pet. 2.22.) offred him selfe for the people only Heb: 5:3. and. 7.28.
Aaron and his successors offred oftentimes one manner of sacrifice; but Christ offred himselfe once only Heb. 10.11.12.
Aaron and his successors entred into the tabernacle made with handes; but Christ is entred into very heauen Heb. 8.6. and 9.11.24.
Aaron and his successors were but ministers, but Christ is the Author of saluation Heb. 5.9. And there are many moe differe^ces between the priesthoode of Christ and of the Ieuits, mentioned Heb 7. and 8. and 9. and 10.
 Quest. I pray you shewe me briefely what Christes office is, in that he is our priest.
Ans. In one word to answer you, it is to pray for vs, and to offer vp sacrifice
for vs.
 Quest. What was the sacrifice he offred for vs.
It was his owne bodie Psalm. 40.7. Heb. 10.5. Sacrifice and offring thou wouldest not but a bodie hast thou ordeined me:
Christes sacrifice And his owne blood Heb. 9.12. by his owne blood entred he in once vnto the holy place, and obtained eternall redemption for vs. And from all things, from which we could not be absolued by the law of Moses, by Christ euery one that beleeueth, is discharged act. 13.39. Heb 10. Verse. 1. etc. For he is the lambe of God that taketh away the sinnes of the worlde Iohn. 1.29.36.
 Quest. Doe you then comprehend the whole storie of his passion in this oblation of his selfe?
Ans. The history of his passion is at large set downe in the gospell, namely that he suffered in his bodie when he was hungry,
Christes sufferings when he was euill spoken of, when he was persecuted, beaten, buffeted, reuiled, crowned with thornes, crucified vpon the crosse, thrust into the side with a speare, so that at the last he gaue vp the ghost, died, and was buried: and that he suffred in soule when he saide to his disciples that his soule was heauie euen to the death, when he kneeled
downe three times and desired that cup might passe from him if it were possible, when in this his prayer he was in such agonie that his sweate was like droppes of bloud trickling downe to the ground, when he cryd vpon the crosse, my God, my God, why hast thou forsaken me, when he offred prayers and supplications with strong crying and teares vnto him that was able to saue him from death, and was also heard in that he feared Heb. 5.7. I say the storie of the gospell declareth these and others of his suffrings ple^tifully. But you required but the chiefe pointes of his suffering which was seene best in his sacrifice which he our priest offred for vs, and so accordingly I answered you, purposing but briefely to touch that which others haue handled at large.
 Quest. What prayers did he offer to God for vs?
Ans.Christs prayers for vs. We heard but now what earnest prayer he offred, when the curse of God due to vs for our sinnes, was laide vpon our nature in his bodie, that he hauing taken vpon him our nature, euen humane nature, and being co^secrated the prince of our saluation through affliction, might bring vs to glorie Heb. 2.10. But besides this he offred most sweete incense, a most comfortable prayer to God
for vs Iohn: 17. and it is worth the reading a thousand times. Also he being now entred into very heauen, appeareth in the sight of God for vs Heb: 9.24. and is able perfectly to saue them that come to God by him, seing he euer liueth to make intercession for them Heb. 7.25.
 Quest. What vse and comfort commeth to vs by his priesthood? 
Ans. First, we that beleeue in Christ, are deliuered from the wrath of God, and from the punishment or cursse of the law, because Christ was made a cursse for vs, Gal. 3.13.
 Secondly, we that beleeue in Christ are made righteous before GOD, because Christ hath fulfilled the Law for vs Rom. 8.3.4. and 10.4. and 1. Cor. 1.30.
 Thirdly, we that beleeue in Christ may boldly goe vnto the throne of Grace, and receiue mercie, and finde grace to helpe in time of neede, Heb. 4.16. Iohn. 14.13.
 Fourthly, we that beleeue in him, ought therfore by him to offer the sacrifice of prayse alwaie to God, Heb. 13.15.
Quest. Now that you haue shewed how Christ is our prophet, and our priest, let vs heare also his thirde office, and howe he is a
king.
Of the kingdom of Christ.
Ans. Christ was ordeined of God euen from the beginning to be a king, (Micah: 5.2.) and therefore to haue a kingdome, as we see he was prefigured in Melchi-zedek gen. 14.18 and as it is declared Heb. 7.1 and as it is manifest in the kings of Iudah who were types of Christ, as in Dauid; 2. Sam 7.14. Psal. 2.7. and 89.20, 26. in Salomon, 2. Sam. 7.45. Ps. 45. Heb. 1.8. And in others that succeeded til Christ came. For although the regal dignitie after the people were caried captiues into Babylon, was neuer in that glorious estate that it hath beene in before, according to the prophesie of Ezekiel Chap. 21.27. yet Iacobs prophesie Gen, 49.10, was verified, and the scepter or some shew thereof continewed in Iudah till Christ came.
 Quest. Was it then knowen to the Iewes before his incarnation, that he should be aking?
Ans.Christ acknowledged to be a king. As they knew before that he should be a priest, so did they know that he should be a king, for as his priesthoode and kingdome were both prefiguted in Melchizedec Gen 14. Heb. 7.1. as we haue heard before, so also his kingdom and priesthoode were prefigured in Iehoshua the hie priest Zechar 6.11.12.13. And therefore Ieremie Ch.
23.5. Ezekiel Chap, 37.22.24. and Zechariah Chap. 9.9. in expresse wordes called him a king. In the new testament he is acknowledged to be the king of the Iewes Math. 2.2. and 21.5. Iohn. 1.50, When Pilate asked Christ whether he were the king of the Iewes, he himselfe denied it not Iohn. 18.34.36.37. And this superscription did Pilate write ouer his heade when he was crucified, This is Iesus the king of the Iewes Math. 27.3.7.
 Quest. Seing then he is our king, shew me his kingdome.
Christs kingdome not of this world.
Ans. Christ not denying himselfe to be a king, tolde Pilate that his kingdome was not of this world Iohn. 18.36.
 Quest. If his kingdom be not of this world, whence then is it? or what is it?
Ans.The Chuch is Christes kingdome It is the Church of God that is Christes kingdome, and it is from aboue, that is, from heauen.
 Quest. VVhat is the Church of God? or how doe you define it?
Ans. It cannot easily be declared in one word, because vnder this name are comprehended somtimes all the elect of God, whether they be deade and departed out of this life, or they be nowe liuing here vpon the earth, or they be yet vnborne, and thus the
word, Church, is vsed Ephes. 1.22.23. Somtime by the name of the Church is ment the whole visible company of them that outwardly professe Christ and his Gospel in this world, as 1. Cor 12.28. Somtime it is vsed for some particular co^pany of those which professe the gospel, as the company that professed the gospel in the region of Galatia, the Church of England, the Church of France, the Church of Germany etc. And somtimes for the professors of the Gospel in one Citie, as at Ephesus, at Alexandria, at Corinth, or of one parish as we now vsually speake. Now though I might iustly tearme any of these the kingdome of Christ, yet this place specially requireth that we vnderstand the whole militant Church here vpon earth, and as it is visible.
 Quest. VVhat doe you meane then by the Church in this place?
Ans.The Church Both the whole multitude of the professors of the gospel in this world and specially the seueral companies of professors, and each of them, which haue the word of God preached among them, and the sacraments of Christ administred vnto them by Ministers thereunto called.
 Quest. How commeth it to Passe now that those which professe the gospell in this vvorlde,
are the Church and kingdome of Christ? for you saide a little before that Christes kingdom was not of this vvorld.
Ans. I saide before that Christes kingdom was not of this world and so I say still. Nenerthelesse Christes kingdome is in this world though not of this world.
Quest. Hovv can that be?
Ans.The faithful are strange in this life. Verie well: for he that is an English man borne, and a free denizen of England, may vpon occasion trauell into France or Italie, yet when he is in Italieor France, he is not of France or of Italy, but of England stil, and therefore reteineth the name of an English man when he is in France. He is only a stranger in other contries, his home is in England: And so the professors of the gospel in this world are as strangers, yet they are not of this world, but are of the kingdome of heauen.
 Quest. How can that be? this seemeth to me more strange then it was before. For they were borne in this world, were they not? they neuer came as strangers into this world out of any other new world, here they were borne, here they haue beene brought vp, here they liue, and shall till they dye. Did they euer come out of heauen? or what say you to this?
Ans. I can answer you this difficult and
straunge question very easily, and by a familiar similitude. If any man free borne in England, and partaker of the freedom and liberty of the land, do at any time renounce his freedome and liberty, he may well liue in England afterward, but he is none of the land, nor to be counted as one of England, but as a stranger. Againe if any man that is a free denison of London, or of any other place of liberty, and priueledge, do at any time disclaime his freedom and renounce his liberty, he is no longer a citizen of London, or a free denison of that place and liberty which he hath renounced, and if he remaine there afterward,
The faithfull renounce this world he is but as a stranger and a forener. So the faithfull that professe the gospell of Christ, though they were borne in this worlde, yet because they haue renounced the worlde they are none of the worlde, but are strangers in this worlde.
 Quest. Haue they that beleeue in Christ and professe his gospel rencunced this world and the priuiledges thereof at any time?
Ans. Yea they haue renounced it either when they were baptised, if they were heathens before, or else at their confirmation, if they were the children of the faithfull, as I haue shewed before in the first part when I spake of the couenant of GOD, and especially in answering
your 60. and 63. questions; as also in the beginning of this seconde part in answering your second question.
 Quest. I pray you repeate it here againe in a worde.
Ans. All men by nature are the children of Adam the children of their naturall parentes, borne into this worlde, and so by nature also the children of wrath, Ephes. 2.2. wherefore that we may be the children of God, and citizens of the kingdome of heauen, there are two things required, first that we be borne againe the second time, and secondly that we renounce this world.
 Quest. Shew me these two things more plainly?
Ans.The faithfull are regenerate. Christ saith Iohn. 3.3. except a man be borne againe, he cannot see the kingdome of God.
 Quest. How shall a man be borne againe?
Ans.Of our second birth To speake familiarly and plainely of this second birth or regeneration, I obserue these three thinges. 
 First the Church is our spirituall mother in whose womb we are conceiued, and of whom we are borne, as it is manifest in sundry places of the scripture. Esai. 51.18. and 66.7. Canticles cap. 3.4. and 8.2.5. Galat. 4.26.
Secondly, the fathers that beget vs are the ministers of the word, 1. Cor, 4.15. Galat. 4.19.
and 2. Cor. 6.13. And for this cause the Church and the fathers in the Church, are often called by the name of father and mother throughout the booke of the prouerbes of Salomon, and they that are thus begotten in the Church are called children and sonnes in the same booke, in these and such like wordes, My sonne, keepe thy fathers commaundement, and forsake not thy mothers instruction.
 Thirdly, the manner howe the children of God are begotten, regenerate, and borne a newe, is by the outwarde preaching of the worde, and by the inward working of the spirit, 1. Cor. 4.15. and 1. Pet. 1.23. If any man desire more curiously to know this mysterie of regeneration, then the scripture doth reueile it, let him heare what Christ saith, Iohn. 3.8. The winde bloweth where it listeth, and thou hearest the sound therof, but canst not tell whence it commeth, and whither it goeth: so is euery man that is borne of the spirit. Concerning our naturall generation no man can tell howe some part groweth into bones, some into gristles, some into sinewes etc. much lesse can any man conceiue of the spiritual regeneration.
 Quest. Then to come to the second point, how doe the faithfull renounce the world? do they not stall keepe their priuileges and liberties of their first birth and of this world?

Ans. No, they haue not the freedome and the priuiledges of two cities, or of two kingdomes, but when they are regenerate and made citizens of the new Ierusale^, of the kingdom of heauen, then they renounce and forsake the freedome of their first birth and of this world.
 Que. I pray you shew me this more manifestly.
Ans. I will make it manifest foure waies. First, by the practise of the Church and of them that are regenerate. For when any heathen man is conuerted to the faith and baptised, and when any of the children of the faithfull are confirmed, then they, the Church requiring it, do openly before the Church renounce the flesh, the world, and the diuell, as hath beene shewed before.
 Secondly, by the action of baptisme. For in baptisme a man is put into the water as if he were drowned, dead, and quite gone out of this worlde, and so dead with Christ: but immediately he riseth vp againe out of the water, as being raised vp with Christ vnto a new life. And so Paul expoundeth this mystery, Rom. 6.3. Knowe ye not, that all we which haue beene baptised into Iesus Christ, haue beene baptised into his death? we are buried then with him by baptisme into his death, that like as Christ was raised from the dead by the glory of the father, so
we also should walke in newnes of life.
 Thirdly, by the scripture, which saith that we haue forsaken this world, and are no longer of this world. Iohn. 15.19. If ye were of the world, the world would loue his own: but because ye are not of the world, but I haue chosen you out of the world, therefore the world hateth you. Heb. 13.14. heere we haue no continuing citie, but we seeke one to come. Read also, 1. Pet. 2.11.
 Fourthly, by the confession of the faithfull themselues for Dauid confesseth, Ps. 119.19. saying, I am a stranger vpon earth, etc. Abraham and his predecessors confessed that they were strangers and pilgryms on the earth, Heb. 11.13 Paul maketh like confession, 2. Cor. 5.1.2.3. 
 Quest. If the faithful be strangers heere in this world, what freedom or priuiledge haue they in the kingdom of heauen whereof they are?
The fredome of the faithfull.
Ans. They are no more strangers and forreners (as they were before their regeneration, and as all vnregenerate persons are) but they are citizens with the saintes, and of the houshold of God, Ephes. 2.19. and being raised vp together with Christ, are made to sit together in heauenly places in Christ Iesus Ephes. 2.6. and haue their conuersation in heauen, Philip. 3.20. that is to say, as worldly men are continually occupied in their mindes, and in all their labours about earthly things: so
faithfull haue their mindes and cogitations set on heauenly things. And so Paul admonisheth vs to doe, Colos. 3.1.2.
 Quest. Doth the scripture anywhere speake as you doe, and call the Church the kingdome of God, or of Christ, or of heauen.
Ans.The church called the kingdome of heauen. It is a great honor which the Lord giueth to the Church of the Iewes, Exod. 19.6. calling it a kingdome of priestes, an holy nation, which Peter applieth to vs, 1. Pet. 2.9. and Iohn saith we are kings and priests, Apoc. 1.6. But the Church is plainly called a kingdom in Daniel, Chap. 2.44 and 7.18. and the kingdome of heauen often in the gospel, as Mat, 11.11. the least in the kingdom of heauen is greater then Iohn Baptist. And the kingdome of heauen is like to a man which sowed good seed in his ground, Mat. 13.24. the kingdom of heauen is like to a draw net, Mat. 13.47. the kingdome of heauen shal be likned to ten virgins, Ma. 25.1. the faithful are called the children of the kingdome, Mat. 13.38.
 Quest. Now that you haue shewed that Christ is a king, and hath a kingdom, and that the Church is his kingdom: let me heare also how he ruleth and gouerneth his kingdome.
Ans.The church ruled by the word of God. Christ sitting at the right hand of God, ruleth in the middest of his enemies, Ps. 110.2. that though the world rage against him and
his Church or kingdom, more then euer it did against Dauids kingdom, yet he stil preuaileth against them, and defendeth his Church, for he shall crush his enemies with a rod of yron, and breake them in peeces like a potters vessell, Psal. 2.9. Apoc. 19.15. he shall wound kings in the day of his wrath, and shall iudge among the heathen, and fill all with dead bodies, and smite the head ouer diuers countries, Ps. 110.5. Apoc. 14.14.20. But in his owne Church or kingdome he hath ruled, doth, and will rule by the scepter of his word, and by the guidance of his holy spirit to conduct the elect safely through the wildernesse of this world into the land of euerlasting life. And thus Christ God and man doth and must raigne till he haue put all his enemies vnder his feet. 1. Cor. 15.24.
 Quest. How doth Christ rule his Church, which is his kingdom by the scepter of his word?
Ans. As earthly kings rule the kingdoms by good lawes established, by magistrates to execute these lawes and keepe the common people in peace and quietnes, and by prouiding for things necessary at all seasons: so Christ gouerneth his church and kingdome by his lawes which are expressed in his word, and by such persons as he hath ordained to rule his church vnder him and he himselfe by his prouidence watcheth ouer his church that nothing is wanting
to them that leade a godly life.
 Quest. Needeth not the Church then other lawes, as the Popes canon law, as it is called to gouerne his Church?
Ans. No. For the holy scriptures giuen by inspiration of God, are sufficient as Paul saith, 2. Tim. 3.16.17. And we are forbidden either to adde any thing to the word, or to take any thing from it, Deut. 4.2. Prou. 30.6. Apoc. 22.18.
 Quest. Then it is your meaning that all the Church be subiect to the lawes of God expressed in his word.
Ans. As kinges will not suffer, neither it is meete they should suffer any of their subiects to be gouerned by the lawes of a forrein prince or king: so Christ wil not abide that his church should be gouerned by any mans lawes, but onely by his own word. And if any man wil not be obedient to his lawes, heare what he himselfe saith, Luk. 19.27. Those mine enemies which would not that I should reigne ouer them, bring hither, and stay them before me
 Quest. What say you to the lawes of Christian magistrates, is not the Church gouerned by them?
Ans.(...). Christian magistrates make no newe lawes for the gouernment of Christes church, but by their authoritie and by their lawes is the worde of GOD defended,
and spredde abroade, and men are commanded to obey God, so that the Lawes of magistrates doe establish and countenance, the lawes of God, that wicked men doe not at their pleasure contemne the Lawes of God.
 Quest. VVhat vse do you now make of this doctrine, that Christ is our king, and that the Church is his kingdome?
Ans. First as Christ hath triumphed and doth triumph,
The vse of this doctrine. so shall we triumph ouer Sathan, sinne, death, and hel, Rom. 6.14. and 1. Iohn. 2.13. and 4.4.
 Secondly, as Christ was consecrated Prince of our saluation through affliction, so must we also suffer with him that we may be glorified with him Rom. 8.17. Coloss. 1.24. and 2. Tim. 2.12.
 Thirdly, our kingdome and citie which we looke for, is neither of this world nor in this world Heb. 13.14. but we are strangers and Pylgrimes here in this world and daily through patience looke for a citie hauing a foundation, whose builder and maker is God Heb. 11.10. 
 Fourthly, all they that are Christs disciples indeede, they haue alreadie renounced this present euill world, and while they continue here on earth as strangers, solong they vse this world as though they vsed it not 1. Cor.
7.31.
 Fiftly, they are blessed and thrise happie that liue in such a kingdome, in Christs kingdom, and vnder such a king. Blessed are the people that be so, yea blessed are the people, whose God is the Lord Psal. 144.15. for when Christ commeth to Iudgement, they shall meete him in the ayer; and so euer be with the Lord 1. Thes. 4.17.
 Quest. Hitherto you haue spoken of the Father and of the sonne, I pray you proceede, and let me heare somwhat of the holy Ghost?
Ans.The effects of the holy Ghost. I will only shew you some of the effectes of the holy Ghost, which are many and comfortable,  as for example: First, when we were by nature the children of wrath and our bodies no better then swinsties for diuels to dwell in, and we were ruled by the diuel Ephes. 2.2. then as the Lord outwardly called vs by the ministers of his word to resigne vp that our filthy house and harbor of vncleane spirits, and to make our bodies holy temples for Gods spirit to dwell in, the holy Ghost inwardly worketh vpon our soules to breede in vs a loathing of the diuel and of his workes, and a loue of God and of his graces.
 Secondly, the holy Ghost that beginneth his first motion in vs, and stirreth vs vp to a
desire of God and of his graces, doeth also goe forward, illuminateth our blind and darke vnderstanding, mollifieth our harde heartes, reformeth our froward wils, and so regenerateth vs and maketh vs new creatures cleane vessels, holy tabernacles, and commeth and dwelleth in vs, hauing before dispossessed the Diuel, and driuen him out of vs.
 Thirdly, the holy Ghost being now com vnto vs, and hauing taken vp his lodging in vs (1. Cor. 6.16.) he assisteth vs to keepe out the diuel that faine would reenter and possesse vs againe Math. 12.43.44. and worketh in vs euery good grace which we haue.
 Quest. What be those graces which he worketh in vs?
Ans. Whereas the father sheweth al things to the son, Iohn. 5.20. and the son declareth to vs whatsoeuer he hath heard of the Father Iohn. 15.15. the holy Ghost openeth our eares to heare, and enlargeth our heartes to beleeue the glad tidings of saluation 1. Cor. 2.10. Also the same spirit doth strengthen vs in our grieuous temptations. For if Sathan suggest into our mindes our former wretchednes when he possessed vs, the holy Ghost will tel our consciences that we are washed,
and sanctified, 1. Cor. 6.11. Tit. 3.4. And if the Diuel suggest to vs our sinnes committed since we were purged, the holy Ghost will tel our consciences that there is no condemnation to them that are in Christ Iesus, and walke not according to the flesh, but according to the spirit Rom. 8.1. that though in respect of our infirmities we doe the thing we would not, and cry out with Paul, who shall deliuer me fro^ this body of death, Rom. 7.24. yet because it is not we, but sin that dweleth in vs, Rom. 7.17. we may likewise reioyce with Paul. and say, I thanke God through Iesus Christ our Lord. Againe if we be in distresse of bodie or soule or both, that we know not which way to turne vs, or what to say, then the holy Ghost helpeth our infirmities, and maketh request for vs according to the will of God with sighs which cannot be expressed Rom. 8.26. and if we be persecuted and brought before rulers for the testimonie of Iesus, this our comforter will at that instant put into our mindes what to answere Luk. 12.11.12. Math: 10.19. finally there is no grace of God in any faithfull Christian, but it is this holy Ghost, this comforter, that worketh the same in them, and leadeth them into all righteousnes Psal. 143.10. This holy Ghost opened the mouthes of the Apostles
to speake the wonderfull things of God Act. 2.4. And gaue such wisdom to Steuen as al his aduersaries were not able to resist Act. 6.10. and emboldened so many martyres that no distres no death could mak them shrink from the Lorde Iesus Christ: and as the Apostle witnesseth, there are greate varietie and diuersitie of giftes, so he saith it is one and the same spirit that distributeth them to euery man seuerally as he will. 1. Cor. 12.1. etc.
And to note one thing more, which I had all most forgotten, because we are strangers in this world, and walke by faith and not by sight (1. Cor. 5.7:) the holy Ghost is the earnest of our inheritance, which hereafter we shall haue in heauen 2. Cor. 1.22. and. 5.5. 
 Quest. What profit or vse redoundeth to vs of this doctrine?
Ans. First,
Hatred of sinne. it bringeth to remembrance our former state and miserie, to make vs to loath sinne as the poison of our soules. And they that consider deepely of it wilbe as loth to commit sinne, or keepe companie with notorious sinners, as weake stomaked men, or daintie dames are loath to come nere any stinking carion or filthy puddle.
Ioy in the holy Ghost.
Secondly, it will make the true beleeuers so to reioyce in God, and in the blessed state
of their calling to a better and more glorious life, that nothing can take their ioy from them,
Good workes. or make them despaire, Rom. 8.35.
 Thirdly, it will breede newenesse of life, and bring foorth many good workes as frutes of faith, to the glorie of God, and the good of others, and the comfort of their owne conscience. Heb. 12.1.2.
 Fourthly,
Peace of conscience it will bring peace of conscience and certainty of saluation to them that truelie beleeue and are regenerate.
 Quest. Now that you haue spoken of the first article of faith,
The seco^d article of faith. that we must beleeue that God is, I pray you goe forward and declare the other article, that we must beleeue that God is a rewarder of them that seeke him. For these two articles you set downe before in answering my sixt question. And first I would knowe who those be that seeke God.
Ans. Those whome God first sought, and found,
Who seeke God and called, and brought to himselfe, when before they were gone astray with the rest of all Adams posteririe.
 Quest. Doe none seeke after God before he seeke, and finde, and call them?
Ans.God first seeketh man. No, none, no more then the malefactor and the murderer seeketh for the Iudge. For Adam so sone as he had sinned, ranne away and hid himselfe among the bushes or
behind a tree from the presence of GOD Gen 3.8. And so doe all sinners Apoc. 6.15. they dare not abide the Presence of God the iust Iudge against whom they haue sinned. Abraham was an Idolater as his parents were Iosua 24.2. and sought not God, but God first sought him, and called him Gen. 12.1.2. etc.
 Quest. Doe you then make this a generall lesson, and true in all men?
Ans. Yea, for Christ saith none can come to me except the father draw him Iohn. 6.37.44.45. And in an other place Iohn saith, Herein is loue, not that we loued God, but that he loued vs Iohn. 4.10. and a little after Vers. 19. We loue him because he loued vs first. Hereof it commeth that some men giue heede to the word of God when it is preached, and loue it, and follow it, whereas others care not for it, but followe after pleasures and pastimes and vanities. 1. Iohn. 4.6.
 Quest. Seeing then none come to GOD but whome he seeketh and draweth to him, I pray you what is the reward that he giueth them, that seeke him.
The reward of them that seek God.
Ans. The same reward which of his mercie and grace he promised, when he first sought them and called them.
Quest. VVhat is that reward he promised?

Ans. He promised to be their God, and the God of their posteritie, that is, to giue them and their posteritie after them, all things necessarie for this life and for the life to come, as it appeareth when he called Abraham Gen. 12.1: etc. and Gen. 17.1. etc. read Psal. 24.5. and 34.9. and 1. Tim. 4.8. Heb. 11.9.10.
 Quest. What be the promises of this life?
Ans. Both earthly and heauenly.
Quest.
Earthly blessings. What be the earthly promises?
A. Those which are mentioned Leuit. 26. fro^ the third Vers. to the 14. Verse, and Deut. 28. from the beginning to vers. 15. And Exod. 23.25. Psal. 128. and in many other places. And those which the Israelites enioyed when the obeyed the voice of the Lord, as in the dayes of Salomon 1. King. 10.27. in the dayes of Asa 2. Chro. 14.6. and. 15.15. in the dayes of Iehosophat 2. Chro. 17.5. in the dayes Ioash 2. Chro. 23.21. and. 2. King. 11.20. in the dayes of Vzziah. 2. Chro. 26.5.8.15. And in the dayes of Hezekiah. 2. King. 18.7. and 2. Chro. 31.5.10. Reade Iereme. 31.12. Malach. 3.10.
 Quest. What be the heauenly blessings which God promiseth in this life?
Ans. They are many and greate, and to name some few particulars, he giueth them;

 First, peace of conscience betweene God and them, Rom. 5.1.
Heauenly blessing in this life. which is more worth then the Gold of Ophir. He giueth them his holy spirit to conduct them the right way to heauen, to be their comforter in all aduersities, and the pledge of their inheritance till they come to take possession of it themselues:
 Secondly, he grafteth them into the body of Iesus Christ, so that they are members of his bodie, they are of his flesh and of his bones, Ephes. 5.30. and as the branches receiue life and norishment from the vine: so in that they now liue in the flesh, they liue by the faith in the sonne of God, who loued them and gaue himselfe for them, Galat. 2.20. whereby they are made partakers of the godly nature, 2. Pet. 1.4. in that they are in some measure renewed and restored to the image of God, wherein they were first created in Adam, and so haue fellowship with the father and with the sonne, 1. Iohn. 1.3.
 Thirdly, God hath so vnited and conioyned all the faithfull together into one bodie, that they haue one head Iesus Christ, one spirit, one faith, one bapaisme, one God, and Father of all, which is aboue all, and through all and in them all, Ephes. 4.4.5.6. and therefore they mourne together as did Daniel, Chap. 9.3. and 10.2.3. Ezra, Chap. 9. Nehemiah,
Chap. 1.4. the prophets and others. Also they reioyce together, Rom. 12.15. And heere is the catholike Church, and communion of saintes, whose sinnes are forgiuen in Iesus Christ.
 Quest. What be the blessings which God hath promised them after this life is ended?
Ans. The Apostle declareth it in one word, Coloss.
The blessings of the life to come. 3.4. When Christ which is our life shall appeare, then shall we also appeare with him in glorie. For when the sonne of man shall come with power and greate glory to the iudgement of the worlde, and all his holy Angels with him, Math. 24.30. and 25.31. then shall the dead be raised vp. 1. Thes. 4.16. Apo. 20.12.13. and all shall appeare before the tribunall seat of Christ, Rom. 14.10. and 2. Cor. 5.10. and we that beleeue in him shalbe taken vp into the cloudes, to meete the Lord in the aire and so shall we euer be with the Lord, 1. Thes. 4.17. Apoc. 21. and 22. where shalbe fulnesse of ioy for euermore, Psal. 16.11. Whereas the wicked ones and the vnbeleeuers shalbe punished with euerlasting perdition, from the presence of the Lord, and from the glory of his power, 2. Thes. 1.9.
 Quest. And is this the reward which God giueth them that seeke him?
Ans. You see the scripture sheweth that it is.
And seeing it is of the meere mercy of God that calleth and seeketh vp men that are vnworthy to come before him, and affraid of his presence; it is manifest that the reward promised is of the meere mercy of God. For as the sonne can deserue nothing at his fathers hands, because whatsoeuer he can do it is but his dudy: so sinfull man can deserue nothing at the handes of God, but when he hath done all he can, he must say, as Christ teacheth vs, Luk. 17.10. we are vnprofitable seruants.
 Quest. Thus farre you haue spoken of faith,
Of the sacraments. and of two speciall and generall articles of faith: now go forward I pray you and speake of the sacraments which you said before in the beginning of the second part, were annexed vnto faith.
Ans.Three things requisite to make a sacrament. The sacraments are as it were seales annexed to the couenant of God for to confirme our faith in that which God promiseth. And there are three things requisite in a sacrament.
Quest. What be those three things? 
Ans.1. A spiritual grace. First there must be a spirituall and a heauenly thing promised by God. For where God promiseth nothing,  there can be no outward signe or element, no more then a seale set to a blanke. And when God promiseth earthly things which are subiect to our senses, then our senses are sufficient witnesses to perswade our mindes. But when the Lord promiseth
spirituall and heauenly things, which our senses cannot reach vnto, then we haue need, and the Lord hauing compassion on our infirmities, helpeth our weaknesse, and by conuenient sensible things, setteth before our senses spirituall and heauenly thinges.
First therefore it is requisite that to make a sacrament there be some speciall grace promised, and that by God himselfe. For no man hath spirituall graces in his power to promise them to whom he will.
 Secondly,
2. A sensible thing there must be some outward and sensible thing that may liuely represent vnto vs, and set before our senses that heauenly grace which is promised; that our outwarde senses perceiuing it, may conueygh the truth and certenty thereof vnto our mindes. For as light commeth into the house at the windows, so al the knowledge and vnderstanding which we haue, commeth into our mindes at the windowes of our outward senses, and specially in at our eares and at our eies.
 Thirdly, the Lord himselfe must both chuse out that sensible thing which shall represent the spirituall grace,
The institution of God. and also by his own word and institution ordaine it, and all the manner of it, to that end and purpose. For as man cannot make a heauenly promise, because heauenly thinges are not in his power to giue them to
whom he will: so man may not without very great sinne presume to ordaine any outwarde thing to represent a heauenly thing, but this must be done by the Lord onely.
 Quest. I vnderstand these three thinges very well, I pray you now let me see what you call a sacrament, and how you define it?
Ans.Definition of a sacrament. A sacrament is a sensible thing representing a spirituall grace, instituted of God to confirme our faith and assure our consciences in the spirituall grace which the Lord hath promised.
 Quest. Before you called a sacrament a seale; is it no seale now?
Ans. I said so, and I haue not yet denied it, for when I said it was a seale,
A sacrament is a seale. I vsed a metaphoricall speech, because it is fitly compared to a seale. For as a seale set to the conditions that are agreed vpon by both parties, doth ratifie and confirme the trueth of them for both parties, and especially to him, to whom the promise is made: so a sensible thing instituted of God doth confirme the certenty of the spirituall grace which God hath promised, and specially to man to whom it is promised. Wherefore as the holy Ghost speaketh of the oath of God, Heb. 6.17. so may I in some sort say of a sacrament, that God willing more abundantly to shew vnto the heires of promise the
stablenes of his counsell (or of his promise,) bound himselfe by his seale or sacrament, that by two immutable things) the word or promise, and the sacrament of God) wherein it is vnpossible that God should lie, we might haue strong consolation.
 Quest. How doth a sensible thing instituted of God to be a sacrament, differ from it selfe before it be instituted, or from an other thing which is of the same kind, but not yet ordained of God for that purpose?
Ans. As wax put to a writing and sealed differeth from that it was before, and from other wax, which is not vsed for a seale: so doth the sensible thing in the sacrament differ from it selfe as it was before, and from other thinges of the same kinde, as for example: Water when it is ordained by the institution of God for baptisme, remaineth water stil, as wax in the seale is still wax; but in respect of the vse it is put to by Gods ordinance, it differeth from that it was before, and from other common water. The same may be said of the bread and wine in the Lords supper.
 Quest. Whose seale, or signes, or signe is the sensible thing in the sacrament, when it is so ordined of God to be a sacrament, and to represent a spiritual grace? is it the seal of God that promiseth spiritual grace? or is it the seale of the faithfull, to whom the spirituall grace is promised?

Ans.The sacrament is the seale both of God and ma^. Though there be no question but that it is the seale of God; yet it shall not be a misse so say it is the seale of the faithfull also. For as the Lord of mercy promiseth spirituall blessings, and writeth them downe in the bible, and thereto for our infirmities sake putteth his seale, the sacrament to confirme our faith, and this the Lord doth when he instituteth the sacrament: soon the other part ma^ promiseth his faith and his obedience, and likewise setteth thereto his seale by receiuing of the sacrament. For when man receiueth the sacrament, he doth for his part as it were set to his seale and bindeth himselfe by a further testimonie then his word was, to beleeue and to obey God. Wherefore Paul saith, Coloss. 2.14. that the Iewes by vsing the ceremonies of the olde lawe (which were as sacraments) did as it were subscribe their hands and set to their seales that they were sinfull and vncleane. And in like maner euery faithfull man by receiuing of the sacrament, subscribeth and setteth to his seale that he will performe that which he promised for his part. Againe as Christ saith, Iohn, 3, 33. that he which receiueth his testimonie that God is true: so he that receiueth the sacrament setteth to his seale that God is true and will certainly performe the spirituall grace which he promiseth, and setteth to his seale
that he will performe his promise which he hath made to God.
 Quest. What is the spirituall grace which God hath promised?
Ans.The spiritual grace that is promised. Where as al mankind sinned in Adam, and by reason of sinne was subiect to Gods eternall curse and to condemnation, Rom. 5.12. the Lord (that hath mercy on whome he will, Exod. 33.19.) of his vnspeakable mercy called vpon some, as he did vpon Abraha^, and promised him; first forgiuenes of his sins, and a celestial inherita^ce in the kingdom of heaue^ as we read Gen. 12.1.2, etc. for it appeareth, Heb. 11.10. that both God promised, and Abraha^ by faith hoped for the kingdom of heaue^. Secondly, God (who is not foolishly pitiful to forgiue me^ their sins contrary to iustice, for Gods iustice requireth the death of a sinner, promised also the meanes whereby Abraham should haue his sins pardoned and yet with iustice) and wherby he should be made righteous, and co^sequently an inheritor of the kingdom of heauen.
 Q. It semeth to me that you speak of two promises first of forgiuenes of sins and of eternal life, which ye ioine together; and seco^dly of the means wherby sins are forgiuen, and happines is purchased.
Ans. I wold make the promise, that is, the grace promised, to be but one grace or blessing: but because it is so ample of it self, and for our better
conceiuing of it, my desire is to lay open the seuerall branches of it. And for that cause haue I vsed moe wordes, as for example; Because all men are sinners Eccle. 7.31. and sinners shall not stand before God Ps. 5.5. nor inherit the kingdome of God, 1. Cor. 6.9. Therefore it is necessarie that our sinnes be perdonned and doone away, that we may be acceptable to God and capable of the kingdome of heauen. And because God hath giuen this generall law, Gen. 2.17. That whensoeuer man sinned, he should certainly die the death: and to satisfie his owne iustice gaue his only begotten sonne to take our nature of the virgin Mary and be man as we are in all things (sinne only except Heb. 4.15. and laid vpon him the iniquitie of vs all, Esai. 53.6. That is the punishment which was due to vs for our sinnes. And because Christ hath fulfilled the whole law for vs, and imputeth his righteousnes to vs that beleue in him, therefore I comprehend vnder that spirituall grace, the meanes which God ordeined for our saluation and redemption. If I could in fewer words comprehend the spirituall grace, which I said was the first of the three things that make a sacrament, I would very gladly doe it. But I had rather vse many words then not declare
the thing itselfe.
Quest. What is the outward and sensible thing, that representeth that spirituall grace? It may be that the heauenly grace that is promised, will better appeare in the visible thing.
Ans.Of the outward element. Because God hath ordayned moe sacraments then one, I must necessarily speake first of the number of sacraments, and then orderly of each sensible signe which representeth the spirituall promise; and in speaking of them seuerally, we shall see the institution also which is the third thing required to make a sacrament.
 Quest. How manie sacraments doe you say there are?
Ans.Two sacraments. There are onely two sacraments: the first is baptisme; the second is the Lords supper.
 Quest. It may be then that there are two promises, as I saide before, and so now two sacraments according to those promises. Is it not so?
Ans. No, there is but one promise consisting of diuers and specially of two braunches. And the visible signe in either of these two sacraments, representeth the whole promise. If any man will say that baptisme representeth more fully the former braunch of the promised
grace; and the Lords supper, the latter, I will not greatly contende.
 Quest. What is the visible thing in baptisme, which representeth the spirituall grace?
Of baptisme
Ans. It is water, as all men may see.
 Quest. Al men in deede see it is water which is vsed in baptisme. But did God euer make choyse of water to be the sensible element in the sacrament of baptisme? or did he at any time institute and commaund this sacrament to be ministred in water?
Ans.The signe in baptis. me is water. Iohn the baptist administred this sacrament in water Mark. 1. Math. 3. and it may appeare Luke. 1.8. and 3.2. etc. That he had an expresse commaundement for all that he did, though euery thing be not particularly set down in the word. And Christ in plain words commanded this sacrament to be ministred in water, Math. 28.19. when he said Baptizing them in the name etc.
 Quest. Iohn in deede baptized in water: but that Christ Math. 28.19. commanded this sacrament to be ministred in vvater, or wine, or oyle or sand, or any other thing, I cannot perceiue.
Ans. If this word, Baptizing, had bene translated by anie english word, you should haue seene it: for the word signifieth washing, and it might haue beene translated
washing them etc. And so the word is translated Mark. 7.4. Where it is saide, that the pharisies when they come from the market except they wash, they eate not. Thus the word is also expounded, Act. 22.16. Arise and be baptized, and wash away thy sinnes. For when he had saide arise and be baptized, he interpreteth in the next word the signification and meaning of this word baptized and, saith wash away etc. Wherefore you may hereby see that Christ commaunded water for the sensible signe in baptisme. For it is and alwayes hath beene the common custome to washe in water.
 Quest. I Pray you shew me then how water in baptisme representeth the spirituall grace which is promised.
The signe representeth the grace.
Ans. Before I laide out the spirituall promise, or the promised grace, specially in two branches whereof the one was forgiuenes of sinnes and eternall life; the other was the meanes whereby this blessednes shoulde be performed, or if you please so to take it, the author of this happines, which is Christ Iesus crucified for our saluation. Now, to answere you directly, when our bodies are washed with water, in this sacrament of baptisme, it teacheth vs that so also we, euen our bobies and soules are washed from sinne, and
that of vncleane, we are become cleane, and that of deade men in sinnes and trespasses, we are made aliue to God; and that this commeth by the meanes of Iesus Christ, who suffered death and shed his blood vpon the crosse for our redemption.
Quest. I pray you repeat this againe. 
Ans. God promised vnto vs the forgiuenes of our sinnes, he promised also to giue vs eter nall life, and all this by the death of Iesus Christ our Lord. This promise is alreadie performed, Christ is deade for vs, our sinnes are doone away and we are made partakers of eternall life, so much as may be in this present life. Now in baptisme, the water washing away the filthines of our bodies, as our senses are witnesses, doth represent the washing away the filthines of our sinnes, and teacheth vs that it is the blod of Christ, which purgeth our consciences from deade works to serue the liuing God.
Quest. Because you saide afore that the sacrament is also the seale of man, I pray you shew me how man setteth to his seale to confirm his promise in this sacrament.
Man receiuing the sacrament bindeth himselfe to perform his promi^
Ans. When man is called by the word of God to hope of saluation by Iesus Christ, and when man ioyfully receiuing and accepting of this grace offred, entereth into Gods
couenant, then man, the Lord so requiring, doeth promise to forsake the flesh, the world, and the Diuel, to beleeue in God, and to obey his commaundements. And when he receiueth baptisme vpon the former conditions, he goes into the water, and there is vnder the water, as if he were gone out of this world, and had forsaken this world, then he comes vp againe as a new borne man to serue God in newnes of life. And this verie action is as it were a seale, or the setting to of his seale, to testifie that he beleeues the promise of God, else he would neuer do so, and it testifieth his obedience in that he so receiueth this sacrament as God commandeth him.
 Quest. By whome ought this sacrament to be administred?
Ans.Baptisme must be ministred by the ministers of the word. By the ministers of the word, for this office was first committed to Iohn Baptist, secondly to the Apostles Math 28.19. and consequently to all the ministers of the word so that others may no more lawfully chaleng authoritie to baptise then to preach. Also it is a part of the ministry, and when the sacrament of baptisme is administred, then ought the couenant to be laide open and declared. For as men will not set their seales to a blanke not yet to a paper wherein the conditions are
written, except they first heare or reade the conditions themselues: so is it not meete that baptisme, the seale of the couenant betwen God and man be administred, except the couenant and the condicions of the couenant be first manifested that the church may see the ministers haue the warrant of the word for that they doe, and so all may be edified. Seeing then the couenant is to be declared before the sacrament is to be administred, it is not for others, that haue no commission to expound the couenant, to enterprise to minister the sacrament.
 Quest. To whome is baptisme to be ministred vnto?
To those which haue made a couenant with God, that is, to those,
Baptisme ministred to them only that are in the couenant. to whome God is gratious and hath promised that spiritual grace, whereof I spake before.
Quest. How shall we know who those be?
Ans. Those which make profession of the couenant of God, and of their faith.
Who are in Gods couenant. For God hath called a few here on earth into his couenant, and ioyned them together in a holy fellowship, and committed to them his oracles, his word, the tables of the couenant, the old and the new testament. And al they whome God doth call and offer, grace vnto, when they accept of that grace
offred, then they come into the Church, and professe their faith and their couenant with God, and craue to haue their names enrowled and regestred in the church, which is the kingdome of Christ, and so are made partakers of the manifould graces of God which are distributed in the Church by the ministers, which are appointed to be stewards of the manyfould mysteries of GOD 1. Cor. 4.1. And thus shall you easilie know them.
 Quest. Are no other entred into Gods couenant, but those that outwardly professe it?
Ans. None to mans knowledge, but they and their children.
Quest.
Children of the faith ful are in the comenant. Are the children of the faithfull in Gods couenant?
Ans. Yea they are in the couenant. For God sayth Gen. 17.7. to Abraham, and so to all the faithful that he will be their God and the god of their posteritie, and that his couenant shalbe aswell with their posteritie as with them.
 Quest. May all the children of the faithful be baptised in their infancie, because they are the children of the faithfull, and therefore in the couenant?
Ans. Yea, that is reason sufficient, and we neede no more. And for this cause the Israelits
circumcised their men children the eight day after their birth,
Children of the faithfull baptised. and Christians haue alwaies beene accustomed to baptise their children in their infancie.
Quest. Wherefore then serue God-fathers and God-mothers? or what is the reason why there are any? for if your former wordes be true, and your reasons good, I thinke there needs none. Onely it is sufficient to baptise them because they are the children of the faithfull.
Ans. I suppose the Church appointeth not God-fathers and Godmothers for any necessity,
Of God fathers. as though children could not be baptised truely and fully without them, but for order, for edification, or for some other good cause, as that if the parentes die before the children come to know the misteries of baptisme and of saluation, then these Godfathers and God-mothers may be in steede of parents and bring vp the children in the feare of God. Or if at any time those children be vpon some occasion doubted of, whether they be bapsed or not, then God-fathers and God-mothers may giue in their euidence, and testifie that they are baptised.
 Quest. When or vpon what occasion were they first in the Church? For I thinke the children of the Iewes had none when they were circumcised, nor the children of the faithfull when they
were baptised in the daies of Christ, of the Apostles, nor in the first age of the Christian Church.
Ans. I confesse freely that I knowe not certainly the first original cause and occasion, neuerthelesse because you moue this question I will shewe you so much as I knowe, and leaue it to the learned to iudge of. There seeme to me to be two causes whence this custome may come into the Church, but of whether of them twaine, or of neither of them, but rather of some other I will not determine. I will onely reporte them, and so leaue them to the consideration of the godly and the wise.
 The first cause is commonly in euerie mans mouth, and it is this: In former times of the primitiue Church when infidels were conuerted to the faith of Christ, they came into the congregation, and openly renounced the flesh, the worlde, and the diuell, then made confession of their faith in GOD, and promised obedience to the commaundementes of God, and so finally were baptised, as diuers auncient writers doe recorde. Nowe some men are of opinion, that from this custome was taken this order in the Church, that the children of the faithfull shoulde haue Godfathers and
Godmothers to answere for them when they were baptised, because they could not aunswere for themselues. Whether it were Hyginus of Rome that first brought vp this order about the yeare of Christ 140. as Platina and others write, or some other, it is not greatly materiall. The reasons which moued the first authors to ordaine this custome, as Gratian the marrer of the popes lawes (Auent. lib. 6.) hath set them downe C. 13. Q. 1. C. quod autem, etc. and de consecratione, dist. 4. in many Chapters, I will not at this present rehearse, but referre my selfe and the reader to the iudgement of M. Bucer in his censure vpon this question. For he was a man that loued our nation, and came out of Germanie to helpe vs, and though he builded vs not a synagogue, yet he commended to King Edward the sixt, in his bookes de regno Christi the platforme of the spirituall house of God, and how it ought to be builded.
 The second cause I gather by coniecture out of the fifth counsell of Carthage, Chap. 6. and it is this. About Carthage and specially further westward in that continent among the Moriscos or Moores, it often happened through hostile inuasions and troubles of the barbarous people, that many
christians were taken captiues, and some of them being young children. But when the Christians long after redeemed such as were taken captiues in their infancie, there grew a question, whether those were baptised before they were caried captiues or not. At Carthage about the yeare of Christe, 430. there were 73. learned men, Aurelius of Carthage being a chiefe man among them, assembled in a councell to determine of the causes of the Church and among other thinges they consulted of this also, what was to be saide or done touching those of whome there was no certentie whether they were baptised or no. This question they handled the rather, because the christians among the Moores sent their messengers to Carthage for counsell in that case. Heereon I comecture that the worthy fathers of the Church to preuent such doubtes afrerward, ordained that there shoulde be speciall witnesses at the baptisme of euery christians childe, which thing if they did, I suppose it was a very laudable decree, though at this day, the Lord be praised, there is no such cause, except among them of Hungaria, Austria, Slauonia and others bordering vpon the Turkes dominions, or vpon some other insidell nation.

 Quest. Then you thinke it is not meete to haue any witnesses at this day amongs vs when our children are baptised.
Ans. Not so. For though I will not certainely affirme what was the very cause of the first beginning of this custome, yet there may bee good causes rendered why there shoulde be. Also doe you not see that all reformed Churches obserue it as a conuenient order? And the Church of England doth ordaine it, the authority whereof must be obserued.
 Quest. Then I will demaunde no more of you concerning this matter. But seeing Pelagians long since. and Anabaptistes at this day denie that the children of the faithfull shoulde be baptised before they come to vnderstanding, and make confession of their owne faith; I woulde gladly heare some other reason why they shoulde be baptised in their infancie.
Ans.Baptisme of children. The reason I rendered before may be sufficient, and I will repeate it againe thus. With whomsoeuer God hath made a couenant, they ought to haue the sacrament of the couenant. But God hath made a couenant with the children of the faithfull, Gen. 17.7. Therefore they ought to haue the sacrament of the couenant which
is baptisme. Secondly the children of the faithfull belong to the kingdome of heauen, Math. 19.14. and therefore ought to be baptised. Thirdly if the reasons seeme too too general in that manner I haue deliuered them (for I confesse a wrangling sophister may take exception against them) I will reason as Peter doth Act. 10.47. Can any man forbid water, etc. that is, those which haue receiued the holy Ghost as well as we ought to be baptised. But children of the faithfull haue receiued the holy Ghost. This I prooue first because they are in Gods couenant, Gen, 17.7. Secondly because they are holy (that is to say, are sanctified, and haue receiued the holy Ghost) if but one of their parentes be faithful 1. Cor. 7.14. and much more when both their parents are faithfull. Thirdly, because that if the first fruites be holy, so is the whole lumpe also: and if the roote be holy, so are the branches also, Rom. 11.16. And therefore I conclude that the children of the faithfull ought to be baptised.
 Quest. Why doe we not nowe baptise our infantes the eight day after their birth, as the Iewes did circumcise their children?
Ans.Baptisme ministred the eight (...) The Iewes were bound to the obseruation of the ceremonial, law which taught them that a woman was vncleane seuen daies
after she was deliuered of a man childe, and the child proceeding from her was for those seauen daies counted vncleane also, and therfore could not be circumcised before the eight day, as you may read, Leuit, 12.1.2.3. But the ceremoniall law was abolished at Christs comming, and bindeth nor vs to obeserue it. Wherefore we are rather to learne this lesson from thence, that as the children of the Iewes were circumcised so soone as coulde be after their birth, and that was the eyght daye, which they might not pretermitte, and so were straitely charged to circumcise their children that day, without any delay: so the children of the faithfull ought to be baptised so soone as conueniently may be after they are borne, and specially the next Lords day after, if there be not conuenient oportunity sooner.
 Quest. And may not baptisme be deferred for many daies, or for a moneth, or longer?
Ans.Baptisme not to be deferred. The children of the Iewes were not deferred one day, but so soone as possibly it might be done, which was the eyght day, so soone were they circumcised by the expresse commaundement of the Lorde, Genesis. 17.12.14. And I knowe no priuiledge graunted to vs vnder the gospell.

 Quest. Some make great haste, and if the childe be weake baptise it at home by the midwife: and others stay very long till their friendes be come from farre, and that is sometime a moneth, sometimes two monethes, or longer, what thinke you of that?
Ans. I can say nothing to it, because I know no warrant out of the word of God for eyther of them both. But because they shalbe iudged by the word, Ioh. 12.48. therfore I wish all men to be carefull what they doe in so weightie a cause, and that they dally not with God.
 Quest. Doe not infantes goe to hell, if they die vnbaptised?
Ans. God forbid that we should eyther speake or thinke so,
Contempt or neglect of the sacrament, not the want depriueth men of Gods fauour. seeing the Lord neuer said so. But contrariwise the scripture witnesseth that they are in the couenant of God, and so in state of saluation, so soone as they are borne. And baptisme doth not make them Christians that were none before, but is the sacrament, the seale, the signe, the badge of them that are Christians before. As men become not seruantes to greate personages by putting on their coate with their badge, but first are receiued of some greate personage into his seruice and then after put on his coate and weare his badge
as an outward token to shew whose seruants they are. So men are first reconciled to God, receiued into his fauour, into his couenant, into his seruice, and so become Christians, then afterward doe they receiue baptisme as it were the coate, the badge and testimonie of their profession. Besides it is not the want of the sacrament that depriueth a man of Gods fauour. For the children of the Israelites were not circumcised all those fourtie yeares which they liued in the wildernes. The reason whereof was, because they were euer to remoue and iourney whensoeuer the piller of the cloud, that was their guide ascended and went forward Num. 9.18. etc. so that they were alwayes to attend vpon the cloude both night and day, not knowing when it would remoue, and therefore could not circumcise their children in the wildernes, as ye may reade Iosh. 5. Vers. 2. And the rest following to the ninth verse. And I wish you to reade the place. But it is the contemning or despising of the sacrament that depriueth men of Gods fauour, when they make no more account of it then Esau did of his birth-right, Gen. 25.32. then Ahaz did of the Lords helpe Esay. 7. and it is also the neglecting of it, when God offreth time and
oportunitie that we might haue it. And as many neglect the heareing of the word and say they can heare it when they list: so many neglect to offer their children to the Church in the Lords due time, and thinke they may haue them baptized when they will. Againe the Lord neuer saide, that whosoeuer died vncircumcised, or vnbaptised should be wiped out of the booke of life: but he hath saide, Gen. 17.12.14. That whosoeuer contemneth or carelesly neglecteth the sacrament, shalbe cut off from among his people. As if a maister should say of his seruant, if he despise my cloth, or if he will not put it on when I bid him, thrust such a fellow out at the dores, let him tary no longer in my house. Wherefore there is no danger to them that die before they can conueniently be baptized. But they had neede to take heede which neglect and pretermit the time when God doth offer it, and will tary for their friendes, as though the presence of their friendes were to be preferred before the pleasure of God. And for this cause it seemeth that God now and then shewes greate tokens of his wrath by taking out of this life lustie and strong childre^ without baptisme, because their parents neglect the time which God offered.

 Quest. Whether would you haue children baptized in the Church the congregation being assembled together, or in a priuate house?
Publique baptisme.
Ans. These matters are not to be ruled by mens desires, but by the word of God. When a childe is baptized, he is receiued into the fellowship of that congregation as a member thereof, and hath his name regestred among the Saintes. Wherefore it seemeth most requisite it should be done openly in the face of that congregation that all may take knowledge of him. Otherwise if it should be done secretly in a corner in hugger mugger, we know not who or what might creepe in the Church, which hath no interest in it. And the Churches to preuent inconueniences, doe not only appoint children to be brought into the congregation to be baptized in the presence of all, but also as if that were not enough, haue further appointed speciall witnesses for euery child that is baptized.
 Quest. One question I would aske you more, and it is this. You saide verie well afore, that in baptisme men were put vnder the water to resemble the death of Christ, and to shew they died with him, Iohn the Baptist baptized in Iordan Math. 3.6. and in Enon besides Salim, because there was much water Iohn. 3.23.
and Philip went downe into the water to bap tise the Eunuch Act. 8.38. and the custom hath beene of late yeres to put children into the water, why is not this custo^ now obserued? and why do they now only sprinkle a little water vpon the child?
Ans. That practise was holie and good, and may verie well be vsed,
Baptisme ministred by sprinkling on of water. and rather then sprinkling on of water in hote countries. But in these northeren and cold climates it might be dangerous to the young and weak infant, as perhaps it hath beene to some, and that is the cause why now water is rather sprinkled on children, then they put into the water. And least you should think this to be humane reason repugnant to the word of God, I would haue you to consider; First, that in the ould ceremoniall law there was purgation aswell by sprincling, Num. 19.9. as by washing Exod. 30.18.19. Leuit. 14.6.16.4. Secondly, that Cornelius and a great number with him were baptized in his house as it semeth Act. 10.47. Paul was baptized in the house of one Iudas of Damascus Act. 8.11 18. the keeper of the prison at Phillippi with all that belonged vnto him, were baptized in his house about midnight Act. 16.33. And these had no riuers ru^ning through their houses, as I suppose but rather had water powred or els sprinkled vpon them. Lastly consider
that in the primitue Church, when heathens conuerted to the faith, fell sick whiles they were learning their catechisme, and before they were baptized, if the sicknes grew dangerous they were baptised in their beds by sprinkling of water vpon them, as that worthie martire of Christ Capryan, a man of greate zeale, learning and iudgment in religion sheweth and approueth, Lib. 4. Epist. 7. Q.  Now I pray you shew me likewise the Lords supper, and declare what the spirituall grace is, what the outward sign, and by whom it was instiuted,
Ans. All these thinges you demaund,
Of the Lords supper. and mo also, are set downe in one place Math. 26.26. wherefore in laying open that place I shall answere all your desires.
 Quest. VVhat order will you obserue in opening that scripture?
Ans. The same which the text offreth.
 Quest. What doe you obserue out of the first words?
Ans.The time of the institution.And whiles they were eating) these wordes shew the time when this sacrament was first instituted, that is, the night before Christ suffred, at his last supper, when he and his disciples were eating the passeouer. So that when the ould sacrament of the passouer ceased, which was a representing of
Christ to come, then was the other, euen the Lords super instituted for a memoriall of his death, and to shew that he is already come. 
 Quest.
The author. What doe you note besides out of the text?
Ans. Iesus) this word sheweth the author who instituted the Lords supper, that it was God and not man, euen the Lord Iesus Christ.
Quest. What obserue you more?
Ans. Tooke the breade) in these words, and in others following,
The visible creatures. euen these, also be tooke the cup, is conteined the outward and sensible thing which Christ made choise of to represent the heauenly grace which was promised. The visible signe or sensible thing was breade and wine. The spirituall grace promised was remission of sinnes and eternall life by Iesus Christ our Lord.
 Quest. Shew me how the breade and wine represent the spiritual grace?
The comparison betwene the signe and the thing signified
Ans. You must remember that I told you before, how baptisme principally doth represent the former branch of the spirituall grace, and the Lords supper specially resembleth the latter. Wherefore as Christ was promised for our saluation and redemption, and that he should suffer death
for vs: so these sensible signes doe notablie represent the same to our senses, to assure our soules of the certentie of it. For the bread broken before our eyes, sheweth Christ was broken vpon the crosse, I meane crucified and put to death. Forotherwise there was not a bone of him broken. And the wine powred out before our eyes sheweth that Christs blood was shed for vs. Agayne as our senses tast the breade and wine, and we feele and finde comfort and norishme^t to ourbodies thereby; so our soules inwardly by faith tast of the benefits of our redemption by Iesus Christ, and our inner ma^ is cheared and comforted.
