And we reme^ber Christs death continually to our greate comfort til he come to iudgment: and thus liuelilie doe these outward signes represent the spirituall grace to vs.
Quest. What followeth in the text? 
Ans.The consecration.And when he had giuen thankes) these words are spoken both of the breade and of the wine, and the meaning of them is, that whiles they were yet eating the passeouer, in the latter end of the supper, Iesus hauing taken to him first the breade, then the wine, and hauing them in his hands or present before him, gaue thankes, that is, by prayer to God
did consecrate and institute these creatures of breade and wine seuerally to this vse, euen to be sacraments or outward signes of the promised grace. And this is the institution and consecrations as we speak co^monly. The very words of Christes prayer when he consecrated those sensible creatures of bread and wine are not expressed, and therefore the Church vseth her libertie in this prayer when this sacrament is to be ministred. 
 Quest. What followeth?
Ans. He brake it) these wordes are spoken of the breade seuerally, and the like also must be vnderstoode of the wine also seuerally, that it was powred into the cup. The meaning is plaine, that after Christ had taken to him these creatures and by prayer consecrated them to this holy vse, then he brake the breade, and powred out the wine for the disciples there present. 
 Quest.
To whom it belongeth. Proceede I pray you with the text
Ans. He gaue it to the disciples) in these words, as also in those following which are spoken of the wine, he gaue it them, he shewed to whome this sacrament is to be giuen, that is, to all the disciples of Christ, and to no other. For the sacraments belong
not to them that haue made no couenant with God.
 Quest. Doth the Lordes supper belong to all Christes disciples as baptisme doth?
Ans. Yea to all aswel as baptisme, but in due time, and after a due manner.
 Quest. What exceptions be these you make? or what difference is there, that the two sacramentes doe not appertaine to all alike?
Ans. The sacrament of baptisme is ministred to euery one that entreth into Gods couenant, and he cannot be receiued into the felowship of the saintes but by baptisme. Also baptisme is ministred but once, whereas the Lordes supper is ministred often. Wherefore as euery one in the Church is baptised at his first entrance, but with certaine conditions of renouncing the world, and of beleeuing in God, as hath beene shewed afore: so euery one after he is entred into the Church, is often made partaker of the Lordes supper but with certaine conditions.
Quest. What be those conditions? 
Ans. The Apostle, 1. Cor. 11.28. putteth this caueat or condition, that euery man trie and examine himselfe before he come to the Lordes table, whether they know what they doe, whether they vnderstand that mystery, whether they come with pure heartes
and cleane handes. Now if you see any in the Church that cannot, or will not, or doe not examine themselues, they may not be permitted to come to the Lordes table.
 Quest. Who be those that cannot or will not examine themselues?
Ans. There are diuers, as first infantes, idiots, lunatike persons, for want of discretion, and of the vse of reason cannot examine themselues, and therefore may not receiue the Lordes supper whiles they are in that state. Also there are diuers of discretion and iudgement in worldly affaires, but yet are blind and ignorant of the mysteries of saluation, and therefore cannot examine themselues nor discerne the Lordes bodie, neyther may be permitted to come to the Lordes table. Againe there are some that are able to examine themselues, but notwithstanding liue and continue in some knowen sinne and will not, or at the least doe not repent, nor satisfie the congregation whom they haue offended, and for that cause are to be kept from the Lords supper.
 Quest. What be the next wordes then in the text?
Ans.All partakers of both creatures.And said, take, eate) these wordes are spoken of the breade, and the like of the cup, drinke ye all of it, the meaning whereof
is so manifest, that there needeth no exposition. We learne heere that all were partakers both of the bread and of the winealso.
 Quest. What then be the last wordes of the text?
Ans.The exposition. The last wordes for the bread are these, this is my body, and for the cup thus, this is my blood of the new testament that is shed for many, for the remission of sinnes. In which wordes he expoundeth all that went afore, for when the disciples saw Christ extraordinarily take bread, and blesse it by prayer after an vnaccustomed manner, and the cup likewise, and giue to them commaunding them to eate that bread and drinke that cup for another purpose then for feeding of their bodies onely, as it might wel be perceiued by the whole action, they might marueile what the meaning of all that might be. Thefore Christ when he deliuered them the creatures, declared also the meaning, and said of the breade, this is my bodie, that is, this bread which I haue thus consecrated by prayer, and giuen to you commaunding you to eate it, it is the signe and sacrament of my bodie which is broken for your saluation, the same also is vnderstood of the cup.
 Quest. Is not the bread turned into flesh, and the wine into blood?

Ans.The dotage of the papisticall transubstantiatio^. No. For that were contrarie to the nature of a sacrament. I tolde you before that to make a sacrament, there must be a spirituall grace promised, and an outward sensible creature to represent that heauenly grace and the commaundement of the Lord to appoint that creature to represent the inuisible grace. Now the outward thing heere is bread and wine, the heauenly thing which is represented thereby is Christes body broken and his blood shed vpon the crosse with all the benefites of his death. But if there were any such grosse chaunging of the breade or wine, where were the creature which Christ instituted? where were the inuisible grace that should be represented? and where were the sacrament? and where were Christes institution? Moreouer all sacramentes are of one nature, but there was neuer yet so much as any doting man that dreamed at any time of the chaunge of the outward signes into the thinges represented and signified in any sacrament of the olde or newe Testament. For who euer hearde that any man saide that circumcision, or the paschall lambe, or the water in baptisme were chaunged into those thinges which they represent. Wherefore this dotage, if I ought not rather to say, blasphemie of the papists in this poynt, is more
a great deale then grosse and absurde, for it is a monstrous and horrible impietie. Thirdly, it is but the vsuall phrase of the scripture to terme the visible signe by the name of the thing signified, as circumcision is called the couenant, Gen. 17.10.11. Christ is called our passeouer, 1. Cor. 5.7. baptisme is called the fountaine of regeneration, Tit. 3.5.
 Quest.
Of the law NOwe that you haue spoken of faith and of the sacramentes, I pray you proceede to the lawe and open that also, for this order you propounded before.
Ans. After the couenaunt made betweene God and man, wherein man first professeth his faith, and then promiseth his obedience to God; the Lorde giueth his lawes and his commaundementes, that man may knowe howe and wherein to obey him. And when all Israell had promised to doe what the Lorde commaunded, Exodus. 19.5. then the Lord gaue his lawes from the toppe of mounte Sinai, Exod. 20.
 Quest. Gaue the Lorde no moe lawes but those tencommaundementes onely?
Ans. He gaue also the ciuill or politicall lawe, as it is called, and the ceremoniall lawe, but the ten commaundementes giuen
by voice from the toppe of mount Sinai out of the middest of the fire, (Deut. 5.22.) are the principall and chiefe summe of all, and abide for euer, whereas both the politicall and the ceremoniall were for the most part but temporal and serued for the morall lawe.
 Quest. What is the ciuill or politicall law? and wherefore serueth it?
Ans.The politicall law It serueth for the morall lawe to strengthen it and vphold it that it be not contemned nor broken; for the Lorde hath ordained the magistrate and giuen him ciuil authoritie ouer all persons and in all causes, that if any man of what calling soeuer doe violate the first or second table of the ten commaundements, and so offend against God or against man or against both, then the magistrate that beareth not the sworde in vaine is to punish him. And because the magistrate may not in execution of his office followe his owne affection nor other mens humors, the Lorde that inuesteth the magistrate, doth giue him the booke of the law, euen this politicall and ciuill law for his commission to tell him what and whome he shall punish, and whome he shall protect and defend. For as inferiour magistrates receiue their commission from their king and supreme gouernour, by vertue
whereof they execute their office, not declining therefrom eyther to the right hande or to the left: so kings and supreame gouernours receiue from God the great king of all the worlde their commission which they may not exceede. And the politicall lawe is the commission which God deliuereth into the hande of the magistrate that he may proceed to execute his office according vnto it. Wherfore Moses the supreme magistrate among the Israelites, gaue the same commission to the magistrates which were vnder him, that he had receiued of GOD, and charging them faithfully to execute their office, giueth them the reason, and saith, Deut. 1.17. For the iudgemente is Gods, as if he had said, looke to your duetie, and though you be inferiour iudges set vnder me, yet do nothing in my name, neither follow your own affections, for I am but vnder another, euen vnder God, and his lawes I giue you by which ye must iudge, and not any of mine own making, and what sentence you pronounce, what iudgement you giue, it is neyther in your owne name, nor in my name, but in the name and authority of GOD, and when you giue sentence, it is as if the Lord gaue sentence. Therefore take heed to your selues that ye make not the Lord
a lyar and in giuing false iudgement say, this is the will and commaundement of God, for he will not suffer his maiesty to be so foully abused, the iudgement is the Lordes. After the same manner did Ichoshaphat, charge the iudges and magistrates that were vnder him, and saide vnto them, 2. Chro. 19.6. Take heede what ye doe: For ye execute not the iudgementes of man, but of the Lorde. And as inferiour magistrates brought hard and difficult causes before Moses, when they were not able to decide them, Deut, 1.17. so if there were any cause so dfficult that Moses himselfe coulde not determine, he brought it before the Lorde to be discoursed, Leuit. 24.11.12.13.14. Numb. 9.8. and 27.5. and Deut. 1.22.23. compared with, Num. 13.2.3.
 Quest. Whether is the iudiciall lawe now abrogated and repealed since the comming of Christ?
Ans.How farre the ciuill law is a brogated. So farre as it serueth to preserue and maintaine the morall law, it remaineth and shall abide for euer. For the Gospell disableth not the magistrate, but giueth him as much power and authority as euer he had vnder the lawe. Neyther yet doth the Gospell set the magistrate at libertie to doe what he list, but would haue him
aswell now obedient to God, as euer he was vnder the law. But concerning the iudiciall and politicall law which God gaue to the Israelites, it doeth not so binde the magistrate now vnder the gospel, as before it did vnder the Law. For there are many things, in it peculiar to those times, to that nation of the Iewes, and to that land of Canaan, which now concerne not vs, neither binde the magistrate to see them executed, as deuiding of their inheritance by Lots, keeping of euery mans inheritance within the same familie and kinred, mariages of women that were inheritrixes within the same tribe, with diuers such others. Also there were diuers things in the ciuil Lawes of the Iewes; the equitie whereof only now remaineth and the verie thing it selfe according to the letter is not to be vrged, as they had diuers punishments appointed diuersly for diuers offences, which they were straitly bound vnto; but the verie same are not now to be vrged, and executed precisely according to the wordes and letters of the Law; but according to a generall equitie, that sinne be alwayes punished. Whosoeuer among the Iewes did steale an oxe or a sheepe the magistrate was bounde to make the theefe to restore fiue Oxen for one Oxe, and
foure sheepe for one sheepe Exod. 22.1. but now the magistrate is not bound to the letter of this law, but to the equitie, that sinne be punished, and some reasonable satisfaction be made.
 Quest. What is the ceremorial law?
Ans.The ceremonial law. It is the ordination of such things as belong to the worship of God, and that in outward significant ceremonies, which generally and most espicially represented two things; First, the condition of mankind as it is both by corruption of nature in Adams fall, and by grace in Iesus Christ. Secondly the spirituall worship of God. The condition and state of mans corrupt nature appeato be polluted in that they had so many washings, sprinklings, and cleansings, and to be damnable in that bruite beastes were slaine for their offences and sinnes, as themselues witnessed by laying their hands vpon the heades of the beastes when they were to be slaine. Their state by grace was shewed to be most hap and blessed in that the beastes, which were slaine for their sinnes, did represent and foreshew Christe the immaculate lambe of God, which should be slaine for their redemption and saluation. And how all the ceremonies of the Iewes did represent the true and spirituall worship of
God, which now is vnder the gospel, the epistle to the Hebrewes declareth at large especially in three Chapters 8.9. and 10.
Quest. Whether is the ceremonal Law abrogated? 
Ans. Al the outward ceremonies of it are abrogated, but the true spirituall worship signified by them remaineth and shall abide for euer.
Quest. What is the mortall law? 
Ans. It is an eternall law of trueth,
The moral law. teaching man his duetie both to God and to his neighbour, whereunto are annexed, first a promise of eternal life to them that keepe it, secondly a commination and threatning of condemnation to them that breake it in any one point.
 Quest. Wheather were these conditions of life and death annexed to the law when it was first giuen to Adam (for you call it ane ternall law) or since when it was giuen and written at mount Sinai?
Ans. At both tymes; for the first is manifest Gen. 2.17. and the second likewise appeareth Deut. 30.15.19.
 Quest. All man kinde sinned and was dead and condemned in Adam by reason of his disobedience, how commeth it then to passe now that they haue life and death set before them
againe? or how happenneth it that there is life set before man if he keepe the law? Can man now by his workes recouer his first fall, and here after keepe the Law better then he did in his innocencie?
Ans. In Horeb the couenant of grace, made with their forfathers long before euer since the blessed seede of the woman was promised, was renewed, and the people hauing all their sinnes originall and actual freely pardoned in Iesus Christ, and being newly entred into Gods couenant, were as new bome babes, and so had life and death set before them againe.
 Quest. I thought the law had propounded death only to all men, because all men sinne, and not life to any, because no man keepeth the law.
Ans. The law giuen at the time of the couenant of grace, conteineth in it aswel the righteousnes of saith as the righteousnes of the law, as Moses sheweth Deut. 30.11.12.13.14. and Paul expoundeth it Rom. 10.6. for when the couenant of grace is made, Christ is the mediator, who of God is made vnto vs wisdome, and righteousnes and sanctification, and redemption, 1. Cor. 1.30.
 Quest. Whether is the morall abolished
now?
Ans. Partly it is and partly it is not, for it commandeth obedience, and that remaineth for euer, because all men are bound to obey the moral law. But where there is a promise annexed of eternal life, this promise remaineth for the faithfull, who fulfil the law in Christ, but it apperteineth not to the reprobate. Also the curse denounced against the breakers of the law remaineth for the vngodly, but shal not touch the godly who are iustified and saued by Christ.
 Quest. Whether is it your purpose to speake of the iudiciall, ceremoniall, and moral law or of some one of these only?
Ans. It is my purpose to speake of the morall law conteined in the ten commaundements specially, and to the end of euerie precept to ad the punishment appointed in the ciuil law for them that transgresse it. As for the ceremoniall law it is quite abolished, and therefore at this present I will say nothing of it.
 Quest. What order will you obserue in speaking of the morall lavv?
Ans. The same order they stand in. For they are deuided into two tables, and into ten commaundementes Deut. 4.13. Math. 22.37. But this must generally
be vnderstoode of them all, and of euerie one of them.
First, that wheresoeuer any vertue is commaunded, we must vnderstand the contrary vice is forbidden; and againe where any vice is forbidden, there the contrary vertue is co^maunded.
Secondly, because it was the Lordes purpose to comprehend much matter in fewe wordes for our benefittes, we must not rest vpon that particular thing only which is either commaunded or fordidden, but take with it all the causes, branches, and fruits of it and whatsoeuer accompanieth it.
Thirdly, though the things me^tioned in euery commandement be external, yet we must make the exposition to reach to the counsels, intents, and desires of the hearte, as al so to he words of the mouth, as Christ plainly sheweth, Math. 5.21. etc. in expounding the 6. and, 7. commaundements.
 Quest.
The first commandement. 15. Theu to come to the commandeme^ts, which is the first?
Ans. I The Lord am thy God, thou shalt haue no other Gods before me, Exod. 20.2.3.
Quest. Which of these two sentences conteineth the cemmaundement.

Ans. They both make but one comma^dement. For I tould you before, that where any thing is commaunded, there the contrary is forbidden. And where any thing is forbidden, there the contrarie is commanded. Wherefore I say the former sentence conteineth the commandement, I the Lord am thy God, and the latter sentence forbiddeth the contrary. Thou shalt haue none other Gods before me. So that if either were wanting, yet it must necessarily be vnderstoode. And these two sentences are els where often ioyned together as they be here, as Deut. 4.35 and. 6.4. Esai 43.11. Then wheras in all the other commaundements there is one thing only commaunded or forbidden, and the contrarie left to be vnderstoode, this commaundement expresseth both.
Quest. What is the summe and the meaning of this commaundement?
Ans. The meaning I take to be very manifest, that whereas other people and nations frame and take to themselues innumerable gods, as the Ammonites chose Molech Milcen to be their God Leuit. 18.21. and. 1. king. 11.5. The Zidonians Ashteroch Iudg. 2.13. The philistians Dagon Iudg. 16.23. the Moabites Chemosh Num. 21.29 the Syrians
Rimnon. 2. king. 5.18. The Assyrians Nisroch 2. king. 19.37. The Ecronites Baalzebub. 2. king. 1.2. The Babylonians Bell Esai 46.1. The Persians the Fire Socrat. lib. 7. Chap. 8. the Barbarous Masagete the Sunne, Herodot. lib. 1. the Egiptians almost all kinde. of beastes and birdes Herodot.
Epiphan. in Ancora ^0. lib. 2. the Grecians haue taken dead men for their gods Cicer. lib. 3. de natura deorum, the Romanes haue taken the gods of al nations, and whom it pleaseth the Senate to consecrate he shalbe their God, whereby it comes to passe that they haue moe Idols (for all the gods of the they haue are but Idols Psal 96.5.) then any other nation. And as the Romaines vnder their councels, and by the authoritie of the senate began to exceede other nations in this execrable Idolatrie; so their Emporours afterward by their owne authoritie, but aboue all other their holy cacolick Popes especially haue surpassed all that euer were before them. And not without great cause. For where others had nothing but vaine glory for making Gods, the popes haue also gotten great treasures of gold and siluer, first for making Thomas of Aquine, Thomas Becket, and an infinite number moe to be Gods, secondly through worshipping of their newe made Gods all the wealth of Europe hath
come to the popes coffers. For the popes haue made seuerall Gods for seuerall nations, for seuerall cities, for seuerall diseases, for seuerall dangers, and all for money. Wherefore though other nations had other Gods, 2. King. 17.30. yet the Israelites chosen out of the world to be the Lords people, should acknowledge no idoll of any nation to be their God, their helper, and their redeemer, but onely the Lord. And for this cause the Lord saith, I the Lord, or I Iehoua that haue created all thinges, of whom and in whom all things haue their beeing, euen I Iehoua am thy God, and thou shalt haue no other before me.
 Quest. What else doe you obserue in this commaundement?
Ans. I said before that we must not rest onely vpon one word commaunded or forbidden, but take all that appertaineth vnto it. As if we acknowledge the Lord to be our God, we must also acknowledge him to be almightie, righteous, iust, true, holy, good, gracious, etc.
 Quest. What more is there heere to be considered?
Ans. The third thing to be obserued in euery commaundement, and therefore in this is, that we doe not onely confesse with our mouth, but also beleeue in our hearts that the
Lord is our God.
 Quest. What is the vse of it then?
Ans.To trust in God. Although the commaundementes of the Lorde be exceeding broade and large that much vse may be made of them, yet at this present I will name onely fiue things, and; First we must learne to beleeue in him, and to repose all trust in him as in our onely God and helper to saue vs and deliuer vs in all distresses, and to giue vs all good and necessarie blessings. For the scripture euery where describeth God to be such a one, as Deut. 32.39. Behold nowe, for I, I am he, and there is no Gods with me: I kill, and giue life: I wounde, and I make whole: neither is there any that can deliuer out of my hand. And often else where, Psal. 115.9. and 125. Esay. 43.11.12.13.
 Quest. Is there any that professeth and acknowledgeth God, and trusteth not in him onely?
Ans. Yea there are many such, for how often did the Israelites distrusting Gods power and goodnes, murmure and rebell against the Lord and against Moses his seruant in the wildernesse. And how did a prince in Israell distrust, on whose hand the king leaned, when he said thus to Elisha the prophet, Though the Lord would make windowes in the heauen, could this thing come to passe,
2. King. 7.2. And how did king Ahaz distrust, when he answered to Esaias the prophet that promised him helpe from the Lord, I will not aske, neither will tempt the Lord, Esay. 7.12. And how did the Apostles distrust when they said Master Master, we perish, Luke. 8.24. Whereby we see clearely, that when we murmure against the Lords seruants, when we cry out desperatly because we see not the outward meanes of helpe, when we thinke that the Lords ministers speake to be vntrue or vnpossible, when we refuse grace that is offered vs, we the^ do not trust in God, we beleeue not in him. How doth the corrupt iudge trust in God when he wittingly giueth false iudgement for a bribe? the gentleman when he oppresseth his tenants to strengthen himselfe in his riches? Churchrobbers, miserly niggards, and all couetous men who scrape as it were to a heape the trash of this world, as though they could not otherwise liue? and that thinke to make goodly houses, and cause their memorie to last for euer? How trust they in God which dare not giue one smale penny, or one morsell of bread to the poore, for feare they themselues should want? The Apostle saith plainely, that such as repose their confidence in their riches that they gather them by right or wrong, that they keepe all to themselues,
they are idolaters, Ephes. 5.5. The poore man murmuring distrusteth God. The marchant whe^ he counterfetteth or corrupteth his warse, and the shop-keeper when he vseth false lightes, false measures, false weightes, they distrust God. When any man vseth vnlawfull meanes whatsoeuer, they distrust God, and they that put their confidence in lawfull meanes more then in God, and they that wil enterprice great matters without the Lords aduise and counsell, Esay, 31.1. Wherefore the further we wade into the vse of this commaundement, the further shall we finde our selues guiltie of distrust in God, and thereby perceiue that we are not in so good case as we thought we had beene, for keeping of this commaundement.
 Quest. What is the second thing you will obserue heere?
Ans. That we pray vnto God onely both in prosperity and in aduersitie.
Praier to God. Psalm. 50.15. Call vpon me in the day of trouble: so will I deliuer thee, and thou shalt glorifie me. And againe, aske and it shalbe giuen you: seeke and you shall finde, knocke and it shall be opened vnto you, Math. 7.7.
 Quest. Is there any that do not dailie craue of God by prayer whatsoeuer they neede?
Ans. Yea many. For in that I haue shewed there is great want of saith in many, so it
is certaine there is greater want of prayer in moe. For how shall they call on him whom they haue not beleeued? Rom. 10.14. And not onely they that distrust Gods power and goodnesse cease to call vpon him, but many also that repose all their confidence in God, often forget themselues, and pray not at all. Dauid beeing sore sicke, tumbled and tossed himselfe vpon his bed, and roared for verie griefe a great while before he remembred himselfe, and then at the last he praied, Psal. 32. The good king Asa sought not to the Lord in his disease, but to the phisicians, 2. Chro. 16.12. And there are with vs very many that doe as Dauid did, that is, lie groning, mourning, and sometimes weeping vpon their beddes in their sicknes, and cry out, yea roare for paine, and tumble from one side of the bed to the other, and out of one bed, or out of one chamber into another, and finde no comfort, because they cry not vnto the Lord that laid that sicknes vpon them, eyther for their sinnes, or triall of their faith and patience, or to awake them out of securitie, or for some other cause. And I thinke there are moe which doe as Asa did, that is, if they haue the gout, the palsie, the ague, the stone, the colike, the plurisie, or any other disease, if they send their seruantes on foote or on horsebacke, to fetch the phisitian
with all speede, they be stowe cost and spare not for any thing, they inquire the cause diligently, whether it came of cold or of heat, of ouer-streining themselues, or of idlenes as often it doth, or of distemperate diet by eating and drinking till they surfet and vomit. And all the house is too little to attend vpon them. But all this while neyther the sicke party by himselfe, nor the familie with him, nor with their neighbours do seeke by earnest praier to the chiefe phisician both of bodie and soule the Lord their God, who sendeth affliction to those that forget him in prosperirie, that he may driue them to seeke him in distresse as it is plainely declared in Hosea, Chap. 5.15. and 6.1.2. I will goe, and turne to my place (saith the Lord) till they acknowledge their fault, and seeke me: in their affliction they wil seeke me diligently. Come, and let vs returne to the Lord: for he hath spoyled, and he will heale vs: he hath wounded vs, and he will bind vs vp, etc. Paule teacheth vs the same doctrine, 1. Cor. 11.32. But when we are iudged we are chastened of the lord because we should not be condemned of the Lord. Thus we are taught to call vpon God by earnest praier, and doubtles the feruent praier of the faithful is very auailable with God, Ia. 5.16 But where is our obedience, where is our praier? forsooth that comes in last. For when the
phisician giues ouer his patient, and when his senses be gone, and he cannot speake, but is as good as dead, then we toule the bell, then we send for the minister to pray ouer him that is dead, whereby we shew what care we haue to call vpon God, when we doe thus as it were the day after the market, and so vse the minister or the ministerie for fashion sake. But in health how many great families, yea and such as would seeme very religious lie downe in the euening, and rise vp in the morning without praying together al the week long, al the yeare long, all their life long. And when many men be so carelesse of priuate prayer, it is not greatly to be marueiled that they care so little for publike prayer.
Quest. What is the third thing? 
Ans. That we reuerence and feare the Lord,
The feare of God. not with such a seruill and slauish feare as the reprobate haue, who feare the Lord and hate him, trembling onely at his iudgements, which they repine against, but with such a feare as a sonne beareth to his father, fearing of loue to displease him any way, and therefore feare to commit any sinne whereby the Lord might be displeased with them. For as godly men preferre the fauor of God before al the world, so they feare to displease him or to doe any thing that might displease him least they
should loose his louing fauour. Wherefore Moses ioyneth the feare of the Lord, and the keeping of his commandements together, Deut, 6.2. and 8.6. Dauid saith, Psal. 25.13. What man is he that feareth the Lord? him will he teach the way that he shall chuse. His soule shall dwell at ease, and his seed shal inherit the land. The secret of the Lord is reueiled to them that feare him, and his couenant to giue the^ vnderstanding.
 Quest. Who be those that feare not the Lord with this reuerent feare you speake of?
Ans. Those that feare men more then God, and temporall punishment more then eternall conde^nation, not considering what Christ hath said, Mat. 10.28. Feare not them which kill the bodie, but are not able to kill the soule: but rather feare him, which is able to destroy both body and soule in hel. Such be they which in persecution deny Christ and his Gospell, as Peter did, but vpon serious and hearty repentance when he wept bitterly, was forgiuen. Such be they that are diligent and ready to doe whatsoeuer a magistrate commaundeth, though it be flat contrary to the expresse commaundement of God, as did the ten tribes of Israel, when they obeyed wicked Ieroboam and worshipped the calues at Dan and Bethel, and after followed whatsoeuer Idolatrous kings commanded, as the prophet Micah complaineth
Cap. 6. The statutes of Omrie 16. are kept, and all the manner of the house of Ahab, and we walke in their counsels. And for this cause the Lord afflicted them as witnesseth the prophet Osea Chap. 5.11. Ephraim is oppressed and broken in Iudgment, because he willingly walketh after the commaundement, to wit, of their Idolatrous kings. Vriiah the priest is noted for obeying the commandement of King Ahaz and making an alter like to the alter of Damascus, 2. King. 16.11. But the poore women the Midwiues of Egipt, which had not beene instructed in true religion as Israel had, nor had not so much knowledge of God as, Vriiah the priest, feared God more then they, and would not kil the Hebrues children at the commaundement of Pharaoh Exod. 1.17. Yea the men that were of Sauls guarde would not kil the priestes at the kings commaundement 1. Sa. 22.17. The like godly feare we reade of in Daniel, and in his three companions, Dan,  3. and 6. and in the Apostles Act. 4.19.
Also we may reckon those in this number, that rush bouldly into al manner of sin, for which there is no penaltie or punishment inflicted by magistrates, and thereby they shew that they neither dreade Gods iudgements nor regard his commaundements.
Such be they that commit open or outragious wickednes: Absolom killed his brother Amnon 2. Sam: 13.28.29. burned Ioabs barly 2. Sam. 14.30. craftily stole the hearts of the subiectes from Dauid his Father 2. Sam. 15.2, openly rebelled against his father, 2. Sam. 15.10. etc. and lay with his fathers concubines in the sight of all Israel, 2. Sam. 16.22. Such a one was Ioab. who guilefully flew two men better then his selfe, Abner, 2. Sa. 3.27. and Amasa. 2. Sam. 20.9.10. and conspired treason with Adoniiah against Dauid and Salomon 1. king. 1.7. Such were the sons of Eli. 1. Sam. 2.2. Such are they that in Spaine can dissemble their religion. Such are they that openly prophane the Lords day, and contemne the word of God. And such are a greate number which liuing in riote call themselues good fellowes, though they set themselues in no good way, neither abhorre any thing that is euil. And whosoeuer will not submit themselues to liue in obedience to the commaundements of God.
 Quest. What is the fourth thing?
Ans. That we loue the Lord with all our heart, with all our soule, and with all our minde, Deut. 6.5. Math. 22.37. That seeing he is become our God, and hath done
so much for vs, and yet hath prepared greater things for vs then we can perceiue in this life, we should loue him as the author of our happinesse. And he that doth not thus loue God aboue all things, is not worthie to be one of his, Math. 10.37. He that loueth father or mother more then me, is not worthie of me etc.
 Quest. Who be those that loue not God with all their heart?
 First those that loue not neither reuerence his word, as first they that neuer come to the hearing of the word but against their willes, as delighting rather to hunt tauerns and alchouses, to keepe open their shoppes, to sit Idle at home, to cast their accounts, to walke into their gardens, about their ground, to remoue their cattel, to send their seruants to gather vp their dettes, and twentie such like things wherein they take greater pleasure then in going to heare the word of God. Secondly they that goe to the Church but spend the time there in sleeping, in talking, in meditating vpon worldly busines, and giue no attendance to the word of God. Lastly they that abuse the word of God either to defend and excuse their sinnes by the infirmities of holy men which are mentioned in the scriptures, as to excuse their drunkennes by the
example of Noe: their incest and addulteries by the examples of Lot, Iuda, Dauid, as thogh these things were written for men to imitate. But the holy Ghost hath written them for ensamples to vs: to admonish vs, on who^ the ends of the world are com, that we co^mit not the like as Paul sheweth 1. Cor. 10.6.11.12. that if any man thinke he stand, he should take heede least he fall: or else abuse the word in gibing, scoffing and mocking, and so turn the word of God into wantonnes to sporte themselues or others withall, as they doe that make plaies, comedies, or tragedies of the word of God, which is a horrible abuse. For the word of God is written, and the dispensation thereof committed to the ministers to saue the elect of God. 1. Tim. 4.16. and not to stage-players to make sport withal. Now whosoeuer they be that care not for Gods word or abuse it, as too too many do, it is as manifest as the sun in the midst of the firmament that they loue not God. Therfore let no man deceiue himselfe, and thinke he can loue God, when he doth not loue his word.
 Secondly they that loue not the saintes of God, but disdaine them, reuile them, intreate them euil, suffer them to be harbourles, hungry, naked, in destresse and miserie, and yet she who compassion to them. But
if a rich glutton, a cruel vsurer, a common blasphemer; a prophane Atheist, or a hypocriticall papist come to them, he shalbe curteously saluted, curiously interteined, often bidde welcom, and for him shall the fatt calfe be killed, and the best chamber in the house prouided and made readie. They Isay againe, that so highly esteeme the wicked, and so basely account of the Godly, they shew what loue of God is in them. For our common prouerbe is, loue me, and loue my dog: a thousand fould more then, Loue God and loue his saints, Iohn saith, whosoeuer hath, this worlds good, and seeth his brother haue need and shutteth vp his compassion from him: how dwelleth the loue of God in him 1. Iohn 3.17. And in an other place, If any man say I loue God, and yet hate his brother, he is a lyar 1. Iohn 4.20. When Christ would haue Peter to testifie his loue to him, he bad him feede his sheepe, Iohn 21.15. Christ gaue this admonition to all his disciples Iohn. 13.35. that by louing one another they should be knowen to be his disciples.
 Thirdly they that heare and see Gods name blasphemed, his word and truth slandered, peruerted and abused, yet they keepe silence and say nothing vnto it, it appeares they loue not God: for if their friend were so abused,
they would be very hote in his defence, but when God is abused, no man sayes any thing to it. And the world is so full of these, that he is counted a busie bodie that reproueth a blasphemous oath, and defendes the trueth. As no man that loueth his prince wil suffer his prince to be abused by word or deede, but he will and ought to defend him, though it be with his owne peril: so euery godly man wil be full of zeale and godly anger to see or heare the Lord his God to be abused. This zeale and godly anger was in Moses when he came with Ioshua from the top of Sinai and the two tables of the couenant of God in his hands. For when he came neere to the people and perceiued their idolatrie, he brake the tables of the couenant for very zeale, and sharply reproued them all, and commaunded the ringleaders of that Idolatrie to be slain. Exod. 32. This Godly anger and holy zeale was in Phinehas the Priest when he slew Zimrie and Cozbi. Num. 25.7.8. in Samuel when he reproued Saul and hewed Agag in peeces 1. Sam. 15.26.33. in Eliah when in defence of Gods truth he reproued Ahab boldly, and caused the false prophets to be slaine. 1. King. 18.18.40. And when he reproued Ahab for killing Naboth and his children. 1 King. 21; 19. etc. in Elisha when he reproued
Ahaziah 2. King. 1.16. and Iehoram 2. King. 3.13.14.15. in Erza, Chap. 9.3. in Nehemiah, Chap. 13, 17, 25. in Iohn Baptist, in Christ, and in the Apostles when they re proued sinne with bouldnes. Wherefore they that are as it were neither hote nor could, that they are neither grieued to heare Gods truth slandered, nor glad to heare God praised, they haue not the loue of God in the^. If a manseruant or beast be abused if his coate be but rent a little, how angrie wil he be? But when Gods name is blasphemed, his word euill spoken of, it is little regarded, as though it concerned vs not. Hereby it appeares we loue our seruants, our beastes or garments, better then we loue God.
Quest. What is the fift thing? 
Ans. That we giue thankes vnto God for euery thing we receiue of him dailie either for this life or for the life to come.
Thankes giuing to God. Wherefore if we doe acknowledge the Lord to be our God, and that we receiue euery good thing from him, we must of necessitie dayly praise him, as Dauid did almost in euery psalme, as Psalme, 34. and 103. and 136. and 147.
 Quest. Who be they that asscribe not all thanks and praise to God?
Ans. Those that sacrifice vnto their nets
and burne incense vnto their yearne as the prophet Habaccuk, speaketh Chap. 1.16. that is, those which ascribe al that they haue to their owne witte, to their owne strength, to the mony, to the ship, to their axe, to their flaile, to their spade, to their mattock, or to any other meanes whereby they get their liuing. For though God giue vs his blessings by ordinarie meanes, yet we are to acknowledge him to be the giuer of all. Many giue greate thankes to men for smal matters, but few doe hartely thanke God for their life and for all they haue. Least the Israelites should forget their strength and their redeemer, the Lord prescribed them a yearely protestation Deut. 26.5. etc. the wordes I omit because they are long, but reade them and ponder them diligently.
 Quest. What is the punishment which God hath appointed for them that breake his commandement?
Ans. It is death Exod, 22.20. He that offreth to any Gods, saue vnto the Lord only, shalbe slaine. Likewise we may reade Deut. 13. Leuit. 20.2. etc. not euerie one which transgressed in any of the particular branches afore mentioned, should be put to death, but he only that sinned in the highest degree, and reuolting from the Lord, chose an Idol to
be his God.
 Quest. What is the second commaundement?
The second commandement.
Ans. Thou shalt make thee no grauen image, etc. Exod. 20.4. etc.
Quest. What is the meaning of it?
Ans. The meaning is to prescribe the true worship of God. For as the first precept commaunded the Israelites to acknowledge the Lord onely to be their God: so this commandement sheweth how they must worship him, not leauing it to their liberty to worship him as they list. And this is the meaning of it. It consisteth of two partes: the first is the commaundement, the second is the reason.
 Quest. Shew it more plainely that God heere commaundeth how they ought to worship him. For I cannot yet perceiue it.
Ans. The Lordforbiddeth them to make any grauen images, or to bow downe to them vers. 4. and in the beginning of vers. 5. which cannot be vnderstood as though these images were Gods (for the first commaundement forbad all other Gods besides the Lord who is God alone) but as they represent God, that so he may be worshipped by images. Wherefore the Lord heere forbiddeth them to make any grauen or molten image to represent him, and so thereby to worship him. And the summe is, as if he had said, ye shal not make any image to resemble
me, neither shal ye worship me by such images. Now in that the Lord forbiddeth this worshiping of himself by images, we must vnder stand that he co^ma^deth the co^trary, that is, they must so worship him as he himself prescribeth.
 Quest. Seeing you haue laid down two branches of the commaundement; first making of images to represent God by them, and secondly worshipping of God by images: both which are forbidden, I pray you open both these more plainely. And first why doth God forbid vs to make an image like vnto himselfe, or to resemble him?
Ans. There may be many reasons alledged why the Lord is not to be represented by any image, and first it ought to be a sufficient reason to euery godly man, because God himselfe doth heere expressely forbid it. Secondly the Lorde in giuing of these ten commandements, of purpose vttred his voice that the people might heare him, but appeared not vnto them in any visible forme, because they should not make any fimilitude or likenes of him. Thirdly seeing God appeared not, nor was not seene, for no man hath seene God at any time neyther can see him, Exod. 33.20. and 1. Tim. 6.16. and 1. Iohn. 4.12. it followeth that there is not, neyther can be any image of God, because there is neyther painter nor grauer nor any other artificer that can make the
similitude of that he neuer saw, nor no other man that could describe it vnto him. Fourthly, there is nothing in heauen, nor in earth that is like vnto God. For God is a spirit, Iohn. 4.24. and not a creature and therefore cannot be resembled by any creature. Fiftly, they that haue attempted any such wicked thing, as to make an image of God, they haue shewed their folly by their dissenting one from another, when some haue painted God after one fashion, and some after an other, that their foolishnes may be derided, as Dionysius derided the superstitious heathen in his daies,
Cic. lib. 3. de natur. deor. and tooke away a golden beard from Aesculapius, saying it was an vnseemely sight that the son should be made with a beard, seeing his father was made without. Sixtly, they that haue tempted to make any similitude of God haue sinned, and the Lord hath punished them, Ro. 1.23.24.
 Quest. Seeing there are so many reasons why they neither could make any image of God, neither were permitted to do so, how commeth it to passe that God forbids them to worship him by an image. For if they might not make an image of God, yea if they could not make an image of him, it seemeth a needlesse thing to prohibite them to worship him by any such image. And yet that you noted as the second branch of this commaundement. I pray you therefore shew me the reason.

Ans. Ierome in his commentaries vpon the second chapter of Hosea hath a true sentence, Omnia idola ex mortuorum errore creuerunt, Al (this kinde of) idolatrie hath his beginning of an error conceiued of the dead. The reason and manner whereof is largely described by Plato, Lib. 11. de legibus. Laertius de vitis philosoph. Tull. lib. 3. de natur. deor. Plini. lib. 2. cap. 7. The booke of Wisedome, Cap. 14. vers. 14.15.16. Tertul. apolog. cap. 10. and 11. and 12. etc. Ciprian de vanitate idolorum and others. But the summe of all is this, as neare as I can collect it from the beginning. Ninus the first great conqueror of Assyria, to gaine more fame to himselfe, commaunded that his father Belus being dead should be rese^bled by an image made after his liknes, and honored for a God. And for the same cause built a te^ple for him in Babylon, and therin set vp his image, which Plinie saith, lib. 6. cap. 26. was there to be seene in his daies, which was about 80. yeares after Christ. The image was made like to Belus, and when the people bowed themselues to that image, they worshipped Belus and not the image. From this beginning of idolatrie first deuised by Ninus (not by Terah the father of Haran, as Epiphanius saith) did the like superstition spread it selfe among all nations: and cruell tyrants in euery country, after their death were consecrated
for Gods and worshipped by their images. And briefly to go forward with these new Gods a little before I apply it to this commaundement, I will passe ouer all other nations, yea the Grecians that abounded with these kindes of Gods, and in a word note the ripe wits of the Romans, who though they receiued this deuise from others, yet after they once found it, haue surpassed alothers, and of whom it is commonly said: Roma alios deos recepit, Caesares dedit, Rome receiued all their other gods (which were before that time) but they haue made their Emperours to be Gods, euer since they had any. And for their Emperours Ireferre the reader to Herodian in the beginning of his fourth booke, where vpon the death of Seuerus he sheweth that the Emperours were consecrated for Gods which left eyther sonnes or other to succeede them in the Empyre. The manner of the consecration he also declareth at large, that they had animage made like to the dead Emperour, which the laide in a bed, and for seauen daies space the Senators sate on the left side of the bed, and the noble matrones on the right side, and phisicians came daily to visite that sicke image in the bed. After seauen daies, as though the Emperour were newe dead, the noble young men of the citie caried the dead image
into the open place called Campus Martius, and put into it a costly tent filled with all kind of sweete odors, and after great solemnitie the senatos first, and then all the rest put fire to the tent, and when all was on a fire and a smoke, one let an Aegle fly out of the middest of the tent in the sight of all the people, and that Aegle was supposed to cary the Emperours soule to heauen, and so was he consecrated for a God euer afterward, and worshipped by an image. And now to goe a little further, the most holy Popes of Rome inferiours to none in all kinde of abhomination, haue thought it a chiefe point of their glory to be as skilfull in making Gods as any heathen, and therefore haue learned this of them, to consecrate and make new gods (they cal them saints, but they iuggle when they say so to be cast a mist before mens eyes, for their owne booke of ceremonies calleth it Apotheosis, that is, deifying) whom so euer they list. And as Herodian describeth the heathen consecration of Emperours: so the booke of the ceremonies of the Church of Rome, Lib. 1. sect. 6. declareth the blasphemous deifying of popish Gods. The chiefe pointes be these. First some men desirous to leaue his friende consecrated for a God after his death, goes to that cursed Calphas the Pope, and commending
his friende to haue liued a most holy catholike popish life, desireth his holinesse to consecrate him. Secondly the pope commaundes inquirie to be made of that dead person whether he were a right papist in his life time. Thirdly the Pope propoundes the matter to the company of Cardinals to see what they say to it. Fourthly the Pope and his crewe inquire more diligently whether that mans life was saintish as any sodomiticall frier or monke. Fiftly that antichrist with his crew consult whether the mans life was such that he deserues nowe to be made a God. Sixtly they decree to make him a God. Seauenthly there must be a great courte of the Pope his Cardinals, Patriarkes, Archbishops, Bishops, and Abbots holden to decree of the matter againe. Eightly the time and place are appointed for the deifying of that dead person. Lastly when they come to doe the deede, first there is great solemnity of many antichristian ceremonies, secondly that beast that counterfeites the lambe, but speakes like the dragon, he makes that dead man a GOD after this manner: Ad honorem sanctae and indiuiduae Trinitatis, and exaltationem fidei catholicae, ac Christianae religionis augmentum: authoritate ciusdem Dei omnipotentis, Patris, Filii, and Spiritus sancti,
and beatorum Apostolorum Petri and Pauli, and nostra; de fratrum nostrorum consilio decernimus; and definimus bonae memoriae N. sanctum esse: and sanctorum catalogo ascribendum; ipsumque catalogo huiusmodi ascribimus. Statuentes, vt ab vniuersali ecclefia anno quolibet in dei taelifestum ipsius and officium deuote and solenniter celebretur. In english thus: For the honor of the holy Trinitie, and for the aduancement of the catholike faith and Christian religion: we with the aduise of our brethren, by the authoritie of the same almightie God, the Father, the Sonne, and the holy Ghost, and of the blessed Apostles Peter and Paul and by our own authority do decree and appoint N. of worthy memory to be a saint, and to be registred among the saintes, and we doe inrole his name in the same kalender. Commaunding the catholike Church deuotely and with solemnity to celebrate his feast and worship euery yeare vpon such a day (as shalbe nominated.) And thus that Antichrist of Rome makes new gods and hath made mo then his kalender wil hold, I meane moe then there are daies in the yeare and for that cause he hath put out ofte^ one of his old gods, to prouide a place in the kalender, and a day in the yere to worship his new God. But now to turn to the co^mandement, and to your question, the Lord giuing his people speciall
warning of the superstitio^ of al heathens round about them, who had many Gods and worshipped their Gods by Images, doeth in this second commaundement expressely forbid Israell to worshippe him by any Image, that they should not be like the heathen. And for this cause the Lord appeared not in the likenesse of any thing when he gaue the law, but only caused them to heare his voice. For this cause the Lord in plaine words forbiddeth them to make any Image to resemble him. And to shew how he detesteth this Idolatrie, and to admonish them often and euery way; he saith further, that they shall not fall downe before any such Image to doe him any worship, that if the Israelites doe so at any time, they shalbe without al excuse. And hereby it appeareth how grossely the papists sinned, and how expressely against the wordes; and against the sense and meaning of this commaundement. For they haue Images of God the father, and of the sonne, and of the holy Ghost, directly against this commaundement. Againe when they say they worship not the Images, but God by the Images, that also you see is here statly forbidden. And to fulfil the measure of iniquitie, they haue made other Gods besides the Lord, euen those which they cal
Saints as I shewed before. But that the pope consecrated them for Gods and not for saints, it is manifest: for if they were faithfull beleeuers, they were Saints before, as Paul in the beginning of euery epistle almost calleth the faithfull Saints. If they were no Saints in this life, the Pope could not make them Saints afterward, neither did he professe so to do. Secondly the Pope appointed sabbaths and dayes of rest for them, that they might those dayes be worshipped. Thirdly the Pope appointed a speciall seruice and worship to be doone to euery one of them, on their seuerall Sabbaths. Fourthly the Pope appointed their Images to be made, and that men prostrate before their Images should worship the^. fiftly appointed that men should prayvnto them al, and seuerally to each of them for seuerall occasions: Al these and diuers such other things shew that the pope consecrated them for Gods, against the first co^mandement. And that popish Images should be made against this co^mandement. And hereby you maysee what acount is to be made of popish Images. 
 Quest. Whether then, doth this commaundement forbid the making of anie Image at all?
Ans. The Lord here forbiddeth to make any Image or any similitude to represent or resemble him: for he is not like to any creature
in heauen or in earth as Esaius sheweth Chap. 46.5.9. etc. and Chap. 40.18.25. But otherwise it is not simply vnlawful to make anie Image of other things. For God himselfe called Betzaleel and Aheleab Exod. 31.1.6. and filled them with the spirit of wisdome in all necessarie arts for the tabernacle, to ingraue and make Cherubims Exod. 25.18. and 36.1. to embroider Aarons garments, to make bels and pomegranats for the skirts of his garment Exod. 28.3.4. Likewise the Lord replenished two Hirans, otherwise called Hurames, the father and the sonne, with wisdome cunningly to worke euery artificial thing belonging to the building of Salomons Temple 1. King. 7.13. and 2. Chro. 2.14. and 4.16. and they made similitudes of Bulles, of Lions, of Cucumers, of Cherubims, of Pomgranats, of Palmetres etc. 1. king. 7. wherby it is manyfest that some Images are lawfull, euen those which are Images or Similitudes of such creatures as are obiect to our senses, whether they be in heauen or in earth or in the waters; and which are made for ciuil, and lawful, and honest vses or recreation. Or more briefely thus. Al artificial Images of the first table are vnlawfull: but artificiall Images of the second table are lawfull, if they be made for honest and lawfull
vses or recreation.
 Quest. Whether may not we now haue lawful Images in our Churches, as well as the Iewes had in the Tabernacle, and in the Temple?
Ans. No, there are many reasons against it. First, Moses, Exod. 25, etc. and Salomon, 1. Chro. 28.11.19. had expresse warrant and commaundement for that they did. Secondly, it appeareth. Heb; 8. and 9. and and. 10. that the Tabernacle, and the Temple with al their furniture, were types and figures to represent before the eyes of Israel the spirituall worship of God vnder the Gospel, and the glorious bewtie of that spirituall house and temple, whereof Peter speaketh. 1. Pet. 2.5. and Paul. Ephes. 2.21. Which Haggai prophesieth of Chap. 2.10. and is expounded Heb. 12.26.27. And thus you see there was good reason for those Images vnder the law. But there is not the like reason for vs now. For first, we haue no warrant, as Moses and Salomon had, to set Images in our Churches, and so it were sinne for vs to doe without warrant. Secondly, it were to turne them from a ciuil vse, to a religious vse, and so they should be conteined in the first table and against this commaundement. Thirdly, if they were set in Churches for ornaments,
that were to bring againe the abolished ceremonies, and to darken the true and perfect bewtie of the Church of Christ, which standeth not in outward painted walles, but in holynes and righteousnes in mens heartes, wordes, aad deedes, in hearing of the word, receiuing of the sacraments, and all other things which Christ hath commaunded.
 Quest. Who then be they that breake this commaundement? 
Ans. First, they that commit this grosse sinne of Idolatrie, and make Images either to represent God, or to worshippe him by them, as the Isaelites did when they made the calfe to worship God by it Exod. 32.4.5. and not that first time only, but a long time after in the wildernes did they breake his commaundement, as we reade Leuit. 17.7. Deut. 12.8. Amos 5.25.26. Act. 7.42. Likewise we reade of Michas Iudg. 17. of Ieroboam 1. King. 12.28. and the rest of the kings of Israel. The papistes a long time haue prophaned his commaundement, and yet doe.
 Secondly, they that worship not God after his own co^maundement, but ad sum thing to his word, or take somthing from it, or alter it, setting vp their owne deuises and traditions in steade of Gods ordinances, as
the Iewes did Esai 29.13. and are reproued by Christ: 15.8. Wherefore Ierome saith in Ierem. 32, in ecclesia ponitur Idolum, quando nouum dogma statuitur, When any new opinion is established, then an Idol is set vp in the Church. The Corinthians thus changed the right vse of the Lords supper 1. Cor. 11. Some indeuoured the like among the Colossians, euen to preferre their owne deuises to Gods word Coloss. 2.18. The papists are deepely guiltie in this point whether you consider the doctrine or the discipline which Christ commended to his Church. And herein they offend also, which in the congregation will pray priuately, or reade priuately, for though priuate praying and reading be good and holy at other times, yet then it is vnlawful, because God hath commaunded a publike worship in the assembly, where all ought to ioyne together with one heart and one voice, euery man according to his calling. They also that say they can serue God as well at home, as in the congregation.
 Thirdly, they that maintaine any vnlawful worship of God, that is alreadie in practise, say they will doe as their forfathers did, as somtimes the Iewes did Ierem. 44.16. And so doe the papists in maintaining their superstions,
which ought rather to be abolished. For whiles all such patrons of wicked traditions, haue no better reasons but because it hath beene accustomed, they may reme^ber that vulgar sentence of Cypryan ad Pompeium contra epistolam Stephani, consuetudo sine veritate vetustas erroris est, a false custom is an ould error.
 Fourthly, they that follow their good intents, and thinke God accepteth what they meane well, as Saul set a faire glose of a good intent vpon a foule sinne, when he tould Samuel the best of the cattel were reserued to be sacrificed to the Lord 1. Sam. 15. but Samuel tould him againe, that the Lord was better pleased with obedience then with sacrifice. And Salomon saith Prouer. 14.12. There is a way which seemeth right to a man but the issues thereof are the waies of death. Dauid had a good intent when he would haue builded a house for the Lord. 2. Sam. 7. But his seruice was not accepted. Peter meant well when he gaue Christ counsell to fauour himselfe, Math. 16.22. but he receiued a sharpe answere. The most parte of Christians in these dayes are sicke of this disease, and think all is wel which they mean well, in coming to the Church when they list, and going out in prayer, in receiuing
both the sacraments when, where, and how they please, and if they haue giuen offence to the whole congregation, they wil make satisfaction as they please, and so the word of God is not the rule of their life, and the minister standes for a Cypher to do what they bid him. But because they must all of them appeare before the Iudgement seate of God, let them heare before, how acceptable to God these their prayers be, such receiuing of the sacraments is, and generally how acceptable all such will-worships, and good intents be to God. For thus saith the Lord. He that killeth a bullocke, (is as acceptable to me as) if he slew a man: he that sacrificeth a sheepe as if he cut of a dogges necke: he that offreth an oblation, as if he offred swines blood: he that remembreth incense, as if he blessed an I dol: yea they haue chosen their owne wayes, and their soule deligheth in their abominations Esai: 66.3. But, if it were not to cast pearles before swne, so vnteachable is the world now a dayes, I could giue them good counsell in the words of the Lord Eccle. 4.17. and 5.1. Take heede to thy foote when thou enterest into the house of God; and be more neere to heare then to giue the sacrifice of fooles: for they know not that they doe euil. Be not rash with thy mouth, nor let thy heart be
hasty to vtter a thing before God: For God is in the heauens, and thou art on the earth.
 Quest. Who be they then that keepe this commaundement?
Ans. They that worship God in sincerity according to his own word, and not after mens fancies. For not euery one that saith Lord, Lord shall enter into the kingdom of heauen but he that doth the will of my father which is in heauen, saith Christ, Math. 7.21. 
 Quest. What if by Gods prouidence we liue in a Church where many abuses are, and God is not so purely worshipped as he requireth in this commaundement? shall we therefore breake off al felowship with that Church, in Gods worship, and goe to some other?
Ans. There hath not yet been any Church, as I suppose, which hath not had her wantes and imperfections, as in the Epistles of Paul, of Peter, of Iames, of Iohn, of Iude, it appeareth there were foule blemishes in the best Churches in the Apostles daies, and since alwaies haue beene, and now are, that a man cannot tell whither to goe, if he may not abide in that Church where diuers imperfections are. Wherefore I suppose many thinges are to be tolerated before we separate our selues from the Church, though euery man must keepe his owne handes thus farre cleane and vnpolluted,
that he doe no such thinges himselfe to iustifie, vphold, or countenance such abuses, but onely tolerate and suffer that he cannot redresse. And thus I suppose a man is bound to abide in the felowship of the Church so long as the foundation is holden, and Iesus Christ onely preached to be the alone sauiour of Gods elect, and the true sacramentes of the Lord be administred; though otherwise there be many abuses. I knowe, for my part, of fewe such separations that haue bene commendably made any where since Christ was vpon the earth, though all ages since his ascention witnes that great corruptions and foule abuses haue beene in euery Church of any note without exception. Of all other Churches, the Church of Rome that a long time boare sway ouer all Churches in Europe almost (the Grecians were neuer vnder the yoke of that antichrist) hath beene the worst, and degenerated most, euen from a true Oliue into a wild Oliue, from the spouse of Christ to be the synagogue of Satan, and yet few separations were made from that Church, till now of late yeares, when the prophesies of the reuelation were accomplished, and all generally almost went out of Babylon together and separated themselues from her. And the whole worlde seemes to approue
this separation to be made by God, that sent so many and so mighty deliuerers. That separation e the Waldenses or poore brethren of Lyons in Fraunce was commendable and praise worthy, though I remember not the like to haue happened in all popery, but many saintes of God, and many whole Churches liued vnder the Popes yoke, and tolerated many grieuous things till the time of deliuerance came. Againe I tremble to remember some separations that haue beene made because of the abuses that were in the Churches, as the Nouatians separated themselues from all other Churches; so afterward did the Donatistes: the Pelagians were not farre from such opinions: and nowe in our daies Anabaptistes forsake the fellowship of the Churches, and all these vnder coloure of holinesse, because they would liue most holily, and obediently to the commandements of God, and because they coulde not beare with some wantes that were in the Churches. But into what foule and grosse opinions, I meane heresies, these separating themselues, did fall, the learned knowe, and I suppose it not greately necessarie heere to repeate.
 Quest. What is the reason of this commandement? 

Ans.The reason of this commandement. For I the Lorde thy God, am a Ielous God, etc. Vers. 5.6.
 Quest. What meaneth the Lorde when he saies, he is ielous, or what signifies that worde?
Ans. It signifieth as much as, zealous, or to be moued with a very ardent affection and feruent desire, proceeding eyther of loue to saue the thing vntouched, which is loued Zachar. 1.14. and 8.2. or else of indignation and wrath against that thing which deserueth reuengement and punishment, Exod. 34.14. Nahum. 1.2. and heere it is vsed in both those two senses or significations. For the Lord saith, he is a Ielous, or zealous God, full of indignation and fierce wrath against them that breake this commandement, yea so feruentlie angrie, that he wil punish them vnto the third and fourth generation. Againe he saith, he is a Ielous, or zealous God, and carieth such feruent loue, such entire affection towardes them that keepe this and the rest of his commaundementes, that he will blesse them and keepe them for thousandes of generations, euen for euer and euer, so that whosoeuer toucheth them to do them any hurt, had as good touch the apple of his eye, Psal. 18.25.26. Zach. 2.8.
Quest. How commeth it to passe that the Lord beeing iust and righteous, will punish the posteritie
of the wicked that break his commandements? shall the childe be punished for the fathers, or grandfathers, or great grandfathers fault?
Ans. The Lord saith plainly, Deu. 24.16. The fathers shall not be put to death for the children, nor the children put to death for the fathers, but euery man shall be put to death for his owne sinne. And Ezek. 18.4.20. The same soule that sinneth shall die, yea the Lord saith. Ezek. 18.21.23. If the wicked will returne from all his sinnes that he hath committed, and keepe all my statutes, and doe that which is lawfull and right, he shall surely liue, and shall not die. Whereupon I reason thus, that if the Lorde, wil pardon the sinner himselfe when he repenteth, it is very certaine he will not punish the child for that offence which is pardoned vpon the fathers repentance. Therefore if you marke the wordes, you may easely perceiue there is no such thing heere said as you suppose. For the Lord doth not absolutely say he wil visite the children of the breakers of this commandement to the third and fourth generation: but he addeth this clause, of them that hate me, as if he had said, if the father hate me and breake this commandement, then will I with greate ielousie and anger visit him and punish him for his sinne. And if his sonne, or his Nephew, or his Nephewes sonne continue in the same sin,
and breake this my commandement or others as his fathers did, then shall my ielousie and mine indignation smoke against them all for a long time, as the prophet Ezekiel declareth plainely, Chap. 18.
 Quest. What is the cause why the Lords mercies and his loue reacheth to thousandes of generations, and his wrath but to foure generations? Is there not as great reason that the Lordes wrath should extend to thousands of them that hate him, as his mercy to thousands of them that loue him? Is there not as great equity in the one as in thother?
Ans. Me thinke you should not find fault either with the length of Gods mercies, or with the shortnes of his iudgements. Notwithstanding because you propound the question, I answer, that where the Lord in respect of mans sins and desarts by reason of sin, and of his own iustice, might iustly extend his anger to thousands and thousands: yet it pleaseth him to shew mercy in respect of his owne name and glory, as it is manifest. Ezek, 20.9.14, 22. and 36.21.22.23 32. For all this is spoken to and of the Church of God, not to them that are without. And that which Moses speaketh of all Israel in generall, may proportionably be applied to the singular parts of Israel Deut. 32.26, 27. I said I woulde make their remembrance to cease from among men; Saue that I feared the fury of the enemy,
least their aduersaries should wax proud, and lest they should say, Our hie hand, and not the Lorde hath done al this. The Lord that loueth his own vnto the end (Ioh. 13.1.) doth now and then punish them for their sins (Heb. 12.6.) and for that purpose giueth them into the hands of wicked me^, which being both his and their enemies and yet the rod of Gods wrath, Esay. 10.5. do not chastice them for their amendement, according to the lords meaning, but hauing once gotten them into their fingers, purpose to destroy them vtterly, Esay. 10.6.7. and reioice in the cruelty against Gods saints, Ezek. 25. and say they sin not against the Lord in so doing, Ier. 50.7, yea sometimes they exalt themselues blasphemously against the Lord himselfe, as though he could not saue his own people and deliuer them out of their handes, (Num. 14.16 and 2. King. 18.35. Esay. 10.10.11.) therefore the Lord, hauing respect to his own glory, in iudgment often remembreth mercy, staieth his visitation, and receiueth his own people to mercy againe (Esay. 54.7.8.) though they deserued a longer punishment: and then recompenceth his and their cruell blasphemous enemies seauen fold into their bosom, Esay 10.12.13. and Cap. 14. And this is the cause why the Lordes wrath is extended but to the third and fourth generation of them that breake his co^mandements, wheras to them that keepe his commaundementes
his mercy endure for euer.
Que. What is to be obserued out of this reason?
Ans. First, as in euery society men are kept in order, and drawen to perform their duty either by reward for doing wel, or by punishment for offending: so the lord in this co^mandeme^t, that eyther he may allure vs with his mercies to keep his commandements, or with his iudgments terrifie vs from doing euil, setteth both before vs, that by one means or other he may keep vs fro^ working our own destruction. And if our mind were as earnestly bent after heauenly things; as after earthly things or if we gaue so much credit to God as we doe to men: then as we spare no labour, neither feare any peril by sea or land by night or day, in the city or in the desart, to get the reward that man promiseth: so should we much more giue our selues wholly to do the wil of God, that we and our posterity to a thousand generations, might be blessed both temporally and eternally, with earthly and with heauenly blessings for euer. But alas, when we carelesly neglect, or wilfully contemne the keeping of Gods co^mandementes, our works are an open profession before the world, and our co^sciences are and shalbe witnesses before God, that we neither beseue the lords mercies, nor fear his iudgments. They are counted litle better then madmen that co^temn the lawes of men, and whe^ the iudge co^meth and sitteth on the bench their folly
appeareth For they are arreined, condemned, and executed. But they are counted wise men which despise Gods Laws and tremble no more then stocks, to heare Gods terrible iudgments denounced both temporally and eternally against them and their posteritie. Neuerthelesse they shalbe brought to iudgement, when it will be too late to repent, and then shall they receiue their full punishment. We see many struggle with this worlde to scrape welth together for them and theirs; but they striue against the streame, it will not do with the^ as they desire, the more they toyle, the faster it falleth from them like water, the more reuenewes they haue, the poorer the wax (Hag. 1.) and that by the iust iudgement of God, who crosseth the^ and visiteth them in all things they haue, and that because they worship him not after the rule of his owne word, but with the deuises of men, or with their good intents. And woulde to God such as professe Christ would spare but one howre of 24. to meditate vpon this commaundement, and in meditation thereof to compare their estate with it. For then should they see and learne, that the Lord blesseth them that loue him, crosseth them that hate him, and so amend what is amisse in them.

Secondly, we learne out of this reason, that which the phophet Ieremie teacheth vs Lament. 3.22. It is the Lords mercies that we are not consumed because his compassions faile not. For when we worship God with our good intents and when we will follow our owne and other mens deuises so stiffely and obstinately, that though the Lord tell vs of it, and admonish vs out of his owne word, and by his ministers, yet will we stop our eares and perhappes hate him for his labour, that is the messenger of such tidings: then the Lord, that might iustly wipe vs and our posteritie out of the booke of life, doeth notwithstanding in iudgement remember mercy (Habac. 3.2.) And for his owne names sake comforteth the third or the fourth generation againe (Esai. 54.7. This is mercie peerels. And yet nothing can moue our hard seared consciences to beleeue the Lord to feare him, or to loue him. Thus God deliuered Israell out of Egipt after 400. yeares miserie. Thus he deliuered them out of the hands of the Philistim many times, as we reade in the book of Iudges. Thus he deliuered them out of Babylon after 70. yeares captiuitie. Thus finally he sent Christ to deliuer them, that sat in darknes, fast bound with the chaines of their sinnes. And since Christ ascended gloriously
into heauen, the Lord hath deliuered his Church, first out of that hote persecution which lasted almost 300. yeres, and since againe out of the most miserable bondage of poperie. Yea euen we were lately deliuered out of a bitter persecution in the dayes of Queene Marie. And yet for all this we follow our owne deuises, our good intents, and in euery deede our hartes lust with greater fiercenesse then euer we did, for which cause we haue neede to feare least som destruction be at hande. For the nearer Gods iudgements are, the more incorrigible alwayes are the sinnes of men.
 Thirdly, we learne here, that they hate the Lord, that do not worship him as he hath commaunded them, but after their owne fantasies, and after the traditions of men. Though they say, yea though they sweare that they loue God; yet their consciences at that day shall conuince them, and God, who is greater then their conscience (1. Iohn. 3.20,) plainely telleth them in this place, that they hate him, Wherefore if the Lorde say we hate him it is not our hard heartes, our stiffe neckes, our obstinate minds, our brasen brows that can proue we loue him And let euery soule weigh with himselfe what it is to hate God. For certainly the
haters of the Lord shalbe found lyars.
 Fourthly, we learne that he which loueth the Lord in deede, keepeth his commaundements, and worshippeth him as he commaundeth in his word. Wherefore let euery one that loueth the Lord in truth, be diligent to declare his loue by obeing the voice of the Lord. For this is the loue of God that we keepe his co^mandements 1. Iohn 5.3. And the Lord loueth them that loue him Pro. 8.17.
 Quest. What is the punishment which the magistrate ought to inflict vpon them that transgresse this commaundement in the highest degree and grossest maner?
Ans. I suppose it is death, for though I remember not so expresse a commaundement for it as there is for the other eight co^ma^deme^ts (For there is no humane punishme^t appointed for the breakers of the last commaundement) yet but that which may be taken out of the word by collection, and these reasons perswade me so to thinke. First the transgressors of the third and fourth commaundements are punished with death, and therefore they that breake this commaundement ought likewise to be punished with death, seeing this is more generall then they both, so that the offences committed against them, may be reduced within the compasse
of this. Secondly the punishment appointed for the transgressors of the seauen first commaundementes is death, and generally you may obserue this order in all the commaundements of both tables, that the greatest sinne is first forbid, and the next consequently by order and by degrees, wherefore there is no reason to exempt this out of them all, seeing it standeth in the seconde place. Thirdly I take this to be a generall rule, that where no satisfaction can be made, there the punishment is death. Lastly, we see that Moses, Exod. 32.27. by the commandement of the Lord, put to death aboute 3000. Idolaters, which were ring-leaders to that Idolatrie in making of the calfe to worship God by, which was most directly against this second commaundement. And for these and such like causes I am perswaded the punishment is death. But this you must vnderstand both here, and in the other six first commaundements, that it is not euery particular branch, but the greatest sinne in the hiest degree that falleth vnder the power of the magistrates sword, that he may put him to death, as for example, if a man smite his neighbour and wound him, hauing a purpose to kill him, though this be a greate sinne against the sixt co^maundement, yet he
is not to be put to death for it.

Ans. What is the third commaundement?

 Quest. Thou shalt not take the name of the Lord thy God in vaine etc. vers. 7.
Quest. What is the summe of this commaundement?
Ans. The whole standeth of two parts, whereof the first is the commaundement, the second is the reason.
 Quest. What is the summe of the commaundement, or the meaning of it?
Ans. It forbiddeth vs to take the name of God in vaine, wherein we must vndersta^d all manner of abusing his name by what meanes soeuer. For though it seemeth that the Lord noteth but that one greate blasphemie of abusing his name in swearing and forswearing: yet I admonished you before, that all other sinnes of like nature and qualitie were forbidden with their causes and effects. The Lord for breuitie sake, and for our infirmitie sake, nameth only in euery commaundement, either the most horrible sinne forbidding it, or else the most singular vertue commaunding it. Also we must on the contrary part vnderstand, that the reuerent vsing of Gods name is here commaunded.
 Quest. Because they abuse of Gods name in swearing is the chiefest sinne here forbidden,
I pray you shew me what it is to swere, and what is lawfull, what vnlawfull.
Quest. To sweare is to call God to witnes that we speake to be true, that so more credit may be giuen to our wordes. But there are so many maners of oathes, that it is more easie to reckon them vp, then to giue a general definition of them al.
 Quest. How many kindes or maners of oaths doe you make?
Two kinds of oathes. A voluntary oath.
Ans. First there are two kindes of oaths: the one voluntarily, when a man is not compelled to sweare; the other necessarie or constreined, when a man by authoritie is compelled to sweare. Againe a voluntarie and francke oath is either when one partie alone sweareth, or els when two parties sweare each to other of their owne accord neither hauing authoritie to compell the other. And one partie alone somtimes sweareth at the request of an other, as when Rahab hauing saued the liues of the two spies which Ioshua sent to view the land of Ierico, she requested them to sweare, that they also would preserue her life, when they had wonne that citie, Ioshua 2.12. and 9.22. Saul requested Dauid to sweare that he would not abolish his name out of his fathers house, and Dauid sware 1. Sam. 24.22.23. And sometimes also one
