partie alone sweareth not being requested, as Dauid mourning for the death of Abner, who^ Ioab had guilefully murthered, protested and sware that he would eate nothing that day till the sunne were downe. 2. Sam. 3.35. and Dauids chiefe men of warre also protested and sware, that Dauid should not goe any more in his owne person to the battell 2. Sam. 21.17. and Salomon perceiuing that Adoniah his brother went about to worke treason protested and sware that he should die for it. 1 King. 2.23. And thus one partie or person sweareth voluntarily in a lawfull matter, and of importance, and vpon good occasion. For if a man sweare in an vnlawfull thing, and rashly, and when there is no cause, he sinneth greatly, as did Herode Math. 14. and Dauid. 1. Sam. 25 22. and Saul. 1. Sam. 28.10.
Againe sometime two parties voluntarily consent to sweare each to other, as did Abraham and Abimelech Gen. 21.23.24.31. Likewise Isaac and Abimelech Gen. 26.28.31 Iacob and Laban Gen. 31.53. Ionathan and Dauid 1. Sam. 2.42. And here also they that sweare in a thing vnlawfull, and without good cause, they offend, as did the Israelites Iu. 21.1. and the Iewes, which sware they would kil Paul Act. 23.12. And thus much for
voluntarie swearing.
 Quest. What say you then to a necessarie oath, as you call it, when a man is commaunded to sweare?
A necessarie oath.
Ans. According as I said before of a voluntarie oath, that if a magistrate commaund inferiour persons to sweare in a lawful matter, lawfully, vpon iust occasion, and when the thing is requisite, it is holy and lawfull on the magistrates part, and on his or their partes that sweare. If otherwise authority compell, and men yeeld to sweare in thinges vnlawfull, and without cause, they both sinne greatly. And I finde two speciall causes wherein a magistrate may commaund, and the inferiour person ought to take an oath by the word of God.
 Quest. What be those two cases in which a necessary oath is lawfull?
Ans. The first is when the superiour person or magistrate commaundeth the subiect and the inferiour person to sweare loyalty, allegeance, and fidelity to performe that which is his duety, as Abraham gaue his seruant charge to prouide a wife for his son Isaake, and caused him to sweare that he would deale faithfully, and according to the charge giuen him, Gen. 24.3. etc. Iaacob also vpon his death bed made Ioseph to sweare that he would bury him where his fathers were buried, and not in
Aegypt, Gen. 47.29.31. and 50.5. Ioseph made his brethren sweare, that they would bring their yongest brother Beniamin with them, when they came againe to buy more corne, Gen. 43.3. and a little before his death he made them sweare to cary his bones with them out of Aegypt, when God should deliuer them, Gen. 50.25. and Exod. 13.19. The king of Babel made Zedekiah king of Iudah to sweare alleageance to him, 2. Chro. 36.13. That good king of Iudah, Asa made all his subiectes to sweare that they would worship God, 2. Chro. 15.10.13.14. Thus the generall of the host taketh an oath of his souldiers. And thus kings cause their subiectes to sweare loyalty and obedience.
 The second is, when a man being brought before a magistrate by his accuser, is put to his oath to purge and cleare himselfe.
 Quest. Then if it be lawfull for a man to cleare himselfe of euery crime by his oath, it is to be feared lest many men will make shipwrake of a good conscience and forsweare themselues, if by their oath they may pay their debts, and escape all punishment. This seemes to me a strange doctrine and to giue to to much liberty to euil disposed men. Wherefore I pray you eyther open it more plainely or else proue it by scripture.
Ans. You say well, that if euery offender might purge himselfe by his oath, many great
inconueniences woulde follow. But it is not lawfull for a man in any cause or crime wherewith he is charged, to cleare himselfe by his oath. For the Lord hath set downe another lawe and an other order for triall of most matters, namely by witnesses, and not by oathes, Deut. 19.15. At the mouth of two witnesses, or at the mouth of three witnesses shall the matter be stablished, etc. Therefore a man may not purge himselfe by his oath in euery thing, but onely in some few speciall cases.
Quest. What be those cases wherein a mans oath may cleare him?
Ans. They are as I take it but onely two: the one, when a man deliuereth his neighbour any thing to keepe, and the thing be lost when it should be restored; then if the owner suspect that his neighbour whom he trusted with the keeping of it, hath deceiued him, and secretly by some meanes conueied it out of his house, and now saith he cannot tell what is become of it, or that it is stollen, then I say, in this case the owner may bring his neighbour before the magistrate, and shew that he suspectes him of fraud, and the magistrate shall put him to his oath. Which oath if he take and sweare by God that he knoweth not howe it went out of his house, or that it was stollen from him, that his oath shal cleare him, and the
owner shal accept of his oath, and be therewith content, and so that matter is ended. Exo. 22.7.8.
The other is, when a man deliuereth to his neighbour his beast to keepe for hire, as if a man hire a sheepheard or any other to keepe his beastes, if any of the beastes be hurt, or lost, or stollen, or deuoured by wild beastes, without any fraud or negligence in the keeper, then if the owner suspect the keeper eyther of fraud or negligence, but can proue neither against him, he may bring him before the magistrate. And if the keeper being put to his oath, will sweare that there was neither fraud nor negligence in him, his oath shall cleare him, he shall not make it good, the owner shal beare the losse, as it is, Exod, 22.10.11.12.13. And in both these two cases, in which a man may purge himselfe vpon his oath, it is worthy alwaies to be obserued, that if there be any witnesses to testifie either with them or against them, they are not to purge themselues by oath, but onely when no man can beare witnesse, as it is expresly said of the latter, Vers. 10. And no man see it. For when the trueth may be found out by the testimony of men, it is to take Gods name lightly and in vaine, to call him to witnesse. But onely when in these two cases no man can witnesse the innocency of these two persons, or conuince the latter of
fraude or negligence, or else the former of fraud onely, then is the suspected person permitted to cal God to witnes, who onely knoweth all his secrets, and so to purge himselfe.
 Quest. Is there then no other case, but these two only, in which a man may purge himself by his oth?
Ans. Because Paul saith, Rom. 14.23. whatsoeuer is not of faith is sinne, and because for my part I know no moe cases set downe in the word of God, therefore I suppose a man cannot cleare himselfe vpon his oath in any other cause. And in these two causes an oath is the ende of strife. In all other cases the matter must be tried by witnesses.
Quest. By whom must men sweare? 
Ans. By God onely, and by no other thing, Deut. 6.13. and 10.20. Esay. 65.16. For to sweare is to call him we sweare by to witnesse that we speake as our heart conceiueth, and so to make him the searcher of our heartes. But it is onely God that is the searcher of all mens heartes, 1. King. 8.39.
 Quest. What conditions are to be obserued in swearing?
Ans. The prophet Ieremy, Cap. 4.2. setteth downe three conditions. 1. In trueth. 2. In iudgment. 3. In righteousnes. In trueth, that is, both true things, not false things; and also truly with out fraud, guile, deceit, or shiftes, plainly and
simply. In iudgement, that is, soberly, aduisedly, when necessity requireth, not rashly as Herod did: see Leuit. 5.4. In righteousnes, that is, in things lawful and honest, not in things vnlawful, as those did which sware they wold neither eat nor drink til they had killed Paul. Act. 23.12.
 Quest. What if a man sweare rashly, and obserue not these three conditions; whether is he bound to performe his oath or no?
Ans. No, he ought not to performe it: but rather to repent betimes, then to ad a wicked deede to an vnlawfull oath. For that were to heap one sin vpon another. But if he repent him of his vnlawful oath, the Lord offereth mercy, Leui. 5.4.5.6. and 6.3.5. Num. 3.2.3. Notwithstanding if any man sweare to do a lawful thing he is bound to performe it, yea though there be discommodity in performing it, or if he was ouerseene, or compelled when he sware.
 Qu. What is the reason of this co^mandement?
Ans. The reason to perswade men to keepe this co^mandement, is that howsoeuer we flatter our selues and say we are innocent albeit we abuse Gods name, Deu. 29.19. yet the Lord the iudge of all will not pronounce vs guiltles and innocent at that day, when the secretes of all hearts shal be disclosed. And if the Lord pronounce vs then guilty, wo worth the time that euer we abused his name. But before the last
day of iudgment come, it is worth the reading to know what temporall plagues are prepared for false swearers, Zach. 5.4.
 Que. Then that we may haue more vse of this co^mandement, shew me who they be that break it
Ans. First, they that curse and sweare at euery word most blasphemously, as by the Lord, by God, by Iesus Christ, etc. or by any thing that is attributed or ascribed to God in the scripturs, as by his arme, his head, his ha^d, his blood his sides, his hart, his flesh, etc. either in earnest or in sport, as though it were a grace to sweare
 Secondly, they that sweare to do things vnlawful, as Saul sware to the witch that he would not put her to death, 1. Sam. 28.10. and that his sonne Ionathan shoulde die for eating hony when he was faint and weary and his sight beganne to faile him, 1. Sam. 14.39.44.
 Thirdly, they that commit periury, by swearing falsly, or fraudulently, or that they minde not to performe. Peter contrary to his knowledge sware that he knew not Christ, Mat. 26.72. and Saul sware that he minded not to perform, when he sware to Ionathan that he would not kill Dauid, 1. Sa. 19.6. Zedekiah performed not his oath to the king of Babel, Ezek. 17.16.18.19. Hatto the archbishop of Mentz co^mitted fraudulent periury when he sware to Adelbertus the Marquis of Bambarge, that he
would either make peace between him and Ludouicus the Emperour, or else bring him safe home againe. For with this traine did he get Adelbertus to go with him to the Emperour. And when they were set forward a little way on their iorney toward the Emperor, Hatto began to say he was hungry and the iourney was long, where upon Adelbertus requested him to returne and eate somwhat before they went any further. So they returned, and did eate and drinke. Thus the archbishop brought Adelbertus safe and sound home to his place again and therby thought himself discharged of his oath. And then afterward betraied him, and brought him to the Emperor, who immediatly put him to death Liuth prand. lib. 1. cap. 3. Vladislaus king of Poland, when he was chosen to be king of Bohemia brake the oath and league which that most worthy prince Iohn Huniad a little before had made with Amurathes the Turke; and through the means of pope Eugenius, and the instigation of that wretched Iulian the Cardinal, warring against the Turke, was slaine and a great number with him at Varna, as Paralipomena Vrspergensis do report, though Aeneas Siluius ashamed of such popish counsell, and such miseries as afterward happened to Christians in all those quarters bordering vpon the Turkes dominions, doth slilie
passe ouer so foule a thing, least he shoulde also shame that Romish chaire of pestilence. But this is a fruite of popish doctrine, when by their authoritie they commaund Christian princes to breake their oathes and promises that were lawfully made.
 Fourthly, they that vse to sweare indirectly as meaning to sweare by God, name the creatures of God, as the heauens, the earth, the sunne, breade; or the ordinances of God, as the Temple, the alter, the sacraments, and such like, which Christ reproueth Mat. 5.34. and 23.16. and the Apostle Iames Chap. 5.12.
 Fiftly, they that sweare by God and by Idols, making an vnlawful mixture, as Laban sware Gen. 31.53. The God of Abraham, and the God of Nahor, and the God of their fathers be iudge betweene vs. The God of Abraham was the true God, but the God of their father was an idol Iosh. 24.2. This sinne the prophet Zephaniah reproueth Chap. 1.5. them that sweare by the Lord, and sweare by Malcham. And Amos Chap. 8.14. They that sweare by the sinne of Samaria, which is as if he had saide by the sinne of Rome. For as the calues and other Idolatrie were the sinnes of Samaria: so is the masle and such like Idolatrie the sinne of Rome. wherefore when men sweare ordinarily; if I ought not rather
to say extraordinarely, by the masse, by the crosse, by the rood, by Peter, by Marie, by Anne, or by any other sinne of Rome, they commit the verie same sinne which Amos reproueth: for to sweare by these and such like Idols, it is not as willfull mad men say, to sweare them out of the country, but rather to sweare God out of the country, who will not deuide half of his honor to Idols, but haue it wholy ascribed to himselfe, and hath in plaine wordes forbid vs so much as to take the name of such Idols in our mouth Exod. 23.13. Ye shall make no mention of the name of other Gods; neither shall it be heard out of thy mouth, Ioshua Chap. 23.7. seriously admonisheth the Israelites hereof. Iereme Chap. 5.7. telleth the Iewes plainely that they forsake God by this kinde of swearing, and saith, Thy children haue forsaken me, and sworne by them that are no Gods.
And because men will sweare by Idols and so forsake God, and not suffer reproofe for it, that it may appeare such as feare God indeede, reproue not vnlawfull oathes of curiositie or captiousnes, but of conscience and of feare least by silence they should be guiltie thereof, who so list to reade Leuit. 5. in the beginning of the Chapter, shall see that the Lord maks them guilty of an oath, which
heare it and reproue it not.
But thus much of taking Gods name in vain by swearing vnlawfully. Diuers and sundry wayes is Gods name abused and taken in vain contrary to this commaundement without an oath, as First they that professe God and his religion, but in their liues prophane his comma^dements, in that they are talkers, but not doers of his law, of which sort there are whol swarmes at this day. Goe and consider all states and degrees and conditions of men, and thou shalt feele in thy heart that the Lord faith to euery one almost, what hast thou to doe to declare mine ordinances, that thou shouldest take my name in thy mouth (that is, that thou should take my name vpon thee and say thou art a Christian, thou art mine, and that thou belongest to me) Seing thou hatest to be reformed, and hast cast my words behinde thee? for when thou seest a theefe, thou runnest with him, and thou art partaker with the adulterers. Thou giuest thy mouth to euill, and with thy tongue thou forgest deceite etc. Psal. 50.16.17. etc. How many are there at this day which with their mouth professe they knowe God but by their workes denie him as Paul saith Tit. 1.16.
 Secondly, they that vnder color of religion
and of the name of God, commit horrible wickednes, as the sonnes of Iaacob did, when they slew the Sechemites. Gen. 34.13. etc. The Scribes and Pharisies vnder pretence of prayer deuoured widdowes howses Math. 23.14. Two horrible facts happenned of late yeares, the one at Holme in Sweeueland, when the king of Denmarke Christiernus the second by name, and a Christian by profession, through the craftie counsel and helpe of Gustauus archbishop of Vpsalis was peaceablie admitted into the citie with many ample conditions of peace and vnitie, whereto Christiernus did not only subscribe but also sweare. Neuerthelesse when he had refreshed him selfe and his soldiers a few dayes, he repaireth and contineweth for three dayes space a sumptuous and riotous feast for all the chiefe men of Holme, and the third day when there seemed to be least danger or feare, he apprehended them all, shut them vp in prison, and shut the gats of the citie that no man might come in or goe out, and then openly executed the chiefest men, and after let the souldiers loosse vpon all the citie, where such outragious cruelty was vsed, that no tongue is able to expres it, as Krantzius saith in describing it in a seuerall small treatise of this matter only. And
this was about the yere 1520. The other was at Paris in the yere 1572. August. 24. where vnder pretence of religion and peace, that worthie and noble man of France Gasper Colinius, and as many Christians as could be found, were murthered in such crueltie and horrible manner, as hath seldome or neuer beene heard of.
Thirdly, they that haue spirits of diuination or south saying, that is to say, familiars in them, as witches, charmers, coniurers, and such like haue, which the Lord forbideth Leuit. 20.27. And Deut. 18.10.11. Such as can tel men who haue stolen their horses, or other things: such as can vnwitch children or others that are bewitched, and can tel who bewitched them. And a greate number mo, as stargasers, astrologers, and prognosticators, as the prophet Esaias Chap. 47.13. calleth them, which can cast figures, tell natiuities, fortunes, and destinies; and are so excellently and so profoundly learned in the blacke art as it is called, that nothing comes amisse to hand but they can diuine by it, as by the hand, by fire, by water, by the earth by the aire, by siues or ridles, by flying or crying of birdes. Yea and that the world may see their skilfull vanitie, I meane Impietie, they can for neede diuine by smoake
or by a shadow. Neither doe they take vpon them to be Lords ouer mens bodies only, but they can temper their mindes also at their pleasure. And that which farre surpasseth all other things, they can tell the destinies and reade the fortunes of shippes, of houses, of cities, as Tarutias Firmanus found that Rome was borne in the eclipse of the moone, when Romulus laide the foundation, and thereupon would vndertake to read her destinie, as if the heauens had such a mightie operation in boardes, in timber, in iron, in tiles, brickes, stones, morter, daube, clay, straw, and whatsoeuer. This is a singular and a rare skill, of which such fooles boast, as though no man knew anithing but they only. Now if a man might haue leaue to pose them, and know the profounditie of their art, he should finde it a painted building whithout any foundation at all to rest vpon, and so hang by the heauens, as Mahomets tombe doth or heretofore did (as the report goeth) hange by the Loadestone at Mecha in Arabia the stony. And if a man consider either the ground of their art, or the effect of their prognostications, their learning will appear what it is. And first, what demonstration can they make of their art? (I speake not now of witches etc. but of greate astrologers
as they would be counted) whence haue they their names of the twelue signes of the zodiake, of fiue of their planets, and of the fixed starres? what is the nature and qualitie of each of them? If al astrologers that heretofore haue liued could not yet for all their learning make so much as one small demonstration to shew the ground and truth of their art, as learned men haue doone, and dayly doe in all trew liberall arts, it is a token that this Astrologie is a bastard, and hath no place among lawfull and trew artes. If the names that be giuen to the starres, and the properties ascribed to them be childish and ridiculous, or else supersticious and irreligious, as the^ selues know, there is no reason why we should beleeue them. The fiue planets Saturne, Iupiter, Mars, Venus, Mercurie, whence haue they their names? Are they not called by the names of most wicked, vile, and execrable persons that sometimes liued beastlike vpon the earth, and now for their vilanies are honored as Gods of heathen people which know not the trew God of Israell? And haue they not such qualities ascribed to them, as these wicked wretches were of, whose names they beare? If it be dema^ded why any of these planets should be of such nature as they affirme, they are at their
wittes ende. Likewise for the names and natures of the twelue signes. But it were too tedious to rehearse them, let the astrologer consider them, and how vaine they are. Also for the effectes of their diuinations and destinies it needeth not to say much. For first of although they professe much, yet they are daintie or rather warie of their skil, and in that point shew some wisdome, because they will not easily diuine and prognosticate. Secondly when they doe diuine, they speake obscurely, or doubtfully, or with exception, as hauing guiltie consciences, and fearing for shame to be taken in a lye. And so did Apollo, Iupiter Ammon and others in their oracles, that herein it may appeare whose scholers they are. Thirdly when impudencie makes them to diuine in playner speaches without any ambiguitie, the world is witnesse what liers they be. Tully in his seco^d booke de diuinatione sayth, that he hearde these wise astrologers prophesie much prosperitie and many prosperous yeares to Pompeius, to Crassus and to Iulius Caesar, all which prooued to be false. So many astrological prognostications as haue beene publissed in our dayes are so many witnesses of the falshoode of diuining astrologie, as sometimes one contrary to another, and yet both false.
And I maruell they do not remember tha^ pleasant iest of a philosopher, Mirabile vide turquod non rideat haruspex cum haruspicem viderit: It is a wonder that one of these astrologers can forbeare laughter, when he looketh vpon an other astrologer. The knowledge of the heauens for such vse as God appointed them, Gen. 1.14. is the good gift of God, and commendable as it may appeare throughout the booke of Iob, and by daily practise in kalenders, in dials, in nauigation, in Chronicles, in daies, weekes, moneths, yeares, and seasons. But this diuining astrologie is without reason, and condemned by the word of God in the places before cited. Wherefore I wish all prognosticators of things to come by vertue of astrologie (for I take the word as it is commonly vsed, and as it is diuers from astronomie) that because astrologie is void of reason, condemned by the scriptures, and hath no lawfull or good vse among men, they would follow tho examples of those we reade of, Act. 19.18.19. and confesse their vanitie, shewe their workes, and burne their bookes at Paules crosse.
 Fourthly, they that goe to these destinie readers, witches, sorcerers, inchanters, astrologers, or coniurers, to haue their children, or their cattell vnbewitched, to know who hath
stollen their horse, or hurt them any, or else to know their fortune, or aske their counsell in any thing according to that profession. For whiles they are going toward such persons for counsel they may remember that when the messengers of Ahaziah were on their iourney going to Baal-zebub to knowe whether their king should recouer of his disease, Elijah the Thisbite met them and saide, Is it not because there is no God in Israell, that ye go to enquire of Baal-zebub the God of Ekron, 2. King. 1.6. And they that goe to such persons for counsell, do shew openly that they say in their heartes, there is no God in England. They also that goe of curiositie to see if there be any such skill in them, as though they would go to take acquaintance of the diuell. They also that vse such medicines, and such ceremonies as these wise men and wise women prescribe them. Also shipmasters who dare not put out of their port, and beginne their voyage vpon certaine daies, as vpon twese day, or friday, least it should proue vnluckie. And therefore they are often carefull to make choyse of a luckie day, euen the Lordes day, that by breaking the Lordes sabaoth in the beginning, they may haue good lucke afterward.
 Quest. What is the punishment for them that breake this commandement?

Ans. It is death, Leuit. 24.16. He that blasphemeth the name of the Lorde shalbe put to death: all the congregation shall stone him to death, etc. whereof there is an example, Leuit. 24.12. etc. Num. 15.32. etc.
Remember the Sabaoth day, to keep it holy, etc. vers. 8.
 Quest. What is the summe of this fourth commaundement?
Ans. There are three thinges to be considered in it. First the commaundement, vers. 8. Secondly, the exposition, vers. 9.10. Thirdly, the reason, vers 11.
 Quest. What is the meaning of the commaundement?
Ans. The commaundement is short, and my purpose is to ioyne the exposition to it, to make but one speach of both, though I haue seuerally noted the distinct parts. And first note that the Lord comming with authoritie to commaund, doth in this commaundement only say, Remember, wheras in all the other he vseth authoririe and absolutely commaundeth. The reasons whereof may be three. 1. First, though all the commaundementes were giuen before, and knowen to the faithful, as partly by the secret worke of God grauen in their nature, and partly giuen by expresse commaundement,
as for example, the first commaundement was giuen to Adam, Gen. 2. and 3. and to Abraham, Gen. 12.1.2.3. and 17.1. the second was likewise giuen to Adam, and accordingly he taught his children to worship God aright, Gen. 4.3.4. and also Abraham, Gen. 12.7. the third commaundement is manifestin the lawfull vse of it, Gen. 14.22.23. and 21.23.24.31: this fourth was giuen. Gen. 2.3. the fifth appeareth in the sonnes of Adam, Gen. 4. and of Noah, Gen. 9.22.23. the sixt, Gen. 9.6. the seauenth appeareth, Gen. 20.3.26.9. in the godly care which Abraham had for the lawfull mariage of Isaak, Gen. 24. and that Isaak had for Iaacob. Gen. 27.46. and 26.1.6. and in the incest, and iudgement of Iudah, Gen. 38.18.24. the eight was well knowen, as we may see, Gen. 31.19.26.32.37.39. the ninth is manifest in the breach of it, Gen. 37.32. and 39.14.17. etc. The tenth being as it were the root from whence the breach of the other commandements springs, must needs also be know en, though it be so secret a sinne, and so deeply hid in nature that there are no examples of it eyther before or after the law giuen, although there may be some glimse of it in Iosephs mistresse, Gen. 39.8.9. though all these commandements, I say, were giuen before, yet the Israelites were growen into that obliuion of
them all in a manner, that the Lord repeating them againe, Exod. 20. speaketh with authoritie and commaundeth as though they had neuer beene giuen, or knowen, or heard of before, and least they should be forgotten againe, putteth them now in writing. But this fourth co^mandement was better kept in memory, and in practise, then any of the rest, and was but a little before repeated, Exod. 16.22.23.25.26. Therefore the Lord saith now but onely Reme^ber, as if he had said, concerning the saboth you know it verie well, and I gaue you commandement to obserue it but the other day, therefore see that ye remember it. 2. Secondly, as men giuing their sonnes or seruantes diuers thinges in charge, say of some principall matter, remember this, and though thou forget other thinges, yet in any case remember this: so the Lord, to let vs know what reckoning he maketh of the sabaoth, saith Remember the Sabaoth especially, forget it not. 3. Thirdly, he admonisheth vs of our carelesnesse and forgetfulnesse in the best thinges, when he saith Remember, as if he said, knowe thine owne slownes and dulnes, and keepe in mind my sabaoth, that thou forget it not.
 Qu. Seeing you haue giuen sufficient reason for the manner of speach in the first word, Reme^ber, I pray you go forward with the co^mandement.

Ans. The commaundement now standeth of two sentences: first, Remember the sabaoth day, secondly, to keepe it holy.
 Quest. Which, or what call you the sabaoth?
Ans. The Lord sheweth it himself in the exposition, vers. 9. and in the beginning of ver. 10. that it is the seauenth day, euen euery seauenth day, that is the Sabaoth day, that is to say, the day of rest, as if the Lord had said, euery seauenth day thou shalt rest.
 Que. Had the Iewes any other sabaoth daies, or daies of rest, that it was necessary thus to pointe out the seauenth day?
Ans. They had many saboths, ordaies and times of rest: as first euery seauenth day which is heere commanded, and Leuit. 23.3. then the first day of euery month, as it may be collected out of Num. 10.10. and 28.11.14. and 29.6. and as it is manifest, Psal. 81.3.4. Ezr. 3.5. Besides these two sabaoths of daies and moneths, they had euery yeare fiue sabaoths, as first the pasouer, the 14. day of the first moneth, Exod. 12.15. and 13.3. and 23.15. Leuit. 23.5. The second is the feast of haruest, or of Pentecost, or of Whit sontide, which was full seauen weeks after the pasouer, Ex. 23.16.34.22. Le. 23.15. Thirdly in the seauenth moneth they had three feasts, or sabaoths, as the first day of the seauenth moneth was the feast of blowing trumpets,
Leuit. 23.24. Num. 29.1. the tenth day of the same moneth was a fourth sabaoth, euen the day of reconciliation, wherein they were commanded to fast and reconcile themselues to God, Lenit. 23.27. and 16.29. Exo. 30.10. Nu. 29.7. Lastly the fift feast was the fifteenth day of the seauenth moneth, euen the feast of tabernacles in the end of their ciuil yeare when they had gathered in their fruites, Exod. 23.16 and 34.33. Leuit. 33.34.39. Also they had two other great sabaoths of yeares, the first was euery seauenth yeare, Exod. 23.10. Leui. 25.2.3. Deu. 15.1.9. etc. the second was euery fiftith yeare. Leuit. 25.8.
 Qu. Now I perceiue the seauenth day is the sabaoth or day of rest, which is here co^manded. But what is the reason why our sabaoth or day of rest is not the seauenth, but the first day of the weeke?
Ans. There was somthing ceremonial in this commaundement, as the Apostle witnesseth, Colos. 2.16.17. which was abolished at Christs comming as all other ceremonies were, in so much that Paul reproueth the Galatia^s for obseruing the sabaoth before named, Gal. 4.10. and that is the cause why we obserue it not now.
Q. I pray you what was ceremonial in the 7. day? 
Ans. I might giue you a short and ful answer in one word, and say; that wheras al the ceremonies of the Iewes were instituted either for order, or for signification, those which belong to order
generally (for such as were for particular order of that time, that place, and those people, are abolished) do remain and must co^tinually remain for edification and for comely and decent order, as Paul would haue al such indifferent things to be ordred. 1. Cor. 14.26.40. and the other significant ceremonies are abrogated. But because this answer is more general, the^ that euery one can make ful vse of, I wil specifie some particulars, which we haue no vse of, neither may haue. Significa^t ceremonies in respect of time are threefold, and some are remembrances of things past, some are as it were pictures to set forth things present, and others are types and figures of things to come.
 First the saboth was ceremonial, in that it was a reme^brance of the lords rest the seauenth day fro^ creating any more, and this ceremony is ceased. For though it is our duties at this day connually to reme^ber the power and goodnes of God in creating heauen and earth with all the host of them, and in resting the seuenth day: yet the sabaoth or seuenth day of the week is not appointed to vs at this day to cal that to our reme^brance, but as Paul plainly sheweth there was accremony in the seuenth day of the week Gan. 4.10. Col. 2.17. so we see the abrogation of it approued by the spirit of God, and the first day of the weeke chosen in steed thereof, Act. 20.7.1. Cor. 16.2. which is called the lords day, Apo. 1.10

Secondly, the sabaoth was ceremonial in that it was a signe and token to teach the Iewes that the Lorde did sanctifie them Exod. 13.13. Eccle. 20.20. For when according to Gods commaundement they rested so strictly from all kinde of ciuill workes that they might not gather Manna, nor bake nor boile their meate that day, Exod. 16.23.25.26.29. nor kindle a fire Exod. 35.3. nor pretend any necessitie to worke in most necessarie things, as in the building of the Tabernacle Exod. 31.13, or most necessarie times, as in seede-time or in haruest Exod. 34.21. which precise rest was full 24. houres, from euen to euen Leuit. 23.32. When, I say they rested thus precisely from al ciuil labour, they yeelded themselues wholy into the Lords hands, and to his will, that he might worke his will, euen their sanctification. For as the patient standeth, sitteth, or lieth stil as a stone without wagging hand or foote whiles the surgeant or phisician is working vpon him to cure him: so the Iewes resting from their owne workes so strictly, gaue themselues without resistance into the handes of God the Phisician of their saluation, that he might that day worke vpon them outwardly by his word and such ordinances as he had appointed, and inwardly by his blessed
Spirit to sanctifie them, for thus the Lorde doth sanctifie his elect, Iohn 17.17. Now though we be thus sanctified at this day, yet we haue not this vaile of the sabbath to shadow it vnto vs, but the shadow being taken away, we haue all things plainely declared to vs without parables.
 Thirdly, the verie day itselfe, the seauenth and no other precisely appointed to rest in, and to meditate of heauenly things, was to signifie that there ought to be one of seauen daies appointed for Gods worship; and to signifie that spirituall rest from sin into which we that beleeue are alreadie entred, Heb. 4.3.10. for in Christ Iesus we haue peace, righteousnes, and life,
 Quest. Whether are we commaunded so precisely to worke six dayes, that it is simply euill to rest from labour and to serue God any of those sixe?
Ans. This question seemeth to me so intricate, that I cannot answere it in one word as I would. For it is a needelesse question in respect of many masters, who are so farre from resting any of the sixe dayes, that they will not rest the seauenth, nor suffer their serua^ts or their cattel to rest. Many others do nothing els sixe dayes, yea and the seauenth also but rest vpon the alebench at cardes, tables,
dice. Some rest after the same manner in their owne howses all the yere longdiuers young gentlemen are brought vp to no other worke and that they ply night and day so earnestly that they haue scarse leasure to sleepe till they haue plaide away the lands and reuenewes which their parents left them. But to touch your question nearer, the Lord that bounde man to perpetuall labour as a punishment for his sinne, and commanded him to get his liuing with the sweate of his browes, doth not forbid him to lift vp his eyes to heauen to worshippe his maker. Neither was this commaundement of laboring six dayes giuen before the sabboth or together with it but after it, that whereas man was to serue his creator continually (the earth without labour and toyle yeelding her fruits) and specially the seauenth day, the Lordes meaning in bidding him to worke sixe dayes was to tell him that without his labour the earth would not giue her increase, and not to forbid him to worship God at any time. For the more earnest the people haue bene to serue God, the more hath the earth yeelded her fruite, and with lesse laboure Malach 3.10. Also you heard before that the Lord himselfe appointed the Iewes diuers sabbaths besides the seauenth day. And the Iewes
themselues at diuers times, and for sundry causes rested from ciuil labour, and kept sabbaths to the Lord, as 1. Sam. 7.6. And Dauid with al Israel kept a sabbath first when he brought the Arke of God out of the house of Abinadab, and secondly when he brought it out of the house of Obed-Edom. 2. Sam. 6. At the dedication of Salomons Temple they kept a sabbath or rest of seauen dayes long 1. king. 8.65. After their returne out of Captiuity they kept many sabbaths, as when the foundation of the Temple was laide Ezr. 3.8.10. at the dedciation of it when it was finished Ezr. 6.15.16. at the dedication of the wall of Ierusalem Nehem. 12.27. When they were deliuered from that death which Haman conspired against them Ester. 9.17.18.20.21. And at diuers other tymes, as it appeareth Ezr. 10.7.9.13. etc. Nehem. 8.18. Zach. 8.19. The primitiue Church likewise kept diuers sabbaths besides the Lords day, as commemorations of Martyrs Cypryan. Lib. 3. Epist 6. Beatus Rhenanus in Lib. Tertul ad Martyres. The feast of Easter, as we call it, the feast of Pentecost which at the first lasted fiftie dayes continually after Easter, but afterward was turned to whitsontide only as Ierome writeth in Galat. 4. The natiuitie of Christ. Constantine
the greate commaunded euery friday to be a sabbath or day of rest to the Lord Enseb: Lib. 4. de vita Constant. and Sozom. Li. 1. Chap. 8. 
 Quest. What is there more to be obserued concerning the sabboth or day of rest?
Ans. There is one thing more in the exposition which may not be omitted, euen this, that the sabbath or day of rest is to the Lord, that is, we may not rest that day to any creature, but only to the Lord. Which I note, first because heathens keepesabbaths to Idols, but specially because of the papists, who imitating the heathen, first consecrated deade men for Gods, as hath beene saide before in the 1. and 2. commaundements, and secondly appointed sabbaths for their new Gods. It is therefore saide in this comma^dement, that our sabbath must be kept holy to the Lord, not to any heathenish or popish Idol.
 Quest. What then if such a day be appointed by the Church to be a sabbath or day of rest to the Lord, as sometimes the Pope appointed to be a sabbath to one of his new Gods? doe you thinke it vnlawfull to keepe it to the Lord?
Ans. No, I doe not say so, I wish, and it were greatly to be desired, if it might be, that sabbaths appointed for the Lord were vpon
other dayes, that so all shew of euill might be auoided. But it is a thing not possible, except we should keepe no sabbaths to the Lord saue only the Lords day: for the Popes of Rome haue made so many new gods as there are dayes in the yere, as you may see in the kalender there is not one spare day. Yea and of later years the Pope hath bene put to his shiftes to get a day for some of his new made Gods: and because he was not able with all his keyes to make one day moe in the yere, he hath beene faine to blot out of the kalender, one of his ould gods, that his new god might put in his foote.
 Quest. You saide before that this commaundement consisted of two sentences, wherof you haue declared the former, wherefore I pray you now shew me the other also, and how we must sanctifie the sabbath?
Ans. We must sanctifie it so as the Lord hath commaunded. But to speake plainelie and briefely, I will follow the order here obserued, and shew first, what is to be doone that day, for it is saide, to keepe it holy: and secondly what may not be doone, for it is saide in the exposition, thou shalt not do any worke etc.
 Quest. How then must we keepe it holy?
Ans. I will shew it you by the practice, first
of the Iewes and secondly of Christians.
 First of all the Iewes had a holy conuocation according as they were commaunded: Leuit. 23.3. Six dayes shall worke be doone, but on the seauenth day shalbe the sabbath of rest, an holy conuocation etc.
Therefore the Iewes assembled themselues together that day both at Ierusalem, and in their seuerall synagogues which they had for that purpose in euery citie Psal. 74.8. Act. 15.21.
 Secondly, they had the law and the prophets read and expounded Leuit, 10.11. Nebem. 8.8. Act. 13.15.
 Thirdly, they had their sacrifices and other ceremonies Num. 28.9.
 Fourthly, they offred some thing willingly 2. king. 12.4.9. Mark. 12.41.
 Fiftly, they had prayer Psal. 141.2. Luk. 9.10. Num. 6.24.
The exercise of the Christians, and how they keepe holy the day of rest, apeareth to be answerable to the custom of the Iewes, but without ceremonies, for that they had their assemblyes vpon the Lords day it appeareth Act. 20.7. and 1. Cor. 16.2. and for the other foure, yea rather all those fiue thinges which we noted afore to be obserued of the Iewes, are mentioned, but without ceremonies
of the law, in one place, Act. 2.4. And they (being assembled) continued in the Apostles doctrine, and fellowship, and breaking of breade, and prayers. For first they were assembled; secondly they had the Apostles doctrine, that is, the ould testament and the new red and expounded, as may be shewed 1. Cor. 14. thirdly, they had fellowship, euen such as the Apostles taught them, that is, they did communicate their earthly things as euery one had neede, and the richer relieued the poorer: for so Paul ordeined in the churches 1. Cor. 16.1.2. fourthly, they had breaking of breade, that is, the administration of the Lords supper; fiftly, they had prayers. And thus was the day of rest sanctified.
 Quest. What is then forbidden to be done vpon the day of rest?
Ans. He saith, thou shalt not doe any work, Where you must note the persons, which are borbidden to labour about any ciuill worke that day. Thou, that art a king, a magistrat, afather, a maister, or any other superiour. Also thy sonne, thy daughter etc. Where two things are to be obserued: First that there is no libertie graunted more to the superiour then to the inferiour, to the greate then to the smal, to one then to another, but all of
what state or condition soeuer must sanctifie the Lordes day. Secondly that euery superiour standeth charged before God, not onely for himselfe, but also for those which the Lord hath put vnder his gouernment, that both he and they all sanctifie the Lordes sabaoth or day of rest. Both which lessons are very needfull to be often remembred in these our daies, because some men thinke themselues exempted from keeping the sabaoth, and others thinke they are to care for none but for themselues onely.
 Quest. Doe you precisely stand vpon the wordes, that we must doe no worke at al that day? There is mention made of a sabaoths daies tourney, Act. 1.12. whereby it seemeth there euer was and now is liberty to doe some thinges that day. What say you to this?
Ans. A sabaoths daies iourney was not a commandement from God, but a superstitious tradition of the Iewes, which by their traditions prophaned and abused the worde of God as Christ sheweth largly, Mat. 5.21.27.33.38.43 and 15.3. etc. 23.16. etc. But the meaning of the Lord is, that no ciuill worke should be done that day, whereby the godly ciuill pollicie should be violated, the worship of God neglected, and the commuandement of GOD trode vnder foot. For otherwise the Iewes did
many thinges vnder the law, and diuers things are lawful for vs that we may do the^. The Iews went to the Temple at Ierusalem that day, or else to their seuerall synagogues, according to their dwellings, some were further off, and some were nearer, but none brake the sabaoth in going to the ordinarie place of the assemblie, though he dwelt two or three howers iourney off. For they counted the distance of places more by their iournies, then by miles or such other measures. The priestes and Leuites were occupied that day busilie in killing, dressing, washing, burning of the sacrifices with incense, and such other exercises as belonged to the sabaoth. The people they also brought their cattell that day to Ierusalem to be sacrificed with such other thinges as belonged thereto, and yet brake not this commandement. Wherefore this may be set down for a generall rule both vnder the Lawe and vnder the Gospell, that workes of pietie and religion in Gods worship all are lawfull to be done, yea necessarie that they must be done vpon the sabaoth daie. Furthermore, vnto this I will adde two other generall rules, of which this is the first. That is lawfull to be done vpon the Lordes sabaoth, which necessitie vrgeth and compelleth men to doe. As for example, the Apostles constrained
with hunger plucked the eares of corne rubbed them in their handes, and did eate the corne vpon the day of rest, and yet polluted not the sabaoth, for Christ defendeth their doing to be lawfull, Math. 12.3. etc. Marke. 2.27. And who is he that will not drawe his sheepe that day out of a ditch, to saue it? And much more is mans life to be preserued. The second generall rule is this. Whatsoeuer charitie doeth specially require and presently, that may be done vpon the day of rest without breach of this commandement, as Christ healed him that had the withered hand vpon the sabaoth day, Math, 12.10.11. and the woman that had beene bowed together eighteene yeares, Luke. 13.12. and said it was as much charitie to loose her from Satans bonds on the sabaoth, as to loose an oxe from the stalle and leade him to the water. For the sabaoth was made for man, and not man for the sabaoth, Marke. 2.27. Wherefore whatsoeuer religion commandeth, or necessitie vrgeth, or charity craueth that day, the same may and must be done vpon the sabaoth. Then to visite the sicke, or others in destresse, to comfort them, to make their beds, to cure them, and diuers such charitable and necessarie workes may that day be done, yet so that neither godly pollicy and order be violated,
nor Gods worship neglected.
 Quest. I pray you shew me then who they are that breake this commandement?
Ans. There are so many that I cannot reckon the hundreth part of them, yet I will name a few; as, First, they that would bring vs backe againe to the beggerly ceremonies of the olde law, which are abolished, and would haue vs to keep the Iewes sabaoth. The Ebionites obserue it, Euseb. lib. 3. cap. 27. and others after them in so much that the counsell of Laodicea, Can. 29. forbad it more then 300. yeares after Christ. And at this day some men curiously trouble themselues and others about it. Contrariwise they who woulde haue no saboath or day of rest at all, but say all daies are alike sabaothes. For though one day be no better then another, yet there is and euer hath beene, by the Lordes appointment, one speciall day of seauen for the publike worship of God, which we also ought religiously to keepe holy.
 Secondly, they that forsake the assembly of the congregation that day, as too too many do. Some find fault with the ministery and ministers as if they were not of God: others haue no tast at all of the goodnes of the word of God, and therefore carelesly contemne the congregation, and lie in their beds, or sit idle, or are occupied
in their own affaires, or walk into the fields for recreation, or go looke to their ground and to their cattell, or spend the time at cardes and dice and drinking in the alehouse, or runne after plaies, pipings, dancings, or other points of sinfull felowship with a greate number moe which that day aboue all other daies in the weeke follow hard after great sinnes and that with greedinesse. And these ought to be excommunicated, if vpon due admonishment they amend not.
Thirdly, of them that come to the Church, it woulde make a godly Christians heart to bleede, to see the dishonor that is done to God that day, and to tremble for feare of the iudgements that hang ouer their heades for such disobedieuce and misdemeanor in Gods presence, that he may say with Dauid, Psal. 119. vers. 53. Feare is come vpon me for the wicked, that forsake thy lawe, and vers. 136. Mine eies gush out with riuers of water, because the keepe not thy lawe. For some come so late and goe away againe so soone, that it is all one as if they had not beene there.
Some come of custome. Some behaue themselues so vnreuerentlie as if they came to the market, or rather as if they came among some idle companie where they might take a nappe, seeing that for worldlie cares which runne in their
heades, they could not sleepe of all the last nightlong. Some come for fashion and sit like sottes, and ve haue no more of them but onely their bodily presence, they cannot tell what was said, or what they did there, but only that they went for company.
Other to shew their pride. Some come to shew themselues in their braue apparrell, in their proud lookes, in their loftie countenance, in their stately going, in their tripping and mincing after the same manner that Esaias the Prophet speaketh of Chap. 3.16. etc. And if their wanton eyes, their hautie lookes, with all their pride and brauerie be noted of others and talked of at dinner, O then it is well with them, then they haue their desire, euen the thing for which they went to the Church, then are the merrie and glad.
Others to intrappe the minister. Some come to the Church, as the Scribes and Pharisies came to heare Christ, to marke the minister that they may intangle him in his words, to watch whether he weare the surplus or not; if he doe weare it, some will not heare but goe away againe presently, againe if he doe not weare it, other will not heare him. And so the minister is watched on each hande, and had neede to desire wisedome of the Lord to walke holily in the middest of such a froward generation. Some come to heare
some strange doctrine, that is, some strange newes, (as if it were at Venice, which Citie is now giuen to heare nothing but newes, as sometimes Athens was, Act. 17.21.) and if they heare nothing but Iesus Christ purely and plainely preached, and such holy and holsome words as they haue heard before, they thinke they haue lost their labour. And these men are more puffed vp with an ambitious desire of bare knowledge, then inwardely touched with any zeale, feeling, or religious minde.
Some com for pleasure. Some looke that the preacher shoulde tickle their itching eares with an eloquent oration, and care not to haue their soules cured, which are grieuously wounded with many grosse sinnes. Some that come are such as the Prophet Hoseas speaketh of, Chap. 4.4. Thy people are as they that rebuke the priest. For one saith the minister wantes learning; an other saith he wantes vtterance, and hath no grace at all in his speach; an other saith hee vtters manie wordes but no matter; an other saith he is a flatterer and hath no conscience; another sayeth hee is so zealous that he forgettes himselfe, or is halfe madde as Paul was, Actes. 26.24. another saith hee speakes of the splene, and of malice noteth mee. And all these knowe not, nay
they will not knowe that there are diuersities of giftes, but the same spirite which distributeth to euerie man seuerally as he will, and that no man can say that Iesus is the Lorde but by the holie Ghost, 1. Corin. 12.3.4.11. Neyther doe they knowe that they themselues are like children sitting in the markets, which call vnto their fellowes, and say, We haue piped vnto you, and ye haue not daunced; we haue mourned vnto you, and ye haue not lamented, Math. 11.17. Some come to the Church but they hate Micheah, and heare him with ill will,
1. King. 22. because he neuer preacheth good vnto them, but euill: and therefore will not haue such to preach vnto them, (Mich. 2.6.) but get them an heape of teachers after their owne lustes, 2. Tim. 4.3. Some will come in the forenoone, and thereby thinke they haue pleasured God as greatly as if they had done some popish supererogant worke, but in the afternoone they will make themselues a dispensation though they neuer come at the Pope for it, and goe a sporting, or sit at Cardes and Tables or such like exercise. But for all their dispensations and liberties let them heare what the Lorde saith, Leuit. 23.32. From euen to euen shall ye celebrate your sabbaoth.
Some will come to the sermon but not to prayer,
Som com^ by halfes. others will come to prayer but not to the sermon. Some will come both to prayer and to the sermon, but if the Lords supper be administred, they wilbe gone, for either they are not (as the common vaine excuse is) or they will not be prepared for it. But let all that feare God truly heare what the Lord saith to the Iewes concerning the passeouer Exod. 12.47. All the congregation of Israell shall obserue it. And Numb. 9.13. The man that is cleane, and is not in a iourney, and is negligent to keepe the passeouer, the same person shallbe cut off from his people etc For the sacrament of the Lords supper a proportionable reason may be taken from the passeouer, and Paul wisheth the Corinthians to tarie one for another, 1. Cor. 11.33. But because I will not stand here to bring reasons to make it manifest, I referre the reader to that most worthie and religious smal book written by the Iewel of England, M. Iewel his apologie, a booke worthie of greater co^mendation then I am able to giue vnto it: in which as in the defence thereof, which should be in euerie Church, he sheweth that all the congregation ought to celebrate the Lords supper together, and that whosoeuer negligently or co^temptuously withdraweth himselfe,
to be excommunicated. Some gouernours of housheholdes come themselues to the Church, but they let their families, sons, daughters and seruants runne at random which way they will, or else send them about worldly busines. Some come in deede to the congregation, but so soone as they are out of the Church doore, their mouthes are full of cursing, swearing, contention, malice, and such lewde talke as they vsed before, which is a foule token they gaue smale reuerence to God in the Church. And if a man would enter further into this matter, he should finde moe abhominations. Now seeing there are so many vnprofitable commers to the Church, besides them that heare the word, but follow it not, and whome Christ compareth to him that builds his house vpon the sande Math. 7.26. it is not like the number should be greate of those which sincerely keepe and sanctifie the Lords sabbath aright. And among many other causes of Gods wrath, this is not the least, whie these diuers yeares past for eight or ten the Lord hath sent euery yere a new and strange kind of sickenesse, such as neither we nor our forfathers haue knowen, and why in the yere 1593. the Lord sent such a terrible plague and pestilence as amazed all, and slew many, and
made all nations round about vs a greate way of, afraide of our companie; and why we haue had vnseasonable weather and great dearth of almanner of foode these diuers yeares, whereas before the land was so blessed with al maner of plentie that we releiued many forren countries. And because neither the word nor the iudgements of God haue yet driuen vs to some such rare kinde of publike repentance as our sinnes require, the Lord looketh for, and others in former tymes haue vsed, as in the dayes of Iehosaphat, of Ezra, of Nehemia, but we continue in our sinnes, or rather wax worse and worse, therefore behold the hand of the Lord is still stretched out against vs, that we had neede to say with Ieremie Chap. 9.1. O that our heades were ful of water, and our eyes fountaines of teares, that we might weepe day and night etc. For if we accept not the condition offred vs Ieremie 17, 21. we shall certainely tast of the Iudgment denounced Vers. 27.
 Fourthly, they offend against this commandement, who take away the maintenance of the ministery. For where mainteinance is wanting, there can be no minister, and where there is no minister, there is no sanctifying of the sabbath, reade Malach. 3.10.
Quest. What is the punishment which is
appointed for him that transgresseth this commaundement?
Ans. It is death Exod. 31.14. He that defileth it (that is, the sabbath) shall die the death etc. He. that gathered stickes that day was put to death Num. 15.32.
Honour thy father and thy mother etc. Vers. 12. Q What is the summe of the fift co^mandement? 
Ans. Hitherto you heard the commaundements of the first table, which teach vs our duties to God: now followeth the seconde table wherein our duties towards our neighbour are conteined. But yet this is to be obserued, that when the duetie is performed to man, the obedience is giuen to God, who commaundeth vs to performe these dueties to our neighbours. Of all the commaundements of the second table this first onely is affirmatiue, the other fiue following are al negatiues. This first conteineth in these two things, first the co^mandeme^t, seco^dly a reason or a promise. The summe of the comma^dement is to honour our parents, which if it be duely obserued, it is a marueilous help for the keeping of the rest. For this well obserued, we cannot easilie breake the rest.
 Quest. Whome doe you call our Parents?
Ans. All our superiours may be called our parents, and that either by nature, or by
age or by office.
Quest. Whome call you our Parents by nature? whome by age? and whome by office?
Parents by nature.
Ans. They are our Parents by nature, which are the Parents of our bodies, and of whome we are begotten and borne, and these are so called in the scripture, as you may se a large catalogue of Parents and of their sons Gen. 5. and. 10.11. and in the 10. first Chapters of the first booke of Chronicles, and Luke. 3.23. etc.
Parents by age. They are our fathers by age, which are our elders in yeares. For thus speaketh Steuen hauing respect to the diuers ages of all that were present Act. 7.2. ye men, brethren, and fathers, hearken. And Paul giueth this admonition to Timothe, and saith 1. Tim. 5.1.2. Rebuke not an elder, but exhort him as a father and the yonger men as brethren, the elder women as mothers etc.
They are our Parents by office,
Parents by office. whom the Lord hath set ouer vs in any authoritie, as magistrates ouer all their subiectes, ministers ouer their flockes, husbands ouer their wiues, maisters ouer their seruants. Magistrates they are fathers of their Countries and of all that be put vnder them, specially of the fatherlesse, of the Widdowes and of the poore. Machir of the tribe of Manasses being Prince of Galead, Numbers 32.39. is called
the father of Gilead 1. Chro: 2.21.23. Ashur the prince, is called the father of Tekoa 1. Chro. 2.24. and 4.5. read also 1. Chro: verse: 42.45, 49.50.51.52. Iob saith I was a father vnto the poore Iob, 29.16. The Lord saith of Eliakim the sonne of Hilkiah, and he shalbe a father of the inhabitants of Ierusalem, and of the house of Iudah Esai. 22.21. Ministers are likewise called fathers in the scriptures. Micas saith to the Leuite Iudg. 17.10. dwell with me, and be vntome a father and a priest. The Danities afterward saide to the same Leuite Iudg. 18.19. Come with vs to be our father and priest. When Eliiah was taken vp into heauen, Elisha cryed saying 2. king. 2, 12. My father, my father. The king of Israell saide to Elisha, My father, shall I smite them? 2. king. 6.21. When Ezechiah fell sicke of his sicknes, whereof he died, Ioash. the king of Israel came to him, and saide, O my father, my father, the charet of Israel, and the horse-men of the same 2. king. 13.14. Paul. saith he was the father of the Corinthians, because in Christ Iesus he begat them through the preaching of the gospel. 1. Cor. 4.15. Maisters also are called fathers, as when Naaman the Syrian disdained the counsell of Elisha, his seruants came vnto him, and saide, Father, if the prophet had commaunded thee a greate
thing, wouldest thou not haue done it. 1. king 5.13.
 Quest. Seing the scripture speaketh thus, how commeth it to passe that Christ saith Math. 23.19. Call no man your father vpon earth: for there is but one, your father which is in heauen.
Ans. Many things are spoken in the scriptures, which seeme strange vnto vs, because we consider not well the occasion, nor the drift of the holy Ghost. Christ reprouing the ambition of the Scribes and Pharisies, teacheth his Apostles to be humble and lowlie minded, not loftie and proude: for this purpose he giueth them this generall admonition vers. 8. and saith, yee are all brethren. If any father haue a greate familie and many children, and make one of his sons his stewarde, another his clarke or secretarie, an other his bailife etc. one to ouersee things in the house, another to take charge of thinges abroade: it beseemeth not the sonnes being all brethren and so farre equall, to take vpon them one to crow ouer another, one to commaund an other imperiously, to looke for greate reuerence one of another; but that euerie one doe his office faithfully, and help one another as brethren, and in giuing honour (not in claiming ambition) to goe one before
another (Rom. 12.10.16.) So saith Christ, ye are all brethren, and haue al one father, as it is written, Esai 64.8. O Lord, thou art our father: we are the clay, and thou art ourpotter, and we all are the worke of thine hands. and Malach. 2.10. Haue we not all one father? hath not one God made vs? as if Christ had saide, though you haue diuers offices and callings, yet you haue all one father, euen God, and all our teacher, euen Christ: therefore affect not ambitiously titles of honour as the Scribes and Pharisies do, but diligently performe the duties of your calling with humility. And thus you see there is no repugnancie in the scriptures. For though the Lord hathe made one man father, and another sonne, yet God is father to them both, in which respect they are brethren both by creation and by addoption. And though one man be maister or Doctor and another disciple and scholer, yet Christ is Doctor, maister, and teacher to them both, as it is Math. 17.5, Heare him. wherfore that rare and excellent man of God M. Caluin hath most plainly expou^ded the plac, saying, that maistershippe or fathershippe is not forbidden by Christ, which neither violateth brotherly fellowship, nor dishonoreth God. But if any man wil lifte himselfe
so hie as to chalenge the name of Father in such sort that he doe not plainely professe and shew by worde and deed that God is father to vs all, and so moderate his fathership that he also she we his selfe a brother euen to them ouer whom he is a father by the Lords appointment: and if a doctor, master, or teacher so swell with pride of his calling, that he doe not manifestly declare himselfe also to be but a fellow disciple, and that Christ is our only chiefe teacher: if I say, eyther father or master thus ambitiously dishonor God our father or Christ our schole-master and shew not him selfe to be a brother, and a felow-disciple, he offendeth. And it is his pride which Christ reproueth. For authoritie is giuen to men to honour God withall, not to dishonour him: and to maintaine brotherly fellowship, not to violate. Christ then findeth fault with the abuse, not with the authoritie it selfe.
 Quest. What meane you by honour when it is said in the commandement, honor thy father, etc.
 This worde, Honor,
To loue our superiours. containeth in it especily these foure thinges: First, inwardly to loue our parentes and superiours from our heartes, not to hate them or curse them in our heartes, as it is written in the booke of the Preacher, Chap. 10. vers. 20. Curse not
the king, no not in thy thought, neither cursse the rich in thy bedchamber: for the foule of the heauen shall carie the voice, and that which hath wings, shall declare the matter. And Exod. 22.28. Thou shalt not raile vpon the iudges, neyther speake euill of the ruler of the people.
 Secondly, to reuerence and worship them, euery one according to his calling,
To reuetence them. with such outward reuerence as the manner and custome of the countrie, where they dwell requireth, as it is said of strangers that honored Salomon (but chiefly of them that should honour Christ in his kingdome) Psal. 72.9. They that dwell in the wildernesse shall kneele before him, and his enemy shall licke the dust, that is, they shall fall downe so lowe when they worship him, that their mouths shall touch the earth. So saith the prophet Esaias, Chap. 49.2. Also it is thus written, Leuit. 19.32. Thou shalt rise vppe before the hoare heade, and honour the person of the olde man, and dread thy God.
 Thirdly, to obey them, and doe that which they commaunde,
To obey them. as Paul biddeth vs, Rom. 13.1.2. Let euerie soule be subiect to the higher powers: and whosoeuer resisteth the power, resisteth the ordinance of GOD. Likewise Peter saith, Submitte
your selues vnto al manner of ordinance of man for the Lords sake, whether it bevnto the king, as vnto the superiour, or vnto gouernours, as vnto them that are sent of him, etc. 1. Pet. 2.13. read more, Prou. 23.22. and Coloss. 3.22. and Heb. 13.17.
 Fourthly to maintaine them, to succour,
To mainraine them. cherish, and defend them as occasion requireth, and as we are able, as to defend their liues in time of danger, though it be with perill or losse of our owne life: to maintaine and succour them if neede be in sicknes, in pouerty, or any other necessity, as Ioseph succoured his olde father Iaacob.
 Quest. Concerning the third of these foure things, I stand in doubt whethir superiours are to be obeied in all things; wherefore I pray you open that point a little further.
Ans. The Lorde that hath giuen vs that commaundement to obey our superiours, hath rendred a reason also why they ought to be obeyed. For as all honour and all obedience is due to God without any exception: so hath he most gratiously commaunded some of his owne honour and glorie to superiours, as if he had put some of his owne royall garmentes vpon them, thereby to cause vs to honour them, as for example; although the Lorde be God alone, Deut. 4.35. yet this
glorie hath he commuicated so farre to kings and magistrates that he calleth them Gods, because they are his vicegerentes, and sustaine his person in certaine causes, as you may reade, Exodus. 21.6. and 22.8.9. and Psalm. 82. And albeit we haue but one teacher or master, euen Christ, Math. 23.8. yet the Lorde hath put so much glory vpon the ministers of his word as to call them our doctors or teachers, because as the father sente Christ, so Christ sente them, (Iohn. 20.21.) with the worde of reconciliation as ambassadours to intreate men to be reconciled to GOD, 2. Corinth. 5.20. Although God onely be our father, Math. 23.9. Ephes. 4.6. our onely creator and maker as Esaias sheweth, Chap. 64.8. neuerthelesse he hath imparted this glorie to our naturall parentes, that they are called our fathers, because he hath giuen them this power and appointed them to begette vs. Notwithstanding that Christ alone is the onely heade of his Church and of euerie member there of, Ephes. 1.22. yet this honour is giuen to the husband, that hee is called his wiues heade, Ephes. 5.23. because he is to loue and cherish his wife, as Christ loued his Church. Whereby you may see first that obedience is to be giuen to all
superiours, and secondly that all obedience is not to be giuen to all superiours, but onely to euery one that obedience, which the glorie, that GOD hath imparted to each of them, requireth. And for this cause we giue one obedience to the magistrate, and an other to the minister, and an other to the master, and an other to naturall parentes, and eache wife an other to her owne husbande. Nowe whatsoeuer any superiour commaundeth according to the glorie which the Lorde hath put vpon him, that ought the inferiour to obey and doe. But if any superiour will extende his authoritie aboue the glorie receiued, he ought not to be obeyed in that thing. As for example, if the magistrate commaunde a subiect to giue him that honour which a wife oweth to her husband, and in all thinges to obey him as a wife doth her husbande, the subiect is not bound, neyther ought to giue that obedience to the magistrate. And that which is manifest, and so cleare in this example that no man can or will for shame denie, the same may be saide of the rest. For the authoritie of euerie superiour is finite and limited within certaine boundes and listes according to the measure and qualitie of the
glory which the Lorde hath communicated vnto him, and he ought not to go beyond that. For it is God alone who hath al authority ouer all without limitation or exception. And if any superiour doe go beyond his authoritie, yet the inferiour ought not therein to obey him.
And for this cause, when the Lorde commaundeth inferiours to obey their superiours, he doth now and then admonish them how farre they ought to obey. As when he biddeth the subiest obey the king, be saith in the booke of the preacher, Chap. 8. vers. 2. I aduertise thee to keepe the commaundement of the king but according to the oath of GOD. That is, with this limitation, or exception, that thou breake not the oath which thou hast sworne to God. For if the king commaunde thee to breake any of Gods commaundementes, to the keeping whereof thou hast bound thy selfe by an oath, thou must not obey him. So Christ saith, Math. 22.21. Giue to Caesar the thinges that are Caesars; and giue vnto God those thinges which are Gods. So Paule wisheth men to obey magistrates for conscience sake, Rom. 13.5. No we hee that obeieth further then GOD commaundeth, he doth it not for conscience sake,
but against his conscience, because it is the Lorde onely that bindeth the conscience. And for this cause Daniell and his fellowes refused to obey the kings commaundement Dan. 3. and 6. and the Apostles would not obey the commaundement, which the consistorie of the Iewes enioyned them, Act. 4.19.
Also when Commaundement is giuen to obey the ministers of the worde, Deut. 17.12. this clause or caueat is annexeth, that standeth before the Lorde thy God to minister there, as if he had saide, so long and so farre as he executeth his office before the Lorde. The same Christ teacheth vs, Math. 23. that whiles the scribes sit in Moses seate, all that which they command out of the worde of God, is to be obeyed. The same admonition doth the Apostle giue, 1. Thess. 5.12. and Heb. 13.17. Concerning children it is saide, Ephesians. 6.1. Children obey your parentes in the Lorde, but no further. Likewise seruantes must obey their masters, but in the Lorde, Ephes. 6.7.
Againe it is written, Coloss. 3.18. Wiues submit your selues vnto your husbandes, as it is comely in the Lord.
And reason teacheth vs howe equall these exceptions be. For it is a generall axiome among
the learned, that Lex inferioris non praeiudicat nec derogat legi superioris, the lawe of the inferiour is not preiudicall too, neyther diminishieth any thing from the lawe of the superiour.
 Quest. What is the reason of this commaundement: and howe doe parentes prolonge the daies of their children vpon earth?
Ans. The reason I take to be this, that as before the lawe, naturall parentes and gouernours of greate families had power to put to death such as within their house deserued it, Gen. 38.24. so after the lawe giuen at Horeb, that authoritie and more also was committed to certaine men of Israell chosen to be magistrates. And if any naturall sonne disobeyed his parentes, hee was brought before the magistrate and put to death, Deutro. 21.21. Likewise all inferiours were to be punished by the magistrate according to the qualitie of their trespasse, if they disobeyed their superiours. Wherefore seeing God hath giuen authoritie to magistrates to punish offenders, and to put them to death if their offence deserue it; and also made the magistrate a protector and defendor of them that doe well, as it is manifest,
1. Pet. 2.14. Rom. 13.3.4. Deutro. 1.16.17. the Lord in this commaundement chargeth inferiours to obey their suppriours and in so doing they shalbe defended and protected by their superiours from wrongs and from iniuries, and so haue their liues and their dayes prolonged vpon earth. Whereas otherwise if they disobeye their superiours, they haue authoritie to cut them off, and shorten their dayes.
 Quest. Why doth Paul say this commaundement is the first with promise? had not the second a promise added to it?
Ans. That which is added to the second commaundement is rather a declaration of the iustice and mercie of God, then any promise. But whereas God hath made many promises and greate to them that keepe his commaundements and specially Leuit 26. and Deut. 28 of all those promises he hath not annexed any one to any of al the ten commaundements, when he gaue them in Sinai, saue only this one promise, and that to this fift commaundement only, and so it is both the first, and also the last commaundement which hath any of all those promises annexed vnto it. For otherwise this promise perteineth to them that keepe the other commaundementes, as it is manifest, Deut.
6.2.  and 11.9.21. and 32.47.
Quest. Now that you haue shewed me the meaning of the Lord in this commaundement, I pray you declare who breake it, that so we may haue more vse of it.
Ans. First they that rebell against kings, princes, and magistrates, as did Dathau and Abiram the sonnes of Renben against Moses Num. 16. as did sheba the sonne of Bichri against Dauid 2. Sam. 20.1. as did Iozacar and Iehosabad against Ioash king of Ierusalem 2. king 12.21. as the seruants did against Amaziah king of Iudah. 2. king. 14.19. but are threatned with Gods Iudgements for their rebellion Mich. 1.13. And by treason were foure kings of Israel slaine within the space of 34. yeares, as we reade 2. king. 15.
Secondly, they that murmur against their princes and magistrates, and finde fault with paying of tribute, not considering that they, their wiues, their children, and al that they haue are preserued in safetie and peace, by the care, wisdom, and prouidence of their prince. Thus the subiectes in Salomons dayes murmured, as it appeareth 1. king 12.4. although Salomon made siluer in Ierusalem as plentifull as stones 1. king. 10.27. And vppon such sinfull murmuring, follow euil words
and railing speaches contrarie to the commaundement Exod. 22.28. Iob. 34.18. Thus Shemei railed on Dauid.
Thirdly, they that fauour and maintaine triators or mall-content mutinous subiectes giuing them countenance or enterteinement. And such be they that harbour our closse papists and disguised traitours the hipocriticall Iesuites, which are the vipers of England, and will eate out the bellie of England, to let the Pope, the instument of the redde dragon, come in againe, except their fosterers may be well looked vnto, and receiue according to their wicked desertes. And whosoeuer in England loueth hartely the Lords annointed our most gratious Queene Elizabeth that hath made siluer as plenteous as stones in England (for what childe, seruant, or begger hath not siluer in his purse at this day) and through the Lords blessing also hath made such deepe-peace, and roial prosperitie within the walles of England as neuer was in any nation since Salomons dayes; that I may spare to speake of the vnspeakable treasure of the gospel, whosoeuer I say, loueth his dreade Souereigne truly, detesteth these popish Iesuits and all poperie, as aduersaries to Christ, to the gospell, and to all Christian princes, and thereunto desire their fauorites
may be well looked into. For their malice is against the Gospell of Iesus Christ and against al the mighty mainteiners of it. And if the glorious light of the gospell should euer hereafter be quenched in Engand, how shall we sinful creatures in this world, which is full of darkenes, finde the way to heauen, how shal our posteritie and successors corn to saluation, yea and how greately shall God be dishonored, when papists, atheists and heathens throughout the world (for they haue al heard what greate things the Lord hath doone for England) shall say, where is now the God of England? what is now become of the gospell of Christ that was so plentifully preached in England? O that this were well considered of all that feare God. For my part, it is greater then I am able to expresse. The Lord for his owne glorious names sake shew mercie to England, and be good to them that shall come after vs, that our grape-eating set not posterities teeth on edge as the Israelites children did beare the iniquities of their faithers almost fortie yeares in the wildernes Num. 24.33. and that tollerated papists be not prickes in the eyes, nor thorns in the sides of our posteritie.
Fourthlie they doe not faithfully execute their office committed to them by the prince,
whether they haue office in the Church or the common wealth, but turne iudgement into gall and righteousnes into wormewood Amos 5.7. and 6.12. but bite with their teeth, and cry peace, but if a man put not into their mouthes they prepare warre against him Mich. 3.5. For as the kings throne is stablished by iustice and mercie Pro. 16.12. and 20.8.28. So for want of due execution it is ouerthrown. And where there is no vision, the people decay Pro. 29.18. Wherefore seing these two, adminstration of iustice, and sincere preaching of the word at two chief pillers to support a kings throne, and the Lord chargeth the kings to see both these duly performed, they that deceiue the king in these two, are meanes to pul downe his throne.
Also those that obey not the ministers of the worde of God, when faithfully they preach the gospell and deuide the word a right, they oftend against this commaundement, and are causes of greate wrath from the Lord, and of much calamitie among men. For as the Lord commaunded Ioshua to stand before Eleazar the priest, who should aske counsel of the Lord for him Num, 27.21. and as Dauid accordingly did in al his actions aske counsell of the Lord by the priestes and prophets 1. Sam. 22.15. and 23.2.4.6. And as
Iehosaphat prospered whiles he sought the Lord. 2. Chro. 17.3.4.5. and as Ioash did that was right in the sight of the Lord al the time that Iehoiada the priest taught him 2. kings 12, 2, as did also Vzziah King of Iuda in the dayes of Zechariah that instructed him in the feare of the Lord 2. Chro. 26.5. so they that haue not obeyed the word of the Lord declared to them by his ministers, haue purchased many miseries, as the prophet of the Lord tould Amaziah king of Iudah. 2. Chro. 25.16. I know that God hath determined to destroy thee, because thou hast doone this (that is; serued idols Vers. 14.) and hast not obeyed my counsell. for he counselled the kinge to forsake his Idolatrie. For it is a general rule and a truth grounded vpon the law of god Leuit. 26.21.24. and 2. Sam. 22.27. which Azariah the prophet tould Asa that good king of Iudah 2. Chro. 15.2. saying, The Lord is with you, while ye be with him: and if yee seeke him; he wilbe found of you, but if ye forsake him, he will forsake you. And which Semaiah the prophet tould Rehoboam. 2. Chro. 12.1.2.5. ye haue forsaken me (saith the Lord) therefore haue I left you in the handes of Shishak. And Abiah king of Iudah, reproued Ieroboam and all Israel 2. Chro. 13.9. for the same cause. In the Kingdom of Israel,
we reade not of one good King that continewed in the feare of God, and therefore they were depriued of the tokens and testimonies of Gods fauour 2. Chro. 15.3. And also oppressed with many calamities Hos. 5.11. Mich. 6.15. and at the last were destroied for being a kingdome. Likewise the chiefe cause of the destruction of Iudah and Ierusalem when he went into captiuitie, was because they would not obey the priestes and prophets of the Lord, as Ieremie witnesseth Chap. 35.15.16.17. and that also was the cause of their reiection at Christes comming Math. 23.37.38.39. This also is the cause whie the seauen famous Churches in Asia haue their candlestickes remoued from them. This is the cause of the miseries of Germany, Fraunce, and Flanders. And except there be more obedience giuen to the word of God among vs, then I can perceiue there is, we may daily looke for some greate iudgment from God. We had neede dayly to remember the comparison the Apostle vseth Heb. 2.2.3. where he sheweth that if the disobeyers of the Law giuen by Angels, were sharply punished, much more shall they be punished which obediently receiue not such grace as now is offred in the gospell. The Lord of mercie open our eyes that we may
