see it; and mollifie our stonie hearts, that we may vnfainedly repent, and renew the couenant of our God, and so repent his iudgments.
Now if I should come to particular states and degrees of men, or to particular sinnes, to shew how that which the ministers of the word preach in the name and in the wordes of the Lord, is disobeyed; I should be too too tedious, although I haue alreadie ouershot my selfe, as hauing purposed but only to haue pointed with the finger to the capitall heads of things, whose braunches are more fully declared by daily preaching, then I am able to come nere vnto by writing, seuerall occasions mouing the Spirit by which they speake, to touch particulars most notably. What person so mean or so base throughout al the Land almost, that doth not despise the minister and the word he preacheth, as their workes declare? what man followeth no this fantasie? Let the minister preach neuer so much, he will doe what he list, and thinketh all is well if he doe not such open violence as the lawes of the Land will punish. what couetous Idolaters, what cruel oppressors, what vncleane persons, what deceitfull traders, what cunning iugglers in all dealings, what falshood in fellowship, what cosenage
in bargaining, what merciles misers, what discontented murruurers, what virulent hatred, what bloodie murders, that bloode toucheth blood? that a man might heere almost rehearse the sixt verse of the first chapter of Esaias. And yet for all this, who can say that such a man pricked in his soule with remorse of conscience for his sinnes, or else terrified with the iudgementes of God, hath giuen any notable testimonie of true repentance before he durst presume to come to the Lordes table? nay diuers commaunded to testifie their repentance because their offences were publike, doe shift it off, beeing more ashamed of mens faces, then afraide of Gods iudgements. And where then is the obedience giuen to the ministers of the worde of God? Salomon saith, Prou. 30.12. There is a generation that are pure in their owne conceit, and yet are not washed from their filthines.
Thirdly, children that disobey their parents,
They that disobey their parentes. and mocke them, as Ham did his father Noe, Gen. 9.22. of whome thus speaketh the holy Ghost, Pro. 30.17. The eye that mocketh his faher, and despiseth the instruction of his mother, let the rauens of the valley picke it out, and the yong eagles eate it. They that make mariages for themselues without their parentes knowledge, liking, and consent contrary to the law of God.
Ex. 22.16.17. So did Esau, Ge. 26.34.35.27.46. They that by dissention, and by their wickednes grieue their parents, as lacobs sonnes did when they solde Ioseph into Aegypt, Gen. 37.33.34.35. and when they guilefully slew the Sechemites, Gen. 34.30. So did Amnon grieue his father Dauid when he defiled his sister Thamar, 2. Sam. 13.21. and Absolom when he slew his brother Amnon, 2. Sam. 13.31. and when he rebelled against his father. 2. Sam. 15. They that smite their parents and therfore ought to be put to death, Exo. 21.15. Deu. 21.18. They that wil not be ruled by their fathers counsell as Salomon biddeth them, Pro. 23.22. but follow their owne fancies. They that entice children from their parents, or without their parents knowledge lead them to wickednes. They that run away from their parents. They that suffer their parents to famish for want and helpe them not though they be able. They that steale any thing from their parents, as Michah did from his mother, Iudg. 17.1.2.
Fourthly,
Wiues that disobey their husbands. wiues that are not obedient to their husbandes as they ought to be, but eyther forsake the guide of their youth, and forget the couenant of their God, Pro. 2.17. and with harlots be hauiour and subtile hearts, are alwaies babling, sometime within, sometimes without, lying in waite at euery corner to entice young
men to wickednes, and impudently kisse them and draw them home to their houses, as it were sheepe to the slaughter, and say their husbands are gone from home, as Salomon declareth at large, Pro. 7.10. etc. or else are continually chiding, Pro. 19.13. that the husband had better dwel in a corner of the house top, the^ in a wide house with such a wife, Pro. 25.24. or else are idle and do nothing, as though they ought not as carefully to looke to the things in the house, as the husba^d to the things abroad. Or els they wilbe wiser then their husbands and ouer-rule them. But if good and religious wiues woulde learn their duties, and how they ought to be haue the^selues let them read, Pr. 31.10. 1. Pe. 3.1. etc.
Lastly,
Seruants that disobey their masters. seruants breake this commandement when they are idle loiterers, and not painefull labourers; that looke for all their wages, but make no conscience to neglect their seruice; that wil work til they sweat when their master is present, but loiter so soone as he hath turned his back til they catch a cold with being idle. They that despise their masters which are ignorant of the misteries of saluation, and thinke it is no matter before God if they loiter when they haue such masters, not regarding that they cause their ignorant masters to speake euill of their God, of their faith, and of their religion. But these seruants may learne what Paul teacheth
them, 1. Tim. 6.1. Others whose masters haue knowledge and beleeue in God, they likewise grudge and mutter, saying, they are as good as their master, they are his brethren, and that God accepteth no persons. But these seruants consider not the Lords appointment, who could haue made the seruant a master, the subiect a king, the sonne to be the father, the yonger to be the elder, if it had pleased him: but seeing the Lord hath disposed of all men for the affairs of this life, let euery man be content with his calling and therein abide with God 1. Cor. 7.24. And let these seruants read Paul, 1. Tim. 6.2. Others neglect their seruice because their masters are too too hard and rigorous without cause, as though a seruant might doe euill for euill. But let these seruants reade, 1. Pet. 2.18. Also those seruants breake this commandement, which serue their masters as Ziba serued Mephibosheth, 2. Sam. 16.1.2.3. and 19.24.25. Other seruants when a man bringeth their master a present, or a bribe to obtaine vnlawfull fauour in an eull matter, if the master refuse it because he will not be corrupted, then they wil receiue something secretly, promising to do their best to corrupt their master. Sometime where the master is a good man and taketh nothing of his tenants but his rentes, the seruant wil goe in his masters name (but without
his masters knowledge) for something and keepe it to himself, as if it were Gehesie, 2. Kin. 5.20.27. Somtime when the master maketh the seruant his pursebearer, and biddeth him giue a shilling to a poore man, the seruant much like Iudas will giue the poore man sixe pence and put the restin his own purse. Somtime the seruant put in trust to sel his masters goods in the shop, in the fayre, in the market, in the marte, will alwaies be purloyning some to himselfe, whereby some masters are shortly consumed, and the wicked seruant by his wicked Mammon inriched. Some seruants make a couenant with theeues, and so rob their masters. Some seruants get great summes of their masters money into their handes, and runne away with it. Some betray their masters sonnes and daughters, to lewd company, or to be maried. Some do many thinges in their masters names, whereof their masters are ignorant. And there is neither siluer nor golde, nor any other thing so rare to he had at this day, as it is to finde a good and faithfull seruant.
How little reuerence youth giueth to age,
Youth disobeyeth age. is a thing more manifest to the eye of the world then that there needes any wordes to be spent about it. It were rather to be wished that they which are in authority would redresse it by punishment laid open euery boy that hauing but a
feather in his hat, or a poinado at his girdle, or a short cloake on his backe, or twelue pence in his purse, will iustle with euery man that giues him not the way, will saucely crow ouer auncient gray-headed fathers, and contemptuously abuse all ages and degrees, whom they stand not in awe of. So that the obedience they giue to any, proceedeth of a seruile feare of punishment, and not of any reuerence to God, or to his commaundements.
Now it remaineth on the contrary part to see how superiours for not performing their dueties doe also breake this commandement.
The dueties of superiours to inferiours. And heerein it will appeare that sometimes they are the cause themselues why their inferiours doe not obey them as they ought.
 First, when chiefe magistrates, whose duety is to maintaine true religion,
The duty of magistrats. and to administer iustice without respect of persons, Leuit. 19.15. Deu. 1.17. that iudgement may run down euen throughout their dominions like water, and righteousnes like a mightie riuer Amos. 5.24. do omit these things, and giue themselues to ease and pleasure; or else destroy religion, and peruert iustice, then through the iust iudgment of God it comes often to passe that their inferiours honour them not. Absolom tooke occasion vpon some wante of execution of iustice to rebell against his father; and
the holy Ghost hath noted it for our instruction, 2. Sam. 15.3. Because Salomon fell to idolatrie in his olde age, the Lorde both raised vp three aduersaries against him, euen Hadad the Edomite, 1. King. 11.14. and Reson the sonne of Eliadah, 1. King. 11.23. and Ieroboam his owne subiect to lift vp his hande against him, 1. King. 11.26. And also tolde him that he would rent the kingdom after his death that his son should be king but ouer one whol tribe of Iudah, and ouer part of Beniamin. 1. King. 11.11.12.13. when Ahab and Iezabell had put downe true religion and erected grosse idolatrie, and slaine the prophets of the Lord, as Elijah complained, the Lord threatned great destruction to Israell by Hazaell, and by Iehu. 1. King. 19.15.16.17. as also because Ahab had murthered Naboth and his sonnes, 1. King. 21.20.21.22.23.24. the accomplishment whereof together with repetition of the causes, we reade, 2. King. 9.7.26. and 2. King. 10. throughout the whole story of the bookes of Kings and Chronicles it is manifest, that want of administration of iustice, and want of maintenance of true religion, was the cause of ciuill tumults and insurrections, and of forren inuasions, as was partly touched before, when I spake of disobedience to the ministers of the worde. Wherefore Dauids song
of mercy and iudgement, Psal. 101. were a worthy glasse for all kinges and princes to looke in continually. And Salomon hath a memorable sentence, Prou. 16.12. It is abomination to kinges to commit wickednes: for the throne is stablished by iustice. Then as kinges woulde haue their kingdomes confirmed to them and their posteritie, and as they woulde haue all their subiectes loyall and faithfull: so let them maintaine Gods true and pure religion, and minister iustice vprightly without any respect of persons. And then will the Lord stablish them and their kingdomes, then will the Lorde protect them and their kingdomes, that no enemie shall be able to doe them violence. For there is no wisedome, neyther vnderstanding, nor counsell against the Lorde, Prouerbes. 21.30. And who is he that can say, that there was euer any man deceiued, that put his trust in the Lorde and kept his commaundementes. But heere is one thing which is not to be passed ouer with silence, that is, the king may not say to the Lord, I haue appointed magistrates, iudges, and officers, and commaunded them to deale iustly in iudgement, and if they doe otherwise, it is their fault and not mine: Neither may the king say to the Lord, I haue commaunded the ministers of the
word to preach truly and diligently, and if they either preach lyes and heresies, or be negligent, it is their fault not mine, I say a king may not thus answere the Lord, nor think his duetie so discharged. But if Cambises a heathen prince put Sisamnes a corrupt and wicked iudge to death, because he ministred not iudgement vprightly, and caused his skin to be fleade of him, and thereof a seate to be made for the next iudge to sit vpon, and placed Otanes his son iudge in his fathers roome, to sit continually vpon his fathers skin when he sat in iudgement, thereby admonishing him to minister true and vpright iudgement, as Herodotus writeth Lib. 5. how much more ought Christian kings seuerely to punish corrupt iudges, who by peruerting iustice bring danger of Gods wrath to the King and to the whole kingdome. A wise King sayth Salomon 20.26. scattereth the wicked, and causeth the wheele to turne ouer them. Moses that meeke man (Num. 12.3.) was angry with the captaines of the host for sauing the women of Midian aliue, whom they ought to haue slaine, and caused them afterward to put these women todeath Num. 31.14. Dauid confessing that the sonnes of Zeruiah were too hard for him 2. Sam. 3.39. so that he was not able, as being newly established
in his kingdome, to punish them according to their deserts, afterward as occasion serued, put Ioab out of his office and made Amaza captaine of the host in his roome 2. Sam. 19.13. and 20.4. That good king Hezekiah perceiuing that Shebnah the steward of his house (Esai. 22.15.) was a wicked man, and a secret fauourer of al the wicked in his kingdome, founde opportunitie to displace him, and brought him dowen from being chiefe steward, and made him but one of his scribes, and placed Eliakim stewarden in his rome 2. kings. 18.18. Zelous Nehemiah sent twise fro^ Sushan to Ierusalem with great authority, both times reproued the rulers of the people, first because they oppressed the people cruelly Nehem. 5.7. secondly because they suffered the people to breake the Lords sabbath Nehem. 13.17. The good young King Ioash did not only restore religion after the death of that wicked Athalia 2. Chro. 23.18. but also reproued Iehoiada the hie priest and the rest of the priestes for negligence in their office, and straitely commaunded that the things belonging to Gods worship should be better regarded 2. kings. 12.6.7. etc. And for this cause good kings in Ierusalem, haue not only restored true religion in the beginnings of their reigne, but
also proceeded afterward to redresse and make further reformation, as occasion required. So did Asa: 2. Chro. 15, 8. Iehosaphat 2. Chro 19. Ioash 2. Chro. 24.4. and Iosiah 2 Chro. 34.
And besides these examples there is a generall doctrine Leuit 2.4.5. that if the people of the land (that is, the magistrates especially) winke at sinne, will not see it, and so suffer it to goe vnpunished, then the Lorde will set his angry countenance not only against the sinner, but also against the people of the land. A notable spectacle of this doctrine is Ioshu: 22.18. When the Rubenites, Gadites, and halfe of the tribe of Manasses had built an alter on the south side of Iordan for a memoriall to their posteritie, that it might be knowen they were Israelites. But when the Israelites inhabiting within the land of Canaan heard that their brethren had made an alter, they supposing it had bene for Idolatrie, and therefore were afraide of Gods iudgements, and sent messengers ouer Iourdan to their brethren saying, Seeing ye rebel to day against the Lord, euen to morrow he wilbewrath with all the congregation of Israel, acknowledging that if they should suffer sinne vnpunished, the Lords wrath would burst out against them all, as the place euidently sheweth.
Yea if sinne be secretly committed, and kept close from the knowledge of the magistrate, yet the Lord wilbe angry with the whole land, as it appeareth in the example of Achan Iosh. 7. For though he only sinned secretly, yet the army of Israel was put to flight for his offence, and 36. men of Israel were slaine. The same is manifest Deut. 21 in that the magistrates must in such sort protest their innocencie, and so purge the citie from blood guiltines, when a man is found slaine in the field, and the murderer is not knowen. When Isaac soiourning in Gerar saide of Rebecca that she was his sister, Abimelech a heathen king afterward percieuing that she was his wife, called Isaac vnto him, and reprouing him for it, said, one of the people had almost lien by thy wife, so shouldest thou haue brought sin vpon vs Gen. 26.10. he doth not say, so shouldest thou haue brought sinne vpon him that had lien with thy wife only, but he saith, vpon vs, shewing that if sinne be committed, the wrath of the Lord wilbe against the whole land, and specially against them, to whom God hath giuen authoritie to punish it. Also vpon like occasion Abimelech had said before to Abraham Gen. 20.9, what haue I offended thee that thou hast brought on me and on my kingdom this greate sinne?

Secondly,
The dne ties of children. because the ministers of the word sometimes doe not their dueties, therfore it comes to passe that both the seruice of God is abhorred, 1. Sam. 2.17. and the ministers themselues are despised Malach. 2.8.9. Because ye are gone out of the way etc. therefore haue I also made you to be despised and vile etc. For as Paul setteth himselfe for a patterne for all faithfull pastors to follow Act. 20.18. etc. and giueth Timothie a reuerent and a dreadefull charge. 1. Tim. 5.21. and 2. Tim. 4.1.2. so there are feareful iudgements denounced against euil pastors in many places of the scripture, as Zach. 11.17. O Idle shepard that leaueth the flock the sword shalbe vpon his arme, and vpon his right eye. His arme shalbe cleane dried vp, and his right eye shalbe vtterly darkned.
 Thirdly, because husbands sometyme performe not their duties,
Duties of husbands. as they are taught Ephes. 5.25.28. Colos. 19. and. 1. Pet. 3.17. but when they cannot lawfully obtaine a bill of diuorcement, they make them selues a bill of wicked libertie, and giue themselues to commit adulterie and fornication with other women, therefore it comes to passe that their wiues are not obedient to them. 
 Fourthly,
Dueties of parents. because parents bring not vp
their children in the nurture and feare of the Lord, as Paul biddeth Ephes. 6.4. but either cocker them, and feare to displease them, as Hely did 1. Sam. 2.23.24. and Dauid did 1. king. 1.6. or pricke them vp in pride, and teach them to mocke and abuse others, and sometime the father will teach his sonne to miscall his mother, and fomtime the mother will teach her daughter to miscall her father, and thus the parents sport themselues with their children, and make no conscience to sweare and cursse in the presence of their children: therefore doeth it often come to passe by Gods iust iudgment that their children rebel against them, as Absolom and Adoniah did against Dauid, or grieue them, and bring them to such calamitie, as Hophnia and Phineas brought their ould father Heli; or wound their heartes with sorrow when they see them giuen to whordo^, stealing, to robbing, to spe^ding all they can rape or rend, to murder; to treason, to poperie, to arehisme, and so finally to come to the gallows; and when first through their parents wicked education, and secondly, through such a lewd life they come to ignominious deathes, it is most of al other to be feared, lest they depart hence to the diuell in hel. Salomon giueth parents good counsell Prou. 22.15. and 29.15.
But when foolish pitie doeth so possesse the parentes, that they cannot find in their hearts to correct their children whiles they are young, they must afterward, will they, nil they endure the griefe of it in the ende. Parents watch night and day with labour and paines taking, and often pinche themselues to prouide for their children earthly wealth but how to get them inheritance in the king do me of heauen, comes not once into their minde, though God specially charge them to instruct their children in the wayes of his lawes Deut. 6.7. And that is a token what reckoning parents make of God or of heauen. Thereforenoe maruaile though their children disobey them.
 Fiftly, maisters teach their seruants fraude, guile, robberie, impietie, and all wickednes, not only by their euil example but euen by their co^mandement, and therefore haue no cause to looke for obedience or fidelitie ar^ their hands
 Quest. What is the punishment for him that breaketh this commaundement?
Ans. It is death, as you may reade Exod. 21.15.17. Leuit. 20.9. Deut 21.18. etc,
Thou shalt not kil.
 Quest. What is the summe of this commaundement? or what is to be considered in
it?
Ans. This commaundement and the rest following are all negatiues, and the Lord beginning here with the greatest trepsasse that one man can possibly commit against another, euen murder, proceedeth by degrees dowenward from a greate offence to a lesser till he come to the least desire that is in mans heart to couet any thing that belongs to our neighbour, and forbiddeth them all. In this commaundement we wil first consider how many kinds of murder there be, secondly how many wayes it is committed.
 Quest. How many kindes of murder doe you say there are?
Quest. According as man consisteth of two parts, the soule and the bodie: so there is one maner of killing the soule, and another of the bodie.
 Quest. How is the soule killed?
Ans. As the bodie may be famished to death for want of foode or be destroyed with poison so there is a famishme^t of the soule when it is depriued of the spirituall foode of the word of God, and the Lord chargeth him as guiltie of blood that thus killeth any man Eze. 33.7.8. O sonne of man I haue made thee a watchman vnto the house of Israell: when I shall say vnto the wicked, O
wicked man, thou shalt die the death, if thou doest not speake, and admonish the wicked of his way, that wicked man shall die for his iniquitie, but his blood will I require at thy hande. Also they that teach and preach heresie or false and pernitious doctrine, which I suppose is compared to wormewood, Apo. 8.11. they poyson and destroymens soules, as that holy father the Antechrist of Rome doth, and as Mahomet hath done. For these two are pernitious enemies of mans saluation throughout the worlde almost, the Pope in Europe, and Mahomet in Asia and Africa.
 Quest. What say you then of the killing of the bodis?
Ans. The diuers kindes of murdering the bodie are so commonly knowen by lamentable experience, that I shall not neede to stand vpon it. But in one worde or two thus much. If the murderer be not knowen, but a mans life is taken away and no man can tell who shed that bloode, then all the Citie, towne, vilage, or parish where such murder is secretly committed is guiltie of that mans bloode that is slaine, but specially the magistrates and chiefe gouernours of that place, because they kept not better watch and warde for mens safetie, but through some negligence of theirs let a
mans blood be shed, and the murderer to escape and not be knowen. For as we haue a most commendable order for the safetie of mens goods, that if the Citie, towne, village, or parish next to the place where any man is robbed, doe not vpon the complaint of the man that is robbed, prosecute the theeues and robbers to apprehende them, then that Citie, towne, village, or parish seemeth to be priuie to the robberie, and for their negligence are to restore to the man robbed all that he lost: so the Lorde hath made a most holie and necessarie lawe, Deutro. 21. that when any man is murdered and the murderer vnknowen, then the elders or gouernours of that place shoulde in a solemne manner and with such ceremonies as the Lord there prescribeth, first protest that they were not priuie to that murder, vers. 7. and secondly by prayer to intreate the Lorde not to lay that murder to their charge, verse. 8. Of which lawe though the ceremonies be abolished, yet the equitie remaineth, that magistrates should haue speciall care for to preserue mens liues, and knowe that if through their negligence murder be committed, or after it is committed, the murderer winked at and suffered to escape, they
cannot be innocent before GOD. For if that order for safetie of mens goods be commendable and necessarie, a thousande soulde more holy and more necessarie is this law of God, which is for safetie of mens liues.
But to come to other kindes of murders where the murderer is knowen, sometimes a man is his owne murderer and killeth himselfe, as Saul and his harnest-bearer fell vpon their owne swordes and died, 1. Sam. 31.4. Achitophell hanged himselfe, 2. Sam. 17.23. Zimri set his owne pallace on fire and burnt himselfe, 1. King. 16.18. Iudas the traitour hanged himselfe, Math. 27.5. Act. 1.18. The Donatistes in Africa killed themselues when they should haue beene apprehended, and haue suffered iust punishment for their heresies; and some of them, whom Philastrius calleth circuitores, caused those they met in the way to kill them, and said they were desirous of martyrdome. For they termed themselues martyrs when they murdered themselues. The cause which moueth any man to kill himselfe is commonly eyther desperation, or else impatiencie. For some men thinking that nothing goes well with them except they may obtaine that they desire, whatsoeuer it be when they cannot haue it,
and begin to despaire to obtaine it, then they kill themselues. Others brought into some distresse that they must of necessitie suffer some punishment or some shame or both or other miserie and grief, through impatience kil themselues. As for those that haue killed themselues in hope of some good which by that meanes they would obtaine, they haue beene brought into a fooles paradise.
 Quest. What say you of them that kill others?
Ans. I say that sometimes one man killeth another wittingly and willingly, and sometimes against his will or of ignorance. And God pardoneth this latter, but condemneth the former, Exod. 21.12.13: Num. 35.10. etc. Wherefore there is often greate a doe to determine whether it be murther or manslaughter, wilfull murder or chance-medley. Voluntarie and wilfull murder according to the circumstances is somtime more heinous, then at another time, especially in respect of time, place, and persons; though all wilfull murder be most execrable. As for example, to kill a man when he is worshipping GOD, or executing iustice in the Church, in the presence of the king, or where he cannot defend himselfe; these thinges aggrauate the offence. But to kil
a magistrat as Iesuites doe, to kill natural parentes as the sonnes of Senacherib did, 2. King. 19.37. to kill a naturall brotheras Kain did, Gen. 4. and Abimelech, Iudg. 9. and Iehoram 2. Chro. 21. to kil infantes as did Pharaoh, Exod. 1. and Herode, Math. 2. to murder confederates as did Simeon and Leui, Gen. 34. these things are most execrable.
Quest. What say you of Moses that slew the Aegyptian, Exo. 2.12. of Phinchas for killing Zimri and Cozbi Num. 25.8. of Samson who slew many, Iudg. 14.19. and 15.15. and 16.30. of Samuel that hewed Agag in peeces, 1. Sam. 15.33. and of Eliah?
Ans. These extrordinarie workes, which the Lord hath wrought by his owne most holy seruants for the great benefit of his Church and which the holy Ghost hath so highly commended, I take it not to be the duety of any of the Lordes elect to call into question. These thinges are written to teach vs that the Lord both can and will prouide for the good of his Church, and manifest his power and glorie when and by whom it pleaseth him. But they are not written for vs to imitate, as you may perceiue by that one answere of Christ to his disciples when they woulde haue imitated Elias, Luke. 9.55. Yee knowe not of what spirit ye are. For in
all our doings we must walke after the commandements of God but not after euery example. And to be too curious in questioning of these thinges, were to examine the Lord by what authority he did these things by these his seruants.
 Quest. How many waies is murder committed?
Ans. First, when we hate our brother in our heart, Math. 5.22. Whosoeuer is angrie with his brother vnaduisedly, shalbe culpable of iudgement. And 1. Iohn. 3.15. whosoeuer hateth his brother, is a manslaier.
 Secondlie, when we shewe foorth our murdering mindes eyther by our frowning countenance as Kain did, and was reproued of the Lorde, Gen. 4.6. or by malitious, virulent, and spitefull wordes, Math. 5.22. Whosoeuer saith vnto his brother, Raca, shalbe worthy to be punished by the counsell: And whosoeuer shall say, Foole, shalbe worthy to be punished with hell fire.
 Thirdly, by committing the deede, and that eyther when we kill with our owne handes as Kain slew Abell, Gen. 4. and as Ioab slewe Abner. 2. Sam. 3.27. or when we procure others to doe it, as Dauid procured the death of Vriah. For though the Ammonites slewe him, 2. Sam. 11.17. yet Nathan tolde Dauid in plaine wordes that
he had killed Vriah, 2. Sam. 12.9. or when we consent to others that doe it, as when Abimelech slewe the sonnes of Ierubbal, Iud. 9.5. the Shechemites for consenting are accused of that murder, Iudg. 9.18. Abisai for consenting to the death of Abner, whome Ioah slewe is saide to haue killed him. 2. Samuel. 3.30.
 Quest. What is there further to be considered in this commaundement?
Ans. We must vnderstand that al forerunners of murder as preparations to it, are forbidden, as; First, anger, choler, hastines, which corruptions grow in our nature, and except by the grace of God we bridle them, they make men like brute beastes, so that vpon a sudden they will yeeld to their wicked and sinful humors, and strike whosoeuer commeth next to hand, and with whatsoeuer they haue in their hande, be it knife or other thing. Wherefore Paul admonisheth vs, Rom. 12.19. to giue place vnto wrath. And Salomon saith, Prou. 22.24.25. Make no friendshippe with an angrie man, neyther go with the furious man, least thou learne his waies, and receiue destruction to thy soule.
Secondly, enuie, strife, contention, taunting, mocking, quarrelling, etc. whereof commonly commeth hurt, which is to be recompensed
by the magistrate with the like, eye for eye, tooth for tooth, etc, Exod. 21.24. Leuit. 24.19. And very often vpon such brauling at the first followeth murder at the last. Wherfore Salomon giueth good counsell, Prou. 20.3. It is a mans honour to cease from strife: but euerie foole wilbe medling. And in another place, Cast out the scorner, and strife shall goe out: so contention and reproch shall cease, Prou. 22.10. For where enuying and strife is, there is sedition and all manner of euill workes, Iam. 3.16.
 Thirdly, quaffing and drinking till men be drunken and madde as wilde beastes, and care not neither can tell what they doe. For wine is a mocker, and strong drinke is raging. Prou. 20.1.
 Quest. What more doe you obserue in this commaundement?
Ans. That as all murder of what sort soeuer it be, and all the waies of murdering; with all such things as are preparatiues thereunto, or furtherers of it are forbidden: so on the contrary part are commaunded all thinges which may any way tend to the preseruation of mans life, as to feede the hungry, to cloath the naked, to lodge the barbourles, to defend them that are in danger, to helpe them that be in any kinde of destresse.

 Quest. Who be they that breake this commaundement?
Ans. First, they that kil themselues as som doe, because they cannot haue that thing they desire, and thinke it better not to liue, then to liue without that they would haue, or because they are impatient and will rather die then suffer that which troubleth them.
 Secondly, they that kill others any of those wayes which I named before, either with their owne hands, or else by wicked and cruel dealing oppresse others, and so as it were kil them by a languishing kind of death, For of such oppressors Esay speaking Chap. 1.15. saith, your hands are full of bloode, and Vers. 21. he saith that Ierusalem in former times had bene a faithfull citie, full of iustice and iudgement, but now they are murderers. Of like crueltie the prophet Micah complaineth Chap. 3.3. They also breake this commandement, which trouble, vex, and molest others that they dye for griefe and sorrow. For a sorrowfull minde drieth the bones Pro. 17.22. They that poison others secretly, which is a vsual practise among papists, Spaniards, and heathens. They that procure other to kil men, as Iezabel prooured the magistrates of the citie to put Naboth and his children to death. 1. king. 21.13. They that falsely accuse
others to cause them to be put to death. They that liue in continuall malice and hatred, wishing the death of others. They that suffer others to perish any way, when they might saue their liues, but doe not. They that for pleasure set men to fight before them as Abner and Ioab did 2. Sam. 2.14. as the heathen in former times were wont to doe, and as fence-maisters professing themselues to be Christians, now and then doe. They that appoint men to fight with madd or wild beastes. They that keepe either ruffianly seruants or any beast that vseth to kill men. They that intice men to commit things worthie of death, and then reioyce at their destruction, hopeing to get their Lands or goods. They that purpose to kill, though they cannot effect it, as Haman did. They that kil men in vnlawfull warres by Sea or by land.
 Quest. What other thing doe you obserue in this commaundement?
I willset downe two or three reasons to diswade men from murder.
 First, the Lord the greate king of all the world forbiddeth it in this commaundement, and therefore al men ought to consider diligently of all their wayes, for they must giue an account to God of all their actions.
 Secondly, because man is the image of
God, therefore men ought to be afraide of shedding mans blood, as the Lord himselfe doth admonish vs by this same reason Gen. 9.6.
 Thirdly, we haue all one father, and are brethren, and our neighboure is of our flesh as the prophet Esaias speaketh, Chap. 58.7. For which cause we ought to absteine from murdering of our brethren, as from hurting our owne flesh.
 Fourthly, we pollute the Land, euen the whole citie, or towne, or parish or place where we shed blood, and so make a greate multitude gulitie, and subiect to Gods fearefull plagues, as was shewed before out of Deut. 21. for blood defileth the Land: and the Land cannot be clensed of the blood that is shed therin, but by the blood of him that shed it Numbers 35.33.
 Fiftly, he that killeth a man, is the cause also of his owne death, for the magistrate is commaunded of God to put him to death that committeth murder, wherefore in respect of his owne life, if he regard not his brothers life a man ought to auoide murder.
 Sixtly, by reason of murder committed, often it comes to passe that a whole famimilie wife and children are vndone; and constrained to begge, or be in greate miserie, yea
and sometime two families. Wherefore euen for their sakes men ought to refraine from killing, and from all meanes that may prouoke thereunto. And if there be any man whome these reasons cannot moue, I suppose there can be noe reason why he should liue among men.
 Quest. What is the punishment, which is appointed for them that breake this commaundement?
Ans. It is death, as the Lord hath often saide, as Gen. 9.6. Exod. 21.12. Deut. 19.11. And in Num. 25.31. the Lord forbiddeth the magistrate to pardon wilfull murder, in these words; ye shal take no recompence for the life of the murderer, which is worthy to die: but he shalbe put to death.
Thou shalt not commit adulterie. 
 Quest. What is the summe of this commaundement?
Ans. This commaunde ment in the degree of the sinne it forbiddeth is next to the former, as it standes in place, and as adultery is next in degree to murther, as was obserued in the beginning of the sixt comandement, this co^mmandeme^t forbiddeth adultery, whor, dom fornication, incest, and such vncleannes, although here is mention made but of adulterie only, which is the capitall offence
against this precept.
 Quest. What order is to be kept, or will you follow in speaking of it?
Ans. Because this commaundement is broken both in mariage, and of them that be vnmaried, I wil speake of these two seuerally.
Quest How doe men in mariage breake; this commaundement? 
Ans. First in making of the mariage, and secondly after it is made. And first in making of mariages they offend against this law, who being the sonnes of God, match themselues with the daughters of men, that is, with them which are of an other religion. Secondly they that marrie with religious persons but otherwise then Gods word alloweth.
 Quest. I pray you shew me these two more largely, and first how mariages with them of an other religion are vulawful.
Vnequal mariages.
A. The Lord hath in plaine wordes forbidden his seruants and sonnes to make any mariage with infidels Exod. 34.12.16. Deut. 7.4. And the disobedience to this commaundement is reckonned to be one of the causes of the drowning of the world Gen. 6.2. And often in the scripture doeth the holie Ghost note this sinne, as Gen. 36.34. and. 37.1. of Esau for marying against this law, Also of Salomon
1. king. 11. likewise Ezr. 10. Nehem 9.2. and 13, 3.23. Malach 2.11. But Abrahams care for the mariage of his sonne Isaak according to the will of God, is commaunded Gen. 24.
Quest. What say you if a protestant match with a papist?
Ans. Considering that papists haue forsaken the couenant of God, are egregious idolaters, and in very deede deny Christ, in that they wilbe saued by their workes, there is neither scripture nor reason to iustifie a protestants mariage with a papist. And they that so match themselues or their children, prouoke the Lords wrath greately. The mariage of the faithful is the meanes to increase the number of Gods elect, and is as it were the seminarie or seede plot of the Church. And for this cause the Church ought to be very circumspect that none of the faithfull marrie either with papist, Atheist, or Infidel, least in steede of a holy seede there spring vp in the Church a prophane seede, in steede of lawful heires cursed bastards. For commonly the children that come of such a mixture of holy and prophaine seede, proue to be monstrous wicked, as we reade in Gen. 6. that the posteritie which came of the mariages of the sonnes of God with the daughters
of men, were giants, or tirants, wicked Apostates from God. As Anah let beastes of diuers kinds engender Gen. 36.24. contrary to the law Leuit. 19.19. whereof come fruteles mules and machoes: so the posteritie that commeth of vnequall mariages, are for the most part barren and voide of all godlines. And if such posteritie be fruitful,
Plini. lib. 8. Chap. 16. etc. it is commonly in excessiue wickednes, as I noted out of Gen. 6. And as the beast Thoes ing endered of a wolfe and of Hyaena Herodot. Lib. 4. as the Leopard ingendred of the Lion and the panther, and as others so ingendred of diuers kindes are of much fiercer and more cruel nature, then the senerall kinds of beastes are; so the posteritie of such vnequal matches are like to be worse then either papist or common Atheist, or infidel, as it may be seene vpon the borders of heathens when sometimes Christians and heathens marrie together. The like may be saide of the posteritie of Iewes and Christians, for some times there comes of them a third cast, as they co^monly call them, which is worse then either of the parents. And though there be a greate difference betwene papists and Iewes and Infidels, and a greate difference among papists themselues: yet it is in this, that some are not so bad as others,
and if a protestant would be curious in making choise of a papist, it is but as if out of many poisons he would chuse the weakest. The reason which Malachi vseth Chap. 2.15. to reproue the Iewes both for mariages with infidels, and for their often diuorcements, is this, because (the Lord) sought a godly seede: and the same reason serueth fitly for this purpose. For if the Iewes marying among themselues, but sining in this, that they put away their first wife and tooke another, could not haue a promise of a godly seede or posteritie: how can they that marie with papists hope that their posteririe shalbe godly. What man desirous of pure good wheate, will in seed-time wittingly mingle wheat and tares together, or good wheate and bad together, and therewith sowe his fielde and say he hopes all will proue verie good wheate in haruest? But as no simple man hath so little descretion, as thus to sowe his field: so I wish that wise Christians would not be so simple as to make a mariage betwene a protestant and a papist and say, they hope the children wilbe good christians.
 Quest. Secondly, then I pray you shew me whether among protestants or any true faithful people there be any exception for mariages one with a nother? for so you saide before.

Ans. There are diuers exceptions to be taken against certaine persons, why they may not be ioyned together in mariage, though they be both of them true beleeuers, and of the same religion: but at this present I will onely name two sortes of beleeuers, which may not by the word of God be coupled together in mariage. First those which are so neer of consanguinitie or affinitie, that the Lorde hath forbid them to marie together. Leuit. 18. Secondly, those which for some imperfections or wantes in themselues cannot performe mariage dueties.
 Quest. I pray you declare these two pointes, more largely, and more plainly, for I thinke they are at this day very necessary to be knowen.
Ans.What degrees of consangui nitie or affinitie may not marie. Of the former the Lorde speaketh thus generally, Leuit. 18.6. None shall come neere to any of the kinred of his flesh to vncouer her shame: I am the Lord. The particulars are afterward declared in the same chapter to shew how far this general rule is to be exte^ded. And notwithstanding that euery man may read the text, yet I wil do mine endeuor to lay open the particulars very briefly in these three rules.
First, a man may not mary his mother, his grandmother, or great grandmother, nor his daughter, nor his neece, nor his neeces daughter, eyther by consanguinitie or affinitie.

 Secondly, a man may not marrie his aunt, or his great aunt eyther by consanguinitie or by affinitie; because they are as it were his mothers.
 Thirdly, a man may not marrie his sister by consanguinitie or affinitie.
These three short and plaine rules containe in a manner the summe of all that eighteenth chapter of Leuiticus to vers. 18. where bigamie is sorbidden. Notwithstanding that these three rules may more easily be conceiued of the simple, these two lessons must also be learned. First, that affinitie reacheth not so farre as consanguinitie, but stayeth onely in the husband and in the wife, and goeth no further vnto the consanguinitie of eyther of them. As for example, Dauid the sonne of Ishai, marieth Michal the daughter of Saul. Now all that are of consanguinitie to Dauid, are of affinitie to Michal: and all that are of consanguinitie to Michal, are of affinitie to Dauid, in the same degree of affinitie to Dauid, as they are of consanguinitie to Michal. Dauids father, mother, brother, sister, vncle, aunt, cosen by consanguinitie; is Michals father, mother, brother, sister, vncle, aunt, cosen by affinitie. But this affinitie resteth onely in Michal, and recheth not to any of her consanguinitie. So there
is no affinitie at al betweene the kinred of Dauid and Michal. Ishai and Saul are not made of any affinitie though their children be maried together. There is no affinitie betweene Eliab Dauids brother, and Merab Michals sister: there is no affinitie at all betweene Ionathan Michals brother, and Zeruiah Dauids sister. The reason is, because propagation is by generation, as consanguinitie is spread farre by generation; affinitie is not made by generation, but by coniunction, as the word sheweth, affinis, qui ad alterius finem accedit, he is of affinitie, who commeth to the borders of an other kinred.
Secondly, because sundrie inconueniences may fall out both in consanguinitie and in affinitie, whereby that which is not expresly forbidden in the word of God, may sundrie waiesbe vnco^uenient, as in the mariage of cosin germans in consanguinitie; and if the father marie the daughter, and the sonne the mother, whereby affinitie is made: and because we ought not alwaies to stand precisely vpon that which is lawfull, but especially to respect what also is expedient, as the Apostle admonisheth vs, 1. Cor. 10.23. etc. Therfore it behoueth magistrates to haue due regard of these matters, to determine what is conuenient, and all godly Christians ought
most duetifully to obey whatsoeuer the magistrate decreeth in these cases for edification and for honestie, and for auoyding of inconueniences. For which cause also I desire the table of degrees of mariage, which is set forth by authoritie, may heere be inserted.
 Quest. Who are those, which for want of habilitie to performe the dueties of mariages, may not marie?
Ans. There are specially three sortes of beleeuers,
Persons vnapt for mariage. which are not fit for mariage. First children, who for want of ripe age are not mariagable. Secondly, Eunuches, who cannot giue that due beneuolence, which wedlok requireth. Of these Christ noteth three sortes. First those that are so borne, and haue naturall weakenes and imperfection that they cannot performe mariage dueties. Secondly those that are made chast by men, that is, gelded men, who against their willes are by violence disabled to marie, as it hath beene and is too too common a practise in Asia and Africa to geld men, that they may keepe the wiues and concubines of kings and of great men. Herodotus. lib. 8. writeth that one Panionius made a trade of these Eunuches, and solde them for great summes of money. But himselfe afterward receiued
a iustreward, and was made an Eunuch by Hermotimus, whom before he had offered that iniurie vnto. Volataranus writeth that Cocceius Nerua forbad this wicked practise at Rome. Thirdly, those which make themselues chast for the kingdome of heauen, not as Origen did, of whom Eusebius Lib. 6. cap. 8. writeth, but as Paul did, 1. Cor. 9.27. that is, by fasting, praying, watching, and taking great paines in their calling; beate downe their bodies, and bring it into subiection, and so obtaine of God the gift of continencie, that they may more freely and continually serue God, and not be hindred so much with incumbrances of worldly affaires, as maried persons are. The thirde sorte of them that are vnfitte for mariage, are such as haue some foule contagious, infectious, and vncurable disease, wherby the other party should be infected and depriued of mariage dueties, or else their children, if it were possible for them to haue any, shoulde be most miserable lazers full of all sores and diseases.
 Quest. Hitherto you haue shewed howe this commaundement is transgressed in mariage making, you said also there was some thinges to be obserued in mariage after it was made. What be those thinges?

Ans.Matrimonie ought to be chast and holy. I will note onely two thinges. First, that the husband and the wife be faithfull and true each to other, and remember the couenant of God (as Malachi, Chap. 2.14. admonisheth the husband, and Salomon, Prou. 2.17. admonisheth the wife if you list to reade the places) and not to commit adultery with other, which is the great sinne forbidden in this commandement. The second thing I note in mariageis that the husband and the wife liue chastly, and soberly and honestly in that holy state of mariage; not wantonly, not lasciuiously, not worse then brute beastes. For which cause the Lorde that is holie, biddeth all his people to be holy, Leuit. 19.2. and hath giuen maried persons a special precept, Leuit. 18.19. wherin the Lord respecteth both the chast behauiour of maried persons, and also the welfare of their posteritie, as not only diuines, Pellicanus vpon the forenamed place, and Ierome, Oecolampadius Caluin, and Lauaterus vpon Eze. 18.6. but also a very learned phisician Fernelius Pathologiae. Lib. 6. cap. 9. affirmeth.
 Quest. Now that you haue spoken of lawful contractes, and of holy wedlocke, declare also the faultes committed out of mariage against this commaundement.
Ans. Many waies do vnmaried persons also breake this commaundement, as by fornication
and whoredome, when a single man defileth a maid consenting to his lust contrary to the lawe. Exod. 22.16. or lieth with a woman betrothed to an husband, Deut. 22.23.24. etc. And if the priestes daughter play the whore, she must be burnt, Leuit. 21.19. Also stewes and baudery are forbidden, Leui. 19.29. Deut. 23.17. howsoeuer the Pope dispenseth with them. Also incest is forbidden whereof there are diuers examples, Gen. 35.22. and 38.18. and 2. Sa. 13. and 1. Cor. 5.
Also Sodomy and buggery, and all vnnaturall and monstrous lust, Leuit. 18.22.23. Finally the vow of chastity in them that haue not the gift, is the mother of all filthines, and was first set on foote by Montanus and other knowen heretikes, and afterward defended by beastly papistes.
 Quest. What is there more to be obserued in this commaundement?
Ans. As all these things are forbidden, so are all the meanes vnlawfull, whereby these thinges are procured, or maintained, which are many, and first of all our senses may inflame the lustes of the heart, for by them lust enters into the heart, or rather is there kindled. For as gun-powder is all in aflame so soone as fire toucheth it; so the corruptions of the hearte are inflamed when the obiect of sinne entereth
in at our senses.
 First,
Of the sense of feeling. because the sense of feeling or touching should not haue too much libertie to roaue euery where, there is a prouiso made in a certaine case that a woman shall haue her hand cut off, Deut. 25.11.12.
 Secondly, we may not suffer our eies to wander any way wantonly to looke vpon the beauty of a woman,
Of the eyes. for Christ saith, Math. 5.28. that such wanton lookes are adulteries. And the Apostles Iohn and Peter condemne the lust of the eyes. 1. Iohn. 2.16. and 2. Pet. 2.14. It is noted, Gen. 39.7. that Potiphars wife by casting her wanton eies vpon Ioseph, grewe vnto lust, and desired him to lie with her. Dauid looking from the top of his house at the first vpon a sudden, not thinking any such thing, after feeding the lust of his eye with more looking vpon Bathsheba the wife of Vrias, fell to further lust, and committed foule adulterie with her. But at an other time hee saide, Psalm. 119.37. Turne away my eyes from regarding vanitie. And all men that feare GOD, and so feare their owne weakenes will pray with Dauid, and doe as Iob did, Iob. 31.1. I made a couenant with mine eies: why then shoulde I thinke on a maide?
Thirdly, our cares ought to be shut from
hearing filthie and vnchast speaches,
Of hering lest thereby our heartes should be kindled with lust. For as the wicked stop their eares least they should heare the word of God Psal. 58.4.5. Act. 7.57. or the piteous cry of the poore Pro. 21.13. so they that feare God truely, will stop their ears against al euil words and deedes as Esaiah saith Chap. 33.15. He that walketh in iustice, that stoppeth his ears from hearing of blood, that shutteth his eyes from seeing of euill, he shal dwell on hie. For the holy spirit of God, dwelling in the elect, is grieued with hearing of euill words Ephes. 4.30. And that is the cause why the godly cannot abide to heare euil words.
 Fourthly, our tast must not be satisfied with euery pleasant meate and drinke; for the co^mon prouerbe is, sine Cerere and Baccho friget Venus, Lust is cooled when it wants daintie meates and strong drinke. But Salomon describeth the fruites of eating and specially of drinking wine Prou. 23.27. etc. to the ende of the Chapter, and Vers. 29. saith thus; To whome is we? to whome is sorrow? etc. and Vers. 33. Thine eyes shall looke vpon strange women. Lot that liued honestly before, lay with his owne daughters when he was drunken Gen. 19.32. Dauid made Vriah drunken to prouoke him to lust 2, Sam.
11.13.
Besides these things which moue our senses and from thence enter into our heartes there are many other things which are prouocations to vncleannes.
First strange apparel, that is, both newfangled fashions of apparel, and also such as is not meet for our sexe, as when a man weareth womans or a woman mans aparrel, which the Lord forbiddeth and detesteth as abominable De. 22.5. The woman shall not weare that which perteineth to the man, neither shall a man put on womans raimeut; for all that doe so, are abomination to the Lord thy God. When euery one weareth his owne apparell, that is, the apparel of their sex, then both men and women are newfangle and desirous of strange fashions. And England hath the fashions almost of al other nations rounde about, and yet they are not content with any, but daily affect new guises, and when none can be found, then they renewe the ould, and that of late is become a fine fashion. But they must be content to he are what the Lord saith to the Iewes Zephan. 1.8. And it shalbe in the day of the Lords sacrifice, that I wil visit the princes, and the kings children, and all such as are clothed with strange apparrell. And apply this to their new fashions and see how
they will agree together. It is to be feared, that except men and women breake off their sinnes by repentance, that these their new fashioned deuises neuer fitte their humors so well, but the iudgements of GOD for these and such like sinnes, will sit so close to their backes, that they cannot put it off when they would. But women at al times and in all ages haue surpassed men, as also at this day they doe, both for strangenes of the fashion, and costlynes of the garment it selfe. And that women may see themselues euidently, and truely, I will shew them a clearer and a truer glasse to looke in, then there is any in all the Exchange. This true and cleare glasse is with the prophet Esai Chap. 3. Vers. 16. and the rest following, Because the daughters of Zion are hautie, and walke with stretched out neckes, and with wandring eyes walking and minsing as they goe, and making a tincleing with their feete, therefore shall the Lord make the heades of the daughters of Zion bald etc. I wish al women to read the rest of the Chapter. And if they be loath to look in this glasse, for feare they shoulde see their deformities, yet they had better now se their faults while there is time to wash them away with teares of true repentance, then hereafter to feele the punishment, when
it wilbe too late to repent. For will they, nil they, one day they must looke in this glasse when it shalbe set in their consciences, from whence they can neither remoue it, nor turne their eyes from beholding it. For the Lord wil shortly bring al flesh to iudgement, when none can be hidden from him that sitteth vpon the throne. Wherefore I beseech all women, and specially those that make greater profession of religion, that they would tremble to dishonour God, to offend his little ones, to wound their owne soules, and cause the blessed word of God to be euill spoken of through their apparel, and that they would heare and follow the holy counsell of Paul, 1. Tim. 2.9. likewise, I will, that women adorne themselues in comely apparel, with shamefastnes and modestie, not with broythred haire of gould, or pearles, or costly apparel, but (as becommeth women that professe the feare of God) with good workes: and the counsel of Peter 1. Pet. 3.3. whose appareling let it not be outward, as with broidred haire, and gould put about etc. Man in the beginning was created good, holy pure, cleane, without deformitie, but afterward by his owne sinne he became euill, foule, filthie, vnclene, in so much that Adam and Eua hauing once sinned, were ashamed of God, of themselues
and each of other, and began to hide their filthines and their shame one from another with figge leaues Gen, 3.7. Wherefore afterward the Lord made them coates of skins to hide their shame Gen. 3.21. But now a dayes there is a strange metamorphosis or change. For that which was appointed of God to hide and couer their shame, they haue changed into a thing that sets out their shame to the world. For doeth not the attire, the gesture, and the countenance both of men and women, shew the vncleannes of their heartes and bodies? Salomon saith Prou. 7.10. There came out a woma^ with an harlots attire: whereby he telleth vs that there is some attire which is whorish, and which bewrayeth the iniquitie of the minde.
 Secondly, dauncing, as it is now commonly vsed, is an intisement to folly,
Of dansing as lame^ table experience may teach vs, if we be teach able. For young men and maides dance together and make such matches as bringe forth many bastards, Dinah Iacobs daughter was rauished without dancing. For she went out but to see or to be seene Gen. 34. And if the sight of Dinah inflamed Shechems luste, what will dauncing, kissing, and dalying together more then modestly, doe. The fruite of Salomes wanton and whorish dauncing
(for she was her mothers daughter) before Herode and the rest, was the beheading of Io. Ba. Mah, 14.6. etc. To speake of diuers kinds of dauncing, it needeth not, we haue too many by one. And to answer dauncing defenders, I would knowe of them whether they bring Dauids Psalmes, or baudie ballets with their pipes or other musicall instruments? And whether the dauncers com to refresh and solace their heauy hearts, their sighing souls, their sorrowful minds with some of the ioyfull songs of zion, or they come with disguised platformes to entrappe wanton women, to inflame their burning heartes, to feede their adulterous eyes, and to commit folly and defile their bodies. But if the dauncers be wantons, and come to delight their senses with vnlawful pleasure, and bring filthie and vnchristian sonnets, then no christian may for shame stand in their defence. Wherefore together with dauncing, I will put vnchast rimes, lasciuious songs, and sonnets, as prouokers and allurements to kindle our prone nature to breake this commaundement.
Thirdly,
Of stageplayes stage-playing and enterludes, are euen Satans shop or schoole-house to bring vp prentices and young scholers to the arte and mysterie of whordome and adulterie. For the deuil hath nothing to teach such wickednes
by, but it is all set abroade to open sale vpon the stage, and there it is either declared by foule and wicked words, or els most filthily and impudently resembled by gestures and actions, that there is not a greater mart in the vniuersal world for the diuels wares, then is the stage. The first deuisers of it were the infidell heathens, from thence we receiue it, howsoeuer the Lord forbid a man to weare womans apparrell, surely he doth disalow, that a man either in his owne or in womans apparel should vse adulterous and filthie gestures. Cypryan Lib. 1. Epist. 10. demaunded by Eucratius, what he thought of a man, that began to be ashamed of his playing vpon the stage, gaue it ouer, and now did but only traine vp young scholers priuately in his chamber, to make them fit for the stage, answered, that man was a maister non erudiendorum, sed perdendoru^ pueroru^, not of instructing, but of destroying youth, and therefore such a man was not worthie to be of the fellowship of the church. Tertullian Lib. de spectaculis saith, Theatrum proprie sacrarium veneris est, the theater, (or stage) properly is the chappell wherein whordome is committed. And a little after in the same booke he saith, Theatrum est priuatum consistorium impudicitiae, vbi nihil probatur, quam
quod alibi non probatur, The theater (or stage) is a priuate closet for dishonestie, where nothing is allowed but that which els where is disalowed. Chrysostome in his sixt homelie vpon Genesis, threatneth to excommunicate his auditors for running to playes except they leaue it. The counsell of Arles in France about the time of the Nicene cousel Can. 4. and. 5. and also the third counsel of Carthage, Can. 35. decree that stage-players are to be excommunicated. And seing there is not more filthie speach vsed in any other place, I will here leaue al filthie communication vpon the stage, and not make any seuerall speach of it, though there be sufficient occasion. 
 Quest. Seing you haue spoken thus much of the causes, I pray you let me heare somthing also of the effects of adulterie and vncleanenes.
Ans. The fruites or effectes of such vncleanenes must needes be many and loathsom. For as the tree is, such is the fruite. But of many, I will only name a few.
 First,
Returning to our vomit. man borne in sinne, polluted, and defiled, through the grace of God in Christ and the powerfull operation of the holy Ghost, is purged and made cleane, and in testimonie thereof receiueth the sacrament
of baptisme to assure him of his purgation and regeneration. But he that committeth fornication or adultery defileth himselfe againe, and it commeth to passe vnto him, according to the true prouerbe, The dog is returned to his owne vomit: and the sowe that was washed, to her wallowing in the mire, 2. Pet. 2.22. And this is one of the fruites of sinne. The Lord that washed vs from our sinnes, requireth of vs holinesse, as he is holy, Leuit. 20.7.26. and 1. Thess. 4.3.7. If a man be swept and purged, and after supper vncleane spirits do possesse him againe, the latter ende of that man wilbe worse then the beginning was, Luke. 11.24. And if I named no moe fruites of whoredome but this onely, it were sufficient to moue a godly Christian to possesse his vessell in holinesse.
 Secondly,
Banishment of Gods spirit. our bodies are the members of Christ, 1. Cor. 6.15. but he which coupleth himselfe with an harlot, is one bodie with her, and maketh himselfe that before was a member of Christ, nowe to be the member of an harlot. Which is not to come out of the hall into the kitchin, but out of heauen into hell. Againe our bodies are the Temples of the holy Ghost, 1. Cor. 6.19. and of the liuing God, 2. Cor. 6.16. and the Spirit of God dwelleth in vs, working our regeneration and sanctification.
Now they that giue themselues to vncleannes, do not only grieue the spirit of God which is in them, but they labour to expell and driue him out of them. For he will not dwell in such defiled and filthie bodies. Dauid once ouertaken by the infirmitie of his flesh, and fallen into this horrible sinne of adultery was so depriued of the comfortable feeling of the spirit of God, which he had felt in former times abundantly, that, though Nathan the prophet said vnto him in the name of the Lord, The Lorde also hath put away thy sinnes. 2. Sam. 12.13. he neuerthelesse cried pittifully and with a heauy heart, vnto the Lord and said, Create in me a cleane heart, O God, and renew a right spirit within me. Cast me not away from thy presence and take not thy holy spirit from me. Restore to me the ioy of thy saluation, and stablish me with thy free spirit, Psal. 51.10.11.12. This then is an other fruit of vncleannes, euen to banish the spirit of grace out of our bodies (but if any man haue not the spirit of Christ, the same is not his, Rom. 8.9.) and to be without comfort, and without feeling of Gods fauor, and of the spirit of God, yea though we doe so truely repent, that our heartes inwardly bleed for sorrowe, and though the ministers of the word tell vs in the wordes and in the name of the Lord, that our sinnes are pardoned.
And if the penitent heart and heauy soule can very hardly be comforted, though the Lord send vs word by his seruantes that he hath forgiuen vs our sinnes; howe shall they haue any consolation at all, whose heartes are so hardened through custome of sinne that they cannot nor doe not repent, and to whom the Lord neuer promised any mercy or forgiuenes of sinne by his seruants.
 Thirdly, we are turned from darknes to light,
Disinheriting of our selues of the king dome of heauen. and from the power of satan to God, and haue receiued forgiuenes of our sinnes, and inheritance among them that are sanctified, Act. 26.18. and are become the sonnes of God, Gal. 3.26. and are made the heires of God, euen fellow heires with Christ, Rom. 8.17. But he that committeth sin is of the diuell, 1. Ioh. 3.8. and shalbe his sonne, his heire and partaker of his kingdome of darknes. And this is an other fruit of adulterie, euen to change our estate, and of the sonnes of God, to be made the sonnes of the diuell; and of heires of God, to be inheritours of condemnation. For this ye know, saith Paul. Ephes. 5.5. That no whoremonger, neither vncleane person, nor coueteous person, which is an idolater, hath any inheritance in the kingdome of Christ and of God. And againe. 1. Cor. 6.9. Neither fornicators, nor idolaters, nor adulterers, nor wantons, nor
buggerers, nor theeues, nor couetous, nor drunkards, nor raylers, nor extorcioners shall inherit the kingdome of God. Wherefore Peter admonisheth vs to abstaine from fleshly lustes, because they fight against our soules,  1. Pet. 2.11.
Fourthly,
Infamy and pouerty. concerning this present life also, and our conuersation among men, all manner of fornication bringeth with it two thinges which discredite men. First, an euill name; and secondly, losse of worldly welth. For not onely among Christians, but euen among heathen pagans adultery and fornication are odious, and most seuerely punished in many places, as it may appeare in the story of Abimelech, when he tooke Sarah to be his wife. The Saxones, and Germans before they were Christians, vsed most seuerely to punish adulterers with death, sometimes hanging them in chains ouer a fier till they were dead, and sometime burying them aliue in the earth. The Romans punished them with death, and Orosius, Lib. 2. cap. 8. saith, that Popilia a virgin for committing fornication, was put into the earth being aliue, and so buried and put to death. Neyther doth the infamie eyther soone cease, for his reproch shall neuer be put away, Prou. 6.33. or else rest vpon the sinner alone, but the children so vnlawfully begotten, haue a note and name of ignominie set vpon them, and are called bastards,
that is to say, strangers, because they are strangers from their fathers inheritance (for a bastard cannot inherit, neyther among Christians, nor among infidels) and because they are straungers in some sorte from the congregation of the Lordes people, as it is written, Deutro. 23.2. A bastard shall not enter into the congregation of the Lorde, namely, to beare office or to be aduanced to dignitie. And that adulterers and fornicators consume all their wealth, and waste their substance and their inheritaunce, which should be for them, for their whole familie, and for their lawfull heires or successours after them, wofull experience sheweth, and the holy Ghost witnesseth the same, Prouerbes. 6.26. For because of the whorish woman, a man is brought to a morsell of breade. And in another place, Hee that feedeth harlots, wasteth his substance, Prouerbes. 29.3. And this is an other fruite of whooredome. Wherefore if men eyther desire saluation in the kingdome of heauen, or feare condemnation in hell fire with the Diuell and his angels; if they regard eyther their bodies, or their soules; eyther themselues, or their posteritie; eyther their good name, or their wealth, there is greate cause why they shoulde auoyde all manner of whoredome
and fornication, and liue in holinesse and so brietie.
 Quest. What is there more to be considered in this commaundement?
Ans. Hitherto I haue shewed how this commaundement is broken, together with some fewe causes and effectes: nowe we shoulde also speak of the holy keeping of our owne vessels in holines, as the Apostle willeth vs, 1. Thes. 4.3. and so keepe this commaundement. For seeing God hath called vs by so holy a calling, we ought to cleanse our selues from all filthines of the flesh and spirit, and grow vp vnto al holines in the feare of God, 2. Co. 7.1. that our whole spirit and foule and bodie, may be kept blameles vnto the comming of the Lorde Iesus Christ. 1. Thes. 5.23. But I will leaue this to euery mans consideration.
 Quest. What is the punishment for them that transgresse this commandement?
Ans. Adulterie, and rauishment are to be punished with death, Gen. 38.24. Leuit. 20.10. Deut. 22.21.22. Prou. 6.27.29. But if a single man and a maide commit follie, the punishment was not death to eyther of them, because the man made recompence, and the maids father was satisfied, either with mariage of his daughter, or else with a dowrie, which
was fiftie shekels of siluer, Exod. 22.16. Deut. 22.28. The Church excommunicateth them till they repent publikely.
Thou shalt not steale. 
 Quest. What is the summe of this commaundement?
Ans. The sixt commandement gaue charge for preseruation of mans life; the seauenth for the honestie and chastitie of the bodie, to keepe it holy and vndefiled; now the Lord commeth a degree lower, and sheweth, that he doth not onely care for our liues, and for our bodies that they may be kept holy, but also for our goods, and cattell, our corne, our wares, our gold, our siluer, and whatsoeuer we haue that they may be in safety. The very consideration whereof ought to breed in vs all, first thankfulnes to God, for that he vouchsafeth so graciously to prouide for al that we possesse: secondly more faith in his prouidence and protection, knowing that who so dwelleth vnder the defence of the most hie, shal abide vnder the shadow of the almighty, as the prophet saith, Psa. 91.1. thirdly, greater loue to our brethren that because the Lord loueth them so entirely, and preserueth all they haue, we should for his sake loue our brethren, and doe them good. And this exceeding loue of the Lord
also is manifest, in that he hath sent magistrates as his owne lieutenantes, with great authoritie to protect vs, and all that we haue in safety, as was noted in the fift commaundement.
 Quest. How many waies doe men steale our goods from vs?
Ans. This is a harde question, because there are infinite waies to doe euill: notwithstanding I will note three waies of stealing, vnder which are manie contained. The first is by violence: the second by fraude: the third by vsurie, which is both by violence, and by fraud.
Quest. What is violent stealing? or who steale by violence? 
Ans. First, they that by strong hand, and by their power and might take other mens goods from them. Such are the eues and robbers that openly steale and rob at no one day in the hie waies or in any other place, as the Shabeans, and the Chaldeans which robbed Iob. Chapter. 1.15.17. Such are they that rob vpon the seas without a lawfull letter of mart. For if any man hauing sustained no losse by any aduersarie, of a meere coueteous minde to get wealth by right or by wronge, will come to the magistrate, and before him make an open
lowd ly and say or swe are, that he hath sustained losse, when he neuer lost penie vpon the seas and so abuse authoritie to purchase a letter of mart, that man may not thinke he can deceiue God. But if this be the beginning of his voiage, in abusing Gods lieutenant, in lying or in swearing falsely; what successe may he look for or what blessing, (I might say curssing) may he look for at gods hands? Nay with what conscience dare such a man enter the seas, wherein so mightie workes of the Lord are manifest euery moneth. Also if a man hauing a lawful letter of mart go beyond his co^mission, and count all fish that comes neere his net, and catcheth whatsoeuer he can get by mayn strength, where is this mans conscience? or what answeare will he make vnto the Lorde? It is meere foolish and irreligious to say as many doe, such a one is an enimie to God, to the gospell, to our nation, and to me, therfore I may lawfully rob him. For the Lorde hath neuer saide so in all his word. It is a meere deuise of thine owne, O man whosoeuer thou art, that saist so. For then say thus the murderer, the adulterer, the blasphemous swearer, is an aduersarie to God, to religion, and the gospell, to the welfare of our Land, and therefore I will kill him, or I will rob him. No, no, it belongeth to the magistrate to
punish him, and not to thee. The Lorde hath a greate number of aduersaries vpon earth, but no man may do them any violence but when the Lord biddeth, if then thou not commaunded by the magistrate, who is Gods vicegerent, yea forbid by the magistrate, (for when thou goest beyond thy co^mission, thou contrariest the magistrates commaundement) wilt for couetuousnes sake tak violently whatsoeuer thou ca^st, thou hast no warrant for thy doing. The Lord can, and will, and doth punish his aduersaries, when, by whom, and by what maner it pleaserh him. Therefore except thou hast beene of the Lords counsell and knowest his will, seeke not too hastily to inrich thy selfe by robbery. Moreouer when any vnlawfully rob vpon the seas, and bring greate purchases into the land and into their houses, let the cursse neuer beforgotten, which the prophet Zachariah Chap. 5. saw in a vision of a flying booke, which goeth forth ouer the whole earth for euery one that stealeth shalbe cut off aswel on this side, as on that; and euery one that sweareth, shalbe cut off aswell on this side, as on that, I will bring it forth, saith the Lord of hostes, and it shall enter into the house of the thiefe, and into the house of him
that falsely sweareth by my name: and it shal remaine in the middest of his house, and shall consume it, with the timber thereof and the stones thereof.
Such are they that hauing kings treasures in their hands, runne away with it, as Pactias did with the treasure of King Cyrus Herodot. Lib. 1. or being trusted with the treasures of Colleges or corporations, goe away with it.
Such be sheep-stealers, horse-stealers, men-stealers and a greate number moe.
Such be the mightie that oppresse the poor as Ahab oppressed Naboth. Robbe not the poore: because he is poore, neither oppresse the afflicted in iudgement. For the Lord will defende their cause, and spoile the soule of those that spoile them. Prou. 22.22. And such as helpe them in their oppressions are their companions.
Such are they that destroy other mens goods, as they that burne mens howses or their corne. Exod. 22.6. or that kil mens cattell Exod. 21.33.35. Leuit. 24.18.21. Absolom burnt Ioabs barley 2. Sam. 14.31.
Such are church-robbers, which take away the manteinance of the ministerie. It is a destruction for a man to deuour that
which is sanctified and after the vowes to inquire Prou. 20.25.
 Secondly, they that haue any thing in their hands that belongs to others, and yet withhould it, and deliuer it not, as the ministers of the word which hauing the dispensation thereof committed to them, doe not preach, but by silence withhould from the people the bread of life, and so shut vp the kingdome of heauen that neither they enter in themselues, nor suffer them that woulde. Wherefore except they repent of their former negligence, and hereafter amend, they shall feele that cursse which Christ for the same cause pronounced against the scribes and pharises Math. 23, 13. Therefore behould, I will come against the prophets, saith the Lord, (Ierem. 23.30.) that steale my word euery one from his neighbour. And Christ Iohn. 10.1.8. saith plainely, they are theeues and robbers. Such be papists that conceal the death of Christ as much as they may, and extol mans merits, and that shadow the second commaundement, to the intent to set vp their images.
They that haue receiued of their neighbour monie or any other thing to keepe, but either denie it, or deferre to restore it, when it is demaunded againe. Exod. 22.

They that find their neighbours purse by the way, or his beast straying abroade, and do not restore it, but keepe it to them selues.
They that being executors of willes and testaments, or otherwise put in trust with any thing, doe defraud widdows and orphanes, and withhould from them that which belongs to them.
They that being rich, and seing the poore and needie, shut their compassion, and withhould Gods blessings from the^. The Lord saith Pro. 3.27. withhould not the good from the owners thereof.
They that denie or deferre to pay their dettes to the greate losse of them that lent or sould any thing, and gaue them daie for the paiment.
They that keepe backe the seruants wages Leuit. 19.13. Deutro. 24.15. Iam. 5.4.
They that withhould their neighbours pledge
They that refuse to let their neighbor haue corne or other thing for their money, as many doe, they that defende not their neighbour from iniurie, when they may.
 Quest. Who are they that steale by fraude?
Ans. They that in selling vse false weights and measurs Leuit. 19.25. Deut. 25.13. Pro. 20.23.
that sell corrupt ware for good, and counterfaite for true Amos. 8.6. that defraude the simple and ignorant, that take double the worth of the thing in mens necessities.
They that in bying dispraise that which is good, to get it for a little Prou. 20.14. that perceiuing poore men must needes sel, will not giue halfe the worth. Ingrossors which gather all the corne or other commodities of the countrie into their owne handes that no man shall haue any to sell but themselues, and then they make their owne price as they will. Forestallers, which meet the commodities of the countrie by the way; and buy it before it come at the market, whereby the price of things is inhaunced, and the market is not serued sufficiently.
They that are purse-bearers and purloine some to themselues, as Iudas did.
They that buie or sell iustice, which ought not to be bought or sould.
They that game by vnlawfull games.
In a word, the breade of deceite is sweete to a man: but afterward his mouth shalbe filled with grauil Pro 20.17.
 Quest. What say you now of vsurie?
Ans. It is both a violent and a fraudulent theft.

 Quest. Some thinke it to be a lawfull trade; what thinke you of it? for you seeme at the first to condemne it.
Ans. I will answere you by leisure, and by degrees. And first I will shew in what things vsurie doth properly consist: secondly what it is: Thirdiy how many kinds of vsurie there be: and fourthly whether it be lawfull.
 Quest. In what things doth vsurie consist?
Ans. Vsurie cannot properly nor truely be saide to be in buying, in selling, in choping, or changing, or in any such bargaining. For in all these and such like there may be, and there is, fraud, guile, deceit, cosenage, cruelty, oppression, and iniurie; but no vsurie. Neither is there vsurie in hiering out of houses, lands, cattell, or any other thing, but in setting, letting, hyring, there is fraude and oppression, as in the former. It remaineth then that vsurie in properly and truely in lending only, and in no other thing whatsoeuer. But of lending there are twol ortes properly called by two seuerall names in latin, though we haue but one english word for them both. For which cause I must of necessitie vse moe wordes then I woulde, that I may make a plaine difference betwen
these two kindes of lending. The one kind of lending is, when the same thing that was lente, is to be restored againe, and not an other thing for it, as if a man lend his neighbour his cloak, his gowne, his horse, his carte, or any such other thing he looketh to haue the verie same againe which was lent, and not an other for it. The thing that is thus lent is properly called commodatum in latin. The other kind of lending is, when the same thing that was lent, is not looked for againe, but an other as good by weight, measure or number, as for example, a man lendeth his neighbour a loafe of bread, which the borower taketh as his owne, and eateth, and restoreth an other loafe for it as good and by weight.
