Againe a man boroweth a bushell of wheat and spendeth it, and after restoreth an other bushell as good and by measure. Againe, a man borroweth twentie shillings and layeth it out for necessary things, and after restoreth for it so much mony againe, and by number. And this lending in latine is properly termed mutuum. This also must be vnderstood, that all lending is free, and for nothing, but of good will: for if it be otherwise lente then franckly and for nothing, it hath another name. Now vsurie is properly in this latter kind of lending, and onely in it not in the
former, nor in any other kinde of dealing that is betweene men, whatsoeuer it be. The former kinde of lending is franke and free, of good will, for nothing: if it belent for any thing, then it loseth his name and is called, hired, for it is hired for such a thing, and for so much. This latter kinde of lending is also franke, and free, of good will, for nothing. For if it be lent for something, it loseth his name, and is most properly and truely called vsurie. And thus you see plainely that vsurie consisteth in no dealing that is between men, but onely in lending, yea, and in this latter kinde of lending onely. And to make it more plaine, it is not alwaies in this kinde of lending, but onely, when this lending, that ought to be franke and free, is abused to some gaine. So then vsurie is the abuse of this charitable lending.
 Quest. Secondly, then according to your promise, define vsurie, and tell me what it is.
Vsurie is a couenanted gaine for this latter kinde of lending, which is called mutuum in latine. And in this short definition you must marke these two things diligently. First that it is a couenanted gaine. For when a man lendeth frankely, and freely, of meere good
will, of conscience to succour and helpe him that is in neede, according as God commandeth; if the borrower restoring the valewe of the thing againe in due time and according to his promise, and according to his habilitie, wil in such a case freely giue something to the lender, because he hath gained much by that which was lent him freely, it is not vsurie in such a case to receiue that the borower frankly giueth: but this case is so rare, as it scarse needes to be named. Therefore to make it vsurie, there must be a couenanted gaine.
Secondly, that it is a couenanted gaine in the latter kind of lending onely, and not in the former
 Quest. Thirdly then, how many kinds of vsurie are there?
I know but onely one kinde of vsurie, and no moe; which is worth the marking, and hereafter will giue great light for the deciding of the controuersie, whether it be lawfull or no. For though some men committe vsurie in money, some in corne, some in bread, and others in other thinges, which make a distinction of the obiect of vsurie; yet the nature of vsurie is not by these thinges deuided. Wherefore I say againe, there is but one kind of vsurie onely.
 Quest. Now lastly, whether is vsurie a thing
lawfull or no?
Ans. I knowe it is no small controuersie among many at this day, and hath beene a long time, neuerthelesse because the handling of it falleth necessarily into the eight commandement, I will speake plainely what I thinke, and so referre and submit my selfe and my reasons to the censures of the godly learned in any place. I am of this opinion, that to take couenanted increase or lucre for lending of any thing that is put to vsurie is simplie vnlawfull, vnderstanding such kinde of lending as I named before, which in latine is properly called mutuum. For vsurie is not properly, neyther can be in that other kinde of lending, which is called commodatum. I am constrained to vse the latine wordes, because we haue but onely one English worde for these two kindes of lending. My reasons which moue me to thinke that vsurie is altogether vnlawfull, are these.
 First, the worde of the Lorde, Exod. 22.25. Leuit. 25.35. manifestly forbiddeth to lende vpon vsurie, for vsurie, or for lucre and gaine to any of the Lordes people, which are decayed and brought vnto pouerty, that they are not able to maintaine their estate. The wordes be these, Exod.
22.25. If thou lend money to my people, that is, to the poore with thee, thou shalt not be as an vsurer vnto him: yee shall not impose vsurie vppon him. And Leuit, 25.35. Moreouer if thy brother be impouerished, and fallen in decay with thee, thou shalt relieue him, yea the stranger and soiourner, that he may liue with thee. Thou shalt take no vsurie of him, nor vantage but thou shalt feare thy GOD, that thy brother may liue with thee. Thou shalt not giue him thy money to vsurie, nor lende him thy vitailes for increase.
 Secondly, in Deut, 23.19. it is thus written: Thou shall not giue to vsurie to thy brother: as vsurie of money, vsurie of meate, vsurie of any thing that is put to vsurie. Vnto this stranger thou maist lend vpon vsurie, but thou shalt not lend vpon vsurie to thy brother that the Lorde thy God may blesse thee in all that thou settest thine hande to, in the lande whither thou goest to possesse it. In these wordes there is a generall opposition betweene this stranger, that is, the cursed Cananites, and their brethren the Iewes. Where this opposition is to be obserued. For when the Lorde permitteth the Iewes to lend vpon vsurie to that stranger, he doth not meane all strangers, as the Iewes wrest the place, euen to this
day. For in the place before cited, Leuit. 25.35. the Lorde forbad the Iewes to giue vpon vsurie, not onely to their brethren the Iewes, but also to the stranger and soiourner, that is, to such strangers and soiourners as seeing the great workes of the Lorde and his fearefull iudgementes vpon Aegypt, forsooke Aegypt and went out with the Israelites Exo. 12.38. And many of them were circumcised, and receiued the religion of the Israelites, and worshipped the God of Israel. Such also were Moses his father in lawe and those that came with him, and dwelt with the Israelites and worshipped GOD as they did, and afterwarde in the scripture are called Kenites. Such also were others that ioyned themselues to the Israelites and dwelt amonge them. Wherefore it is often said concerning many thinges, that there shall be one lawe for the Iewe borne and for the stranger. But when the Lord permitted the Israelites to lend vpon vsury to that straunger, he meaneth onely those cursed people, the Hittites, the Girgashites, the Amorites, the Canaanites, the Perizites, the Hinites, and the Iebusites, whom the Israelites, were commaunded to destroy, Exod. 23.27. etc. Numb. 3.52. Deut. 7.1.2.16. and no other strangers. Now as we see to what strangers
they might lende vpon vsurie: so we must knowe that to their brethren whether they were Iewes borne or strangers and soiourners that dwelt among them, they might not lende vpon vsurie. Then whether they be rich or poore, that is no distinction to make vsurie lawfull or vnlawfull: but whether they be of those seauen cursed nations or not. For if they be of those cursed people, it was lawfull to lend to them vpon vsurie: if they were not of them, it was vnlawfull. And thus the Lorde sheweth by a distinction of people, namely of these cursed, and of all others, to whome it was lawfull, and to whome it was vnlawfull to lende vpon vsurie. This newe founde distinction of rich men and poore men was neuer made by the Lord, neyther hath it any warrant of the word of God, but onely some men couetously minded, haue coyned it of late yeares. And if we will approue our consciences before almightie God, we must say, Lorde, thine owne mouth hath spoken it, thou hast commaunded it, it is written for my direction and instruction in such a place of the scripture, and therefore, Lorde, I did it, else I woulde neuer haue attempted it, no not to saue my life, much lesse to increase my wealth. And whatsoeuer or whosoeuer shall otherwise shift
it of before men, shal euen be speechles before God. Neuerthelesse this is to be confessed, that the intendment of the holy Ghost in the forenamed places, is to forbid lending vpon vsurie to the poore: but we must hereewithall take the reason; because it was then practised onely vpon the poore, and it was an vncouth and vtterly vnknowen or heard of monster, that rich men should borrow of rich men vpon vsurie, and that of meere coueteousnes. For though there were many greate sinnes among the Israelites, yet this monster I suppose was then vnhatched No this kinde of vsurie is not once mentioned so much as in the last prophets, when perhaps such seede of cruell couetousnes was sowen, as we now reape the fruite of. But we must vnderstand that it is not onely the labourer that by his daily worke getteth his liuing, nor yet the meane husbandman, that is called poore, or said to be impouerished in the scripture; but also the rich farmer, the wealthy marchant, the landed gentleman, or others of greate calling, sometimes fall into decay, and wax poore, so that they haue as great neede to borrowe, as anie poore labourer. For the GOD of heauen that ruleth all thinges after the counsell of his will, sometimes bringeth downe great men, and exalteth
them of lowe degree. Wherefore the Lords meaning is, that if thy brother (whether he be labourer, artificer, husbandman, yeoman, marchant, gentleman, or nobleman) be impouerished and decaied, and his state beginne to fall, that then thou shoulde lend vnto him freely to helpe him, to vphold him, to maintaine his lawfull state and calling, but thou shalt not impose vsurie vpon him, that is, when he is falling, thou shalt not strike him downe and treade him vnder thy feete, but thou shalt take him by the hande, vpholde him from falling, and let thy strength, thy wealth support his weaknesse. For the Lorde offereth thee such an occasion to trie thee, whether thou wilt obey the Lorde thy GOD, and relieue him that hath neede of thy helpe, or thou wilt answere him, as Nabal answered Dauid, 1. Sam. 25.10. And for this cause I beseech all that feare GOD, to consider the reason which the Lorde vseth, Deutro. 23.20. That the Lorde thy God may blesse thee in all that thou settest thine hande to, to perswade men, freely and without vsurie to lende to them that are impouerished and decaied, as if the Lord had said, as thou would haue me to blesse thee, so helpe thou and relieue him that is decayed.

 Thirdly, that which the Lord permitted the Iewes to doe for the punishment and destruction of the cursed Canaanites, cannot possiblely be turned to a blessing to Gods people. But the Lord permitted the Iewes to lend vpon vsurie to the Canaanites for a kind of punishment to destroy them withall. Therefore if one brother lend to another vpon vsurie, whether he be rich or poore, it is to punish, and to destroy him, as wofull experience teacheth vs how true this is: for many whole families, man, wife, and children are destroyed and vndone by vsurie. The gallows are permitted and approued to the sheriffe or to some other vnder him to hang vp theeues, murderers, and such other malefactors, but God forbid that we should thinke them meete for good men. And so vsurie was permitted to the Iewes as a gallous, as a gibbet, or such other punishment to destroy the Canaanites, and how then can it be good for the Lords people.
 Fourthly, I reason thus. Where the principall is not warranted, there ought to be no couenanted and warranted gaine. But in this kinde of lending, which is called mutuum, and wherein only vsurie is, the principall is not warranted. And therfore there is no warrant in the word of God for vsutie.
That the principall ought not to be warranted, it may appeare two wayes. First by co^pariso^, and secondly by scripture. The co^parison shalbe betweene those two kindes of lending, wherof I spake before. For if in the former kind of le^ding, (where the same thing that was borrowed, is to be restored againe, and wherein lesse fauour is shewed to the borrower) the principall be not warranted, then much lesse ought it to be warranted in this second kinde of lending, where greater fauour is shewed to the borrower. But in the former kind of lending the principal is not warranted, if it perish without any falt of the borrower as it is Exod. 22.14. And if a man borrow ought of his neighbour, and it be hurt, or else dye. The owner thereof not being present (and therfore might suspect it perished through the misusage of the borrower) he (that is, the borrower) shal surely make it good. If the owner therof be by, he (that is the borrower shal not make it good. Therfore in this second kinde of lending the principall ought much lesse to be warranted. The scripture to proue that the principall ought not to be warranted in this second kinde of lending, is written Deut. 15. where the Lord commaundeth, that euery seuenth yere should be a yere of freedom for diuers things.
And if any man had lent any thing to his brother, which the borrower was not able to pay againe before the yere of libertie, that then the lender should freely remit and forgiue the debter the principall; the wordes are these Deut: 15.2. And this is the manner of the freedome: euery creditour shall quite the loue of his hand which he hath lent to his neighbour: he shall not aske againe of his neighbour, nor of his brother: for the yere of the Lords freedome is proclaimed. Seeing then the principal is not warranted, but must be remitted and forgiuen, if the borrower be not able to repaye it againe, according to Christs wordes Luke 6.35. lende looking for nothing agaiue, there is no scripture to allow lucre and gaine for the principall,  and so no vsurie alowed by the word of God.
Fiftly, I finde but one kinde of vsurie only in the scripture, and that alwayes condemned, neuer approued, as it may appeare in the three places alledged before out of the law, and Psal. 15.5. and. 109.11. Prou. 28.8. Eze. 8.13. and 22.12. and wheresoeuer else it is mentioned. Wherefore vsurie is not lawfull by the word of God. 
 Sixtly, I saide before, that vsurie is the abuse of lending. For when men couenante for some lucre and gaine for the lending of
that which the Lord commaundeth to be lent freely, and without any vsurie, then they abuse lending. Now the abuse of a thing cannot be iustified, and therefore vsurie is condemned.
 Seauenthly, vsurie is a thing so repugnant to nature and reason, that not only Christian nations, but heathens also, whose chiefest scholmaister is that instinct which is grauen in their natures, doe disalow ssurie throughout the world. For I neuer heard or read of any that doe approue of vsurie. Wherefore that which the Lord disaloweth in his word, and all nations vnder heauen mislike, cannot be lawful, neither ought Christians to defend it. And these are my reasons.
 Quest. But are not many worthie men in the Church of God, of a contrary iudgment?
Ans. Not any at all that I knowe of. For where diuers worthie men seeme to allow vsurie with som caueates and exceptions, I am of their minde, but I must ad this with all, that when they haue hampered, and hemmed in the vsurers on euery side, with such holy and religious caueats and lessons, they alter the qualitie of it, and make it noe vsurie, but a lawful kinde of trade and dealing. There are many strong poisons which the learned phisitian can so qualifie, that a
sicke person may take a potion wherein some of the poyson is. And so holy men of God haue done, and doe temper and qualifie the vsurers poison that they make thereof a holsom medicine for many distressed persons.
Quest. Whether is it lawfull to borrow vpon vsurie?
Ans. I will answer you this question by leasure, and by little, as I haue done the former. For there are diuers sorts of borrowers, al whose conditions are not alike, and therefore one answere wil not serue them al. And specially there are three sorts of borrowers. 
 First,
Som borrow of necessitie some men decayed or in greate distresse and neede, are constrained to borrow, either to supplie present wants, or to preuent great inconueniences. And because in these daies charitie is rather dead, then could, they must either borrow vpon vsurie, or haue nothing lent vnto them at al. These mens cases are to be pitied, and the Lord biddeth vs to lende vnto then freely, and forbiddeth vs to take any vsurie of them Leuit. 25.55. But the are not any where in the scripture forbidden to borrow vpon vsurie, when they cannot otherwise haue to supply their necessitie, no more then they are forbidden to
to giue a greate deale more for a thing then it is worth, when a miserly wretched oppressor knowing their present neede, and that they cannot haue that they want any where but of him, will not sell to them but for doubble the price. 
 Secondly,
Some borrow of couetousnes. others that are welthie and verie wel able to liue themselues, and also to relieue others, doe of meere couetousnes borrow greate summes of monie vpon vsurie, as especially three sortes of men do, first gentlemen of greate Landes and liuings, secondly, rich fermers and yeomen, thirdly, wealthie marchants. And that because they will buie all the Lands that lies neere them, or are co^modious for them, because the poore shall haue no place to dwel in, but by their leaue and good liking, because they wilbe richer then their fellowes, and generally because they are not co^tented with that blessed state the Lord hath set them in this life, and because they are not thankful to God that hath made the^ able to liue very plentifully, and to be co^fortable and helpeful to many besides, whereas he could, and can, and sometime doeth for mens ingratitude, pull dowen vnsatiable couetous men, and setteth vp the meeke and lowlie. And I thinke these borrowers vpon vsurie sinne greatly, and that
for two causes,
The first cause which moueth me so to thinke, is the couetous greedie minde, that moueth them to borrow vpon vsurie, when in trueth they haue no neede, and therefore ought to be content with their estate, and leaue that for others to buie and purchase which of themselues they are not able to co^passe but by this vnlawfull meanes of borrowing vpon vsurie.
The second cause is taken from the effects that follow vpon this vnlawfull borrowing vpon vsurie which are many but I will at this present obserue two effects onlie.
First these borrowers vpon vsurie, mainteine the cursed vsurer, as the receiuer doth maintaine the these. For though there are many of the first sort of borrowers, whom necessitie constraineth to borrow, and the moe a greate deale by these meanes, yet they all are not able to hould so many vsurers plowes going all the yere long as we see there are, but many vsurers should be constrained to cease from making so long furrowes vpon poore mens backes, and buckle themselues to some better trade.
The second effect is, that the poore are greatly hindred, and halfe vndone, by reason that these men borrow vpon vsurie. For
these borrowers vpon vsurie, giue so excessiuely much for the lone of monie, that they must either giue vp housekeeping, and take a chamber in the corner of a house in London for a time, or else greately diminish their house-keeping, that by pinching and sparing that way, they may get vp somwhat towards the paying of the excessiue vsurie, which the tormenting vsurer hath bound them vnto, Whereupon it followeth that the poore which were wont to be set on worke, no we liue idlie, and without maintenance, and which were wont to be relieued with much comfort, are now destitute, and shut out of the doores, and sigh and grone vnto the Lord for very miserie. O would to God these rich borrowers vpon vsurie would thinke it a more glorious thing for them to feede and cloath the poore members of Iesus Christ with some parte of that great wealth the Lord hath made them stewards of, euen for this cause among others, that they should comfort the needie Prou. 3.27. and so honour God with their riches Prou. 3.9. then by vnlawfull meanes to purchase much vpon earth to the great hurt and hindrance of the poore. For this pinching in house keeping to fill vp the vsurers bagges, is the vndoing of the poore.

But besides these two generall effectes, each of the borrowers vpon vsurie, hath his proper and peculiar effectes. The gentlemen borrowing vpon vsurie to buy more landes, racketh his rentes, and makes all the poore tenants to pay the vsurie. The farmer or yeoman selleth his corne and his cattell so much the dearer, and makes the buyer to pay his vsury. The marchant inhaunseth the price of his wares, and who so needes his marchandize, must pay his vsurie. And thus the cursed vsurer (for he is no where not so much as once blessed in the word of God, but continually cursed, besides the pitifull sighing of the poore which sendeth to God a daily curse against him into heauen) he is the head of all this mischiefe; the rich bowers, they are his vpholders; and lastly the poore commonaltie, they haue all the burden laid on their backs, though of al others they be least able. And thus the vsurers crooked plowe goeth forward.
 The third sort of borrowers vpon vsurie, are those Salomon speaketh of, Prou. 13.7.
Some borrow of hypocrisie There is that maketh himselfe poore, hauing great riches. For because they will pay no tribute to Caesar, beare no ordinarie charges of the common wealth, nor pay any man his owne, if they can once finger other mens goods, therefore wil they eyther borrow somthing of a vsurer,
or at the least so giue it out, that men might pitie their case, and let them alwaies scape scotfree. But these whiners neede rather the magistrates authority, then any other answere, and therefore I will leaue such hypocriticall michers without any further answere.
 Quest. What say you of the vsurer?
Ans. I will referre you for answere to, Pro. 28.8. to the booke of the preacher, Cap. 5. ver. 12.13.14.15. and to Ierm. 17.11. which places if you list to read the^, wil answer you fully.
 Quest. What say you of restitution where iniurie hath beene done?
Ans. I wish you to reade the seauen first verses of the sixt chapter of Leuiticus, and there you shall see, that the Lord will not accept his sacrifice that hath wrongfully taken any thing from his neighbour, before there be a recompence made.
 Quest. What say you more of this commandement?
Ans. As I haue said of all the former, that to consent to theft is stealth, and likewise in wordes to wish, or in hart to desire other mens goods, Math. 15.19. But I will onely ad two or three reasons to diswade all men from stealing by any meanes in thought, word, or deed.
 First, it is the decree of God that euery man shoulde liue vpon his owne labour, with the
sweat of his browes, Gen. 3.17.18.19. Christ therefore biddeth vs aske our daily bread, not other mens, Mat. 6. Paul saith, 2. Thess. 3.10. he that will not worke, ought not to eate. And the Lord will satisfie them with good, that walking faithfully before him, call vpon him, Psal. 81.11.
 Secondly, as thou wouldest not haue an other to take from thee, that which in a long time thou hast gotten with sore labour; so thou ought not to take from another. Mat. 7.12.
 Thirdly, the earth is the Lords, and all that is therein, that if thou walke honestly in thy calling, and put thy trust in him, thou needest not to lacke any thing: if thou distrust him, and steale thou makest God thine enemie, and then all thou stealest shall doe thee no good.
 Fourthly, goods euil gotten will not prosper with thee nor with thy posterity, and Zophar the Naamathite telleth Iob. Cap. 20. ver. 5.10. and Iob himselfe confesseth, Chap. 27.13.16. And Salomon saith, Pro. 5.13.22. The riches of the sinner is laid vp for the iust.
 Quest. What is the punishment for him that breaketh this commaundement?
Ans. The breach of all the former commaundements was punished with death, because there could no satisfaction be made. For this is generall, and as I take it, runneth throughout
all the commandementes of God; that where no satisfaction can be made, there the offender is to be punished with death. Wherfore seeing there may satisfaction be made for stollen goods, the punishment appointed for the theefe is satisfaction as you may read, Exod. 22.1. etc. If a man steale an oxe or a sheepe, and kill it, or sell it, he shall restore fiue oxen for the oxe, and foure sheep for the sheep. etc.
Thou shalt not beare false witnesse against thy neighbour.
 Quest. What is the summe of this ninth commaundement?
Ans. If you remember the degrees by which the Lord proceedeth in these fiue last commandements, as I haue noted them before in the beginning of the sixt commandement, then shal you see that here in this ninth commaundement the Lord forbiddeth a man any way to impaire the credit, name, or good estimation of his neighbour. And for this purpose the Lord elsewhere in the scripture somtime setteth before vs the excellencie of a good name to make vs more carefull of it, and sheweth how pretious a thing it is in the book of the preacher, Chap. 7.3. saying, A good name is better then a good oyntment. And in another place he saith, A good name is to be chosen aboue
great riches, and a louing fauour is aboue siluer and aboue gold, Pro. 22.1. And sometime to dehort vs from staining the credit and good name of our neighbour, he setteth out a false witnesse bearer in his proper colours, and saith, A man that beareth false witnesse against his neighbour is like an hammer, and a sword, and a sharpe arrow, Pro. 25.28. And yet for more safety of a mans good name, the Lord that made this law hath backed it or seconded it with an otherlawe, Deut. 19.15. One witnesse shall not rise against a man for any trespasse, or for any sin or for any fault thathe offendeth in. There is no exceptio^ eyther of person or cause, as it is more manifest, Deu. 17.6. Num. 35.50. Math. 18.16. but there must be two witnesses at the least, to proue any man to be otherwise then he professeth himselfe to be, and so to impeach his good name that he caried before. So great care hath the Lord euen of our credit and good name among them. Whereby euery man is admonished to walke soberly and sincerely in his calling, that he empaire not his owne good name by worde or deede: and also to follow the Lords example, and be carefull to maintaine, not captious or sclaunderous to impeach the good name of his neighbour. 
 Quest. What if a man offende and doe that which is euill, shal it not be spoken?

Ans. We may, and we must speake of it, but with discretion, as tendring his good, and not labouring to shame him, that loue may couer a multitude of sins, Pro. 10.12. and 1. Pet. 4.6. considering that thou thy selfe also art subiect to infirmities, and therfore should so behaue thy selfe to thy neighbour, as thou wouldest he should doe to thee, Galat. 6.1. And specially priuate offences are priuately to be spoken, and to the offender himselfe, and to no other except thou call an other to go with thee, as a witnesse to admonish him. But open and knowen, and publike offences, are to be reproued publikely according to the nature and qualitie of the person and of the sinne that is committed.
 Quest. Who be those that offend against this commaundement?
Ans. First they that falsely accuse others, as they that accused Naboth, 1. King. 21. and Irijah falsely accused Ieremie the prophet and brought him before the princes, Ierem. 37.13 and the princes that falsely accused him before the king, Ierem. 38.4. The ruler and gouernors falsely accused Daniell, Dan. 6.13. Haman wrongfully accused the Iewes, Ester. 3.8. We reade how Stephen was falsely accused, Act 6.11. and Paul likewise Act. 24.5. how that reuerent and worthy man of God Athanasius of
Alexandria in Aegypt was most falsely and impudently accused, Theodoret. Lib. 1. cap. 29. sheweth at large, and the story is worth the reading.  Secondly to false accusers we may ad also them that iustifie the wicked, as the scripture ioyneth them together, Pro. 17.15. He that iustifieth the wicked, and he that condemneth the iust, euen they both are abhomination to the Lord. And in another place, He that saith to the wicked, thou art righteous, him shall the people curse. Prou. 24.24. And Esaias Chap. 5.23. denounceth a woe against him.
 Thirdly, they that rayle vpon men and reuile them, as Shemie did reuile Dauid, 2. Sam. 16.5. The Iewes reuiled Christ, Math. 27.29.39.41. and him that was borne blinde, Iohn. 9.28. And many take pleasure in rayling vpon others, and glorie in their ripe and pregnant wittes, as though it coulde be a Christian glorie to reproach the image of God. And he that in euill speeches excelleth, he crowes, as if he had wonne the game, when he hath impudently disgraced and outfaced his neighbour. Which sinne reigneth euen in the countrey also among the meanest sort of people, as though there were the gammes of Olympus, and a gleiue or garlande for the worst. Others by reuiling speaches and tearmes couet to
prouoke men to requite them with the like, that thereupon they may picke a quarrell, either to fight, or to bring him in danger one way or other. Dauid saith that these mens wordes be very swordes. For as man pricked by his aduersarie with a sword, can hardly forbeare to defend himselfe by fighting: so the prouoking wordes of contentious men doe pricke the heart, that it is a difficult matter to bridle the tongue, and not to answere againe. There are a great number of halting papists, Iesters, and prophane persons, which by quipping and nipping make often iolly sport at rich mens tables, and therefore they are heartely welcome whensoeuer they com. And let them haue but an inckling whome they shoulde girde and taunt, and they will doe it smoothly.
 Fourthly, sclanderers which bring vp euill reportes vpon their neighbours, eyther by impudent vntruethes, or by wresting of their wordes and deedes, as Doeg both slaundered Dauid and Ahimelech, 2. Sam. 22.9. Siba slandered Mephibosheth with an impudent lie, 2. Sam. 16.3. and the scripture is full of such examples.
Fiftly, backbiters, which priuily and secretly whisper as in the night, that they may discredite others, as the Pharisies went about to
vndermine Christ, when they came behind his backe and saide to his disciples secretly, why eateth your maister with publicans and sinners Math. 9.11. And many there are in our dayes which reioyce if by secret wispering the can discredit the subiect with the prince, the seruant with the maister, the inseriour with the superiour, and one neighbour with another. 
 Sixtly, scorners, and mockers, which deride euery mans gestures, wordes, and deeds, or whatsoeuer is in them, as if there be any blenish in their nature, any imperfection, any want, any infirmitie, that they will take occasion by to mocke him, as the children that mocked Elisha, and said, Cum vp, thou bauld heade, Cum vp, thou bald heade 2. king. 2.23. When the Lord in his iudgemente hath made any man lame, or laide any other imperfection vpon him either of bodie or minde, some make a mocke and a scorne of it, whereas they ought rather to pittie his case and praise God because he hath dealt better with them. Others mocke men for their pouertie, but Salomon saith, He that mocketh the poore, reproueth him that made him Pro. 17.5. Others and too too many mocke them which exhort them to godlynes, as the men of Ephraim, Manasses, and Zebulun, mocked
Hezekiah and his messengers, when he exhorted them to come to Ierusalem to keepe the passeouer 2. Chro. 30.10. Sanballet and Tobiah mocked Nehemiah for building the wal of Ierusalem Nehem. 4.2.3. Ishmael mocked Isaac Gen. 21.9. When Christ came to raise vp the rulers daughter that was deade, many laughed him to scorne Math. 11.24. Michal despised Dauid 2. Sam. 6.16. When the holy ghost was sent vpon the Apostles, many mocked and saide they were drunken Act. 2.13. If you exhort men to godlynes, they will mocke you and say you are too too holy. Ieremie was daily mocked Ierem 20.7. For the wisdom of God is counted foolishnes of them that beleeue not. But Esaias Chap. 57.4. saith, on whome haue ye iested? vpon whom haue you gaped, and thrust out your tongues? And Salomon saith Pro. 24, 9. the scorner is an abhomination to the Lord.
 Seauenthly, they that are tale-tellers. For, a tale-teller maketh diuision among princes Pro. 16.28, And by comparing Leuit. 19.16. with Ezek. 22.9. you shall see the fruite of them.
 Eightly, they that harken to euil wordes, and receiue false tales Exod. 23.1. as Dauid to too lightly beleued lying Siba. 2. Sa^. 26.1. And co^only there is dissentio^ made among
deare friendes, when men giue credit at the first to euery flying tale.
 Quest. What reason will you render to diswade men from beareing false witnes.
That which hath beene saide is sufficient, not withstanding I will ad this more.
 First, Iames Chap. 3. of his epistle vers. 4.5. compareth the tongue to three things that is, to a bridle wherewith an vnruly horse is gouerned, to the rudder of a ship, whereby it is guided through the great seas, and to firie: and sheweth that as these three things wel vsed serue for good and necessarie vses, but abused or vnskilfully handled ar most dangerous and hurtful, so the tongue well vsed is full of grace, but abused is a world of mischief. For with the fruite of a mans mouth shall his bellie be satisfied, and with the increase of his lippes shall he be filled: death and life are in the power of the tongue, and they that loue it shall eate the fruite thereof Prouerbs, 18.20.21.
 Secondly, lying and false witnes-bearing shew that we should be the sonnes of the diuel. For the diuel is a lier, and the father of lies Iohn 8, 44.
 Thirdly, the Lord hateth a false tongue, Pro. 6.16.19. and 12.22. and therefore good men and godly ought not to loue it.

 Quest. What is the punishment which is appointed for him that beareth false witnes?
Ans. The same punishment he would haue brought vpon him, whome he accused Deut. 19.16.19.
Thou shalt not couet thy neighbours house, neither shalt thou couet thy neighbours wife, nor his seruant, etc.
 Quest. What is the summe of this tenth and last commaundement?
Ans. In all the former commaundements, some outward acte or deed was commaunded or forbidden, but in this last the Lorde forbiddeth only the desire of the heart.
 Quest. You saide afore in euerie commaundement, that the outward facte, was not only forbidden, also the inward desire of the heart, and you shewed it plainely out of Math 5.21. etc. and 15.9. how then commeth it now to passe that this commaundement conteineth nothing but that which was a parcell of each of the former commaundements?
Ans. My former answeare was sufficient, but not manifest enough to make plaine to euery one the difference betwene this commaundement and the other nine which goe
before, therefore I will briefely make the difference as plaine as I can.
First, that you may be fully perswaded that these wordes are not only a repetition or declaration of some things forbidden in the nine commaundements going before, but a new and an other commaundement euen the tenth (for you heard in the beginning out of Deut. 4.13, that there are ten commaundements) expressed by an other word, whereon yet I will not stand, the Apostle Paul shall answere you Rom. 7. who daily examining his owne wayes, and his owne heart by the co^maundements of the Lord, still supposed that bare thought and wandring lust had beene no sinne, till he came to this tenth and last commaundement, where he found it written thou shalt not lust. In consideration whereof he found himselfe deeplier guiltie of sinne, then before he supposed he had beene. Wherefore his wordes are manifest and sufficient to teach vs that here is an other commaundement, euen the tenth, both here, and also Deut. 5.21. in the tenth place.
 Secondlie now to declare the difference betweene this tenth commaundement and the other nine, we must consider sinne, and
the degrees thereof from the beginning to the end. And first of all there is originall sinne in euery man as the scripture beareth record Iob. 14.3. Psal. 51.7. Eccles. 7.31. which is not only sinne of it selfe but also the roote, from whence other sinnes doe bud and spring, and shoot foorth themselues, the fountaine from whence other sinnes flow and the nurce which feedeth and cherisheth other sinnes. In the second place we are to consider the fruites of this originall sinne,
Four fruits of the original corruption. which are four in number and in degree one proceeding after another, and as it were growing one out of another, or one vpon another
 And first out of original corruption, as out of a filthie puddle or chanell when it is stirred arise a sinfull concupiscence or lust with out consent of will, as it may best appeare in young children. For as that lust appeareth in them before they be come to the other three degrees following: so we must vnderstand it lurketh still in mans nature though in riper yeres it be not so manifest.
 In the second place there is the very same lust growne vp with age, and augmented with a generall and wandring consent of the heart, as it were with another fruite, which men shew forth when they say in their hearts,
and some times with their mouths, I would this mans house, landes, cattell, seruant, wife, maide, etc. were mine. Whereby they declare that they couet other me^s goods, and lust after them with an vnsetled and with a roauing consent of the heart, without any endeauour to obtaine the thing that is desired.
Thirdly, this former lust groweth vp, still increaseth as it were a new and third branch, as being growen taller and stronger then it was before, by a full, setled, and resolute consent of the heart, not only generally to wish and couet, but also to endeauour to obtaine that which is desired. And this desire sheweth itselfe in deedes also, as the former did in words only. For after a man hath so resolutely wished and lusted after his neighbours goods, that he will haue them if he can get them, he alwayes vseth meanes to obtaine them as occasion serueth. As if he lust after his neigybours fielde, as Ahab did after Naboths vineyard, he will seeke and vse all meanes to get it by force or by fraude. If he cannot flatter him, and fetch him in with intising words, then wil he finde some quirk, proue it concealed land, or enter some action against him to vndoe him, and by meere oppression obtaine it.

The fourth and last fruit of originall sinne is, when things so vnlawfully desired, are likewise obteined vnlawfully. And this fourth and last degree the Apostle Iames Chap. 1.15. of his epistle, calleth perfect sin, or sin finished. The fruit whereof springing from originall sin, and growing vpon the verie toppe of all these foure branches is death, as the same Apostle saith.
Now of these four braunches growing out of originall corruption, I passe ouer the first, as not mentioned expresly in this commaundement, because it is without any consent of heart, which consent is the thing here forbidden. For this tenth commaundemente is not only thou shalt not lust, but there is added, thy neighbours house. etc. to shew that here is forbid a lust with consent of hearte. For no man can couet his neighbours house but with consent of heart. The second branch then, which is coueting and lusting after our neighbours goods with a roauing and wandring desire (but without any setled and resolute minde to obteine it if we may) is the thing that is forbidden in this last commaundement. The third and fourth braunches are the desires and deedes which were forbidden in the former commaundements.
Wherefore the thing forbidden in this last
commaundement (that I may repeate it againe) is a roauing and raunging lust with a generall consent of the heart to wish it, yet so that a man should checke and reproue his owne heart, rather then he would his desire should be acco^plished. If a man couet his neighbours wife with a wandring kinde of lust, and if there were opportunitie to enioy her, but yet he would refuse her and sharply reproue his ranging desire, euen his lust is here forbidden. Which teacheth vs what perfection of loue to God, to our neighbours, and what holynes of life these commaundements of the Lord require at our handes. Wherefore let vs follow the counsel of Paul 2. Cor. 7.1. and cleanse ourselues from al filthines of the flesh and spirite, and grow vp vnto ful holines in the feare of God. And who so meditateth herein daily, shall finde sufficient cause in himselfe to humble himselfe before the Lord, as finding himselfe deeply guiltie of much transgression, that though he once thought with Paul that he was aliue without the Law, yet now behoulding his soule in this and in the former commaundements, as his face in a glasse, he shal see that sinne reuiueth, and that he him selfe is dead Rom. 7.9.
Quest. In what particular branches wil you
inlarge this commandement?
In the former commaundements each one hath his proper obiect, but the obiect of this commaundement goeth through all the rest of the second table, and in this is to be inlarged, namely in coueting our neighboures house, land, wife, seruant, oxe, etc. And the opening of one of these, shal serue for all. If a sonne hauing a couetous desire and wandring lust in his heart, and say thus in his heart, I would I were in possession of my fathers inheritance, he breaketh his commandement, though he neuer vtter it in word. And there are too many sonnes now a daies, which thinke their parents liue too long. For if the poet could say long since, filius ante diem patrios inquirit in annos, the sonne often counts his fathers age before he dye: we haue no cause to perswade vs that this is the golden age, but rather that according to the dreame of Nebuchad-nezzer Dan. 2. the golden heade, the siluer breastes, the brasen thighs are long since past, and we now liue in the time of the yron legges the feete whereof are partly yron, partly clay. For euen the loue betweene the father and the sonne sometimes is like the coherence of yron and clay. Againe if any rich Ahab desire his neighbour Naboths
house or land, though he neuer vse. Ahabs meanes to purchase it, yea though he would not haue it vnlawfully though he might, yet when he shall appeare before the tribunall seate of Iesus Christ, and the bookes or bills of inditements be reade, then shal he finde that wandring desire written in his own conscience with the point of a Diamond that it cannot be rased or blotted out, except he truly repent him of all his sinnes, and by a liuely faith wipe it out with the blood of Iesus Christ. Wherefore as euery man examining his owne soule shall finde himselfe guiltie of the breach of this commandement in any one thing, so let him trie himselfe in the rest, and therevpon humble himself and fal downe before the throne of grace, that in Iesus Christ our high priest, he may finde grace to helpe in time of neede Heb. 4.16. For Iames saith Chap. 4.5. The spirit that dwelleth in vs, lusteth after enuie. And Dauid saith Psul. 94.11. The Lord knoweth the thoughts of man, that they are vanitie.
 Quest. One question more I would demand, and it is this. Whether God hath giuen this law, these ten commaundements, that a man by keeping them may purchase to himselfe eternal blessednes?
Ans. I haue alreadie dissolued part of this
doubt before in the first part, when I answered your 50. question. Neuerthelesse I will giue you another answere to your demaund now, and repeate one answere twise ouer for to make it plaine.
First when Adam was created in the beginning, euen the sixt day of the creation, God did not create him cursed and miserable, and then gaue him a law by which he might merit blessednes: but God first created him good, blessed, and holy, and gaue him a blessed and happie life. Then afterward the Lord gaue to Adam a law Gen. 2.15. etc, not to purchase a happie life, for he had a blessed life giuen him before at his creation, but that by keeping the law which God gaue him, he might continue still in Gods fauour, and in that blessed state of his creation: for by transgressing the law he lost the blessed life which God had giuen him.
And this was the vse of the Law in the beginning, before the fall of Adam.
Secondly, when all man-kinde was lost in Adam, because of his disobedience as I shewed you in the beginning of the first part, there was none of all Adams posteritie that could redeeme himselfe by his workes, and merit the blessed life he had lost. For if man in innocencie could not keepe Gods
Law that he might continew in that blessed life he had receiued of God, much lesse is he able to recouer that he lost, seing he is now farre weaker then he was before. Therfore the Lord that is rich in mercie, and hath mercie on whome he will, did promise Christ, and in fulnes of time sent Christ, to take our humaine nature vpon him, and so by the sacrifice of his owne bodie once only offred vpon the crosse to make full satisfaction for our sinnes, and so reconcile vs to God againe. And thus by the death of Christ, and not by merits of men, we are reconciled to God, and restored to life againe. Now the Lord, that of his mercy hath thus brought vs to blessednes againe, doth not leaue vs lawles to liue as we list, and do what we wil, but hath the second time also giuen vs his lawes againe, not to purchase life thereby, for of his mercie in Christ Iesus our Lord he hath giuen vs a blessed life the second time, but that by continuing in obedience to his commaundements, and by keepeing of the law, we might abide and continue in the same blessed life which he hath freely giuen vs, and not by transgressing it as Adam did, lose our happie life as Adam did. And this is the vse of the law now to vs al that are reconciled to God in Christ,
euen absolutely and intirely to keepe the whole Law of God that we may abide blessed for euer: for if we but once breake any jot of Gods Law, we lose our blessednes againe as Adam did.
Wherefore the Lord seing that Adam in his in nocencie did not keepe the law and that we in our corruption, though reconciled to God, are lesse able to keepe the law then Adam was, hath also giuen Christ Iesus to be our righteousnes. Christ hath fulfilled the whole law of God for vs, and imputeth his disobedience to vs that beleeue in him, and therefore we desire with Paul to be founde, not hauing our owne righteousnes of the law but hauing the righteousnes of Iesus Christ. And thus in Christ and by Christ it is that we keepe the whole law, and so continue in the blessed life which is purchased for vs by Christs death.
Now it remaineth for vs, not to giue ouer our selues to all vncleanenes, but to striue to the perfection of that sanctification which is begunne in vs by the spirit of God, and so to walke after the motions of the spirit, not after the lusts of the flesh, as Paul teacheth vs Rom. 6. and 7.
Quest. Now that you haue spoken of faith, of the sacraments, and of the ten commandements,
it remaineth, that, according to your owne order propounded before, you should speake of prayer. Wherefore I pray you proceede to open that also.
Ans. I propounded it, as you say, and this is the proper place for it, that whether we giue thankes to God for any blessing and grace receiued either for our bodies, or for our soules, or for both: or else we craue any thing at Gods hands, as increase of faith, co^fort in the sacraments, or strength against the enemies of our saluation, and power to walke after the spirit, we should haue a direction out of Gods word that our prayers framed according to the wil of God, might be acceptable to him. And for this purpose the Lords prayer as the chiefest in all the word of God, for this purpose, were to be taken in hand, and laide out in his seueral partes and branches together with the vse of each part. And there are in it four things chiefely to be considered: first a preface in the first words; secondly a petition or crauing of such things as concerne Gods glorie and our necessitie in the four first petitions, thirdly a deprecation or desiring of God to put those things farre from vs, which are or might be hurtfull or dangerous vnto vs in the two last petitions, and fourthly the conclusion in the last wordes.
But by reason that I haue bene longer in the three former partes of faith, of the sacraments, and specially of the law, then I was purposed, and for other occasions I cannot at this present goe forward with prayer, as I haue done with the rest.
FINIS.
